O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	Oh sons of great fame, I have completed this book which lies behind the science of medicine in assembly, and have finished it for its explanations and by my statements.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it came to me in vision that I would complete this book for you, which is part of the work from hands, namely "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And for this reason that the work of hands is pressed in our region and is strange all around everywhere, it has been lost through science and decay, and nothing remains from the fires except small descriptions in books of the ancient ones who have moved their hands.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this arose the errors and vices, and are closed the intentions, and alienated the science.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation;	It seems to me that I can revive life according to the order of this treatise following the way of exposure, declaration and abbreviation;
et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	and I will assemble the forms of the cautery tools and other instruments in the work with the adjustment of the declaration and preparation as it is necessary.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And because no good masters of hands are found in our time, the art of medicine is extended.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And it is necessary for him who enters this that to study anatomy, as Galen says, until he knows the measure of bones, and their forms and connections and separations, and has knowledge of the marrow, nerves, and bones, and the number of joints, and the movement and rest of veins, and with his new understanding.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc;	And thus Hippocrates said that the art with the hand is most, and with the work is least;
et meismement en l’art de main.	and it is the same in the art of hand.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes;	Let us say in the introduction of this book that whoever is not knowledgeable of the things said here will, if he guards himself, avoid falling into error and will know those who are wise.
ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	Once I have wanted to try many of these who refuse to learn this science, and abandon themselves without knowledge and experience.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col;	For I saw a foolish doctor who cut the abscess of a scrofulous woman or her neck, and cut the arteries in the neck;
por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	because so much blood flowed out that the woman died between his hands.
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans;	And I saw another doctor who treated a stone of an old man, and the stone was large;
si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	so he carried off a piece of the bladder with it, and died of the wound inside three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I have seen it happen many times that they call for treatment, and see the condition of the patient and the size of the wound, and know well whether they will die from it.
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie;	And I saw another doctor who took in the treatment of a duke from our land who had broken his leg, and with the break caused an injury;
et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine;	and let the skilled hands bind the wound with strong ties, and do not leave it until it heals.
et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie;	and command that he does not release it (from its position).
et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	and thus left the leg completely exposed, and the feet came to destruction.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe;	I was summoned to come to him, and I hastened to come to release the leg;
et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	and when I saw that it was dislocated, he was in a peaceful state and felt no pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner;	But all the corruption had been confirmed in that member, and it could not be cured;
et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	and the corruption did not cease until the member was completely lost.
Et vis I autre mire qui effondra I apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And there was another cure that destroyed the abscess, enchanted it, and then inflamed through the evil of its power.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For a boil, when it is purified of melancholic humor, does not suit that one touches it with iron unless there is some way to remove what is corrupted.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions:	And because of this, dear son, you must know that work done by hands is divided into two parts:
c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions;	which means, having or carrying the risk of occurring in various conditions;
et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	and I will show in each one of these books where there is fear and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos.	So that you may guard yourselves, so that no one who knows will be able to speak evil of you.
Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez;	If you take your arms in consideration, and undertake your sick people gently but firmly, and use the best way, so that by God's grace you will be saved and praised.
et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit;	and leave the dreadful diseases to cause sickness.
et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	And put your armor on this that makes you doubt, for sometimes it is in your hands so that you can come from this world to the other of glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens:	The Greeks are mentioned in some of his writings:
«Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	Do not treat yourself with medicine for a bad illness, lest you be called a fool.
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	I have devised this book according to three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez;	The first chapters are on fire cauterization and cold medicine cauterization, and the chapters are ordered from head to toe.
et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	and the forms of excretions, and instruments for cauterization, and all that is necessary in this work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses;	The second chapters are on cutting and piercing, and on ventouses and wounds, and extractions of arrows, and similar things;
et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	and so are the chapters arranged and the forms of the humors.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses;	The third chapter is about restoring dislocations and twists, and similar things;
et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	and is ordered like the chief joints just as pieces, and forms of humors.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Also, as we remember the work, it is fitting to tell which quality of aid and which kind of nuisance each condition has.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus;	I say that the qualities of aid and of harm is the longest speech and subtle science and the secret responses;
et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu;	and this is what the more learned ones spoke about, and agreed upon;
et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	and they soften a little on their words, because I am weary of length.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions:	I say that cauterization helps universally in every complexion where there is matter, whatever the complexion may be:
c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	It is to know the nature of hot complexion with matter, and dry complexion with matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide;	In a hot and dry complexion combined with matter, some have discussed and said that cautery is great aid.
et li autre dirent le contraire:	And the others said the opposite:
que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	That cautery is worth nothing for disease that comes from heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour;	Because the nature of fire is hot, and should not be treated with cold medicine for heat or dryness.
et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	And this one who says the opposite, that cautery is great help to diseases hot and dry that come into the body of men.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	Because when you buy the body of a man and its moisture is in accordance with the hot complexions, you find that the body freezes.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this word.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	Because I have found it one time through experience.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens;	And all ways, do not enter fire unless the one who has proven it, and knows by long usage the cautery chapter, and the diversity of human complexions, and their dispositions and causes of their diseases, and remedies and space of time.
des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	We have no fear of other types of complexion, especially of cold and moist diseases.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all physicians assembled and agreed on the cautery.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, sons, that cautery is made from fire, and contains more healing power than cauterizing with burning medicine.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	The fire is simple, and does not come from fire to other limbs except those which are burned.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation;	The hot medicines come from member to member by removal, and bring about the illness of the diseased in the place of healing.
et par aventure ocit lou malaide.	And perhaps it will cure the patient.
Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	The fire does not act for its height and for the goodness of its substance, unless it has a surplus or excess.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses;	And this I have found through experiment and by the length of my service and study, and it is well known among things.
et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant;	And for this reason I excuse myself from the length of speech, because it does not please me to take away from you the secret that is revealed by fire, and the quality of the work, how it cures diseases of the body, as the philosopher said in demonstrating.
or le recevez en vos pensees.	Instruct the patient to think about this.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, son, when it will be decided to perform the cauteries, and when you should pray.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere;	And I say that cautery is beneficial in all times, because the remaining nuisances are removed by the aid of cautery.
et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	And even more so, when the cuts are for painful purposes and necessary wounds that cannot be endured until greater misfortune comes to the member.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire;	And do not think ever, dear son, how they made those fools.
car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue;	because the disease that is cured by cautery has no return.
et il le dient ensi;	and he says this;
mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	but it is not so as they claim, because cautery is not just a medicine that changes the complexion and dries out the humors that cause pain; rather it is a medicine of great value and virtue, done quickly by its power and operation.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut;	And certainly, it is possible for the disease to come upon someone at any time according to their bodily constitution and the temperament of the illness and its virtues.
et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie;	and the superfluities are assembled in him with the acquisition of food and similar things; but if you do not administer cauterization to him when he has little superfluity and moisture, as is done for cauterizing dens because of pain, and similar things, and the same pain does not return.
mais ce avient poc.	but this happens rarely.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir;	and many people do not understand why cauterization is called the "backside of medicine", and it's seeing.
mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	but they don't believe that cauterization is worth after medicine, but their understanding is false, and it's cauterization being the "backside of medicine" because whenever we administer different kinds of cures for no malady, and they are useless, then we administer the cautery, and it is valuable.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Then open well that cauterization is for those with fever, not according to the foolish opinions of madmen.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance;	The ancient people said that cauterization with an instrument of gold is more effective than iron, and they say that fires only for the quality of the gold and because of the height of its substance;
et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes;	and they said that the cutting of cauterization does not cause putrefaction, but it is not true for me because I have tried it, and found that it's true in some people;
et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	And cauterization with gold is more valuable than iron, as they said.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez;	And whenever you heat an instrument of gold, you don't know when it will be cooled by the color of the gold.
et s’on le chaufe trop;	and if it is heated too much;
si font au feu;	so they are made in the fire;
et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	And thus there is much hindrance.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And for this reason, we will use fire cautery that we have used before on our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	Or you have ordered this chapter on the head to be followed with great care, because the vein is more delicate to find.
dou cautere olivaire	when olive oil cautery
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	This cautery is applied to moist and cold surfaces on the head, and there's one we do by the cause of a disease called "soda", and because of many humors that descend onto the head and ears, and into the eyes, and for many pains and discomfort from teeth, ears, and throat, as well as all diseases that come from cold, such as paralysis, soda, apoplexy, and similar illnesses.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir;	The form of this cautery is that the patients should be purged by medicine, dissolving the humors in the head three or four, according to what the virtues and properties and the custom of the patient can bear;
et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	and then tie up the patient's head.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis;	And then make him sit cross-legged between your hands, and put his hands in a certain position.
aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz;	After placing the root of your palm on the root of his neck between his two eyes;
et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	and when it comes to your two thumbs, if it bleeds from the wound then heat the cautery which is called "olivare", because this is the form:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant;	And put on the patient's hand a signet ring of ink, and do it by lowering and pulling apart your hand little by little while twisting.
puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit;	Then lift the patient's arm without any resistance, and check if you see the bone a little.
et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit;	And if you do not see the bone, then repeat the cautery as I told you until you see the bone like I told you.
aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors;	After applying a small amount of silk, and putting on woolen cloth inside, put it on the patient, and let them remain for three days.
aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre;	After put on cotton moist in butter;
et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee;	and let it remain until the swelling is drained.
aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	After a treatment of the wound on the elbow called "tetrafarmacón", so that it is cured.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge;	And if the old ones say that when the wound remains longer, it purges more.
et por ce si aide mues.	and therefore aid is added.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And any of those said that one must cauterize the wound so much that part of the bone is burnt, and then resettle what has been burned by the bone, and treat it.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors;	And the others say that one must cauterize as long as they can pull off, and pound so hard as you lower on the bone just as wide as the spindle that women use in their sewing, for this reason that the humors come out moved out.
et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte;	and one must pull off the wound longer.
aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	afterwards it must be cured and applied to.
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor;	And these two methods of cauterization do not seem good to everyone, fire or no fire.
et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier;	and I think that he should let him lie;
car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres;	because the joints are weakened by continued solutions of nature, just as we have observed in other members;
et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	and also when the joints of the sick person are weak by nature, and the first treatment of cautery is more salubrious and more soothing for me, and from that comes this same remedy;
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	Of ancient pain in the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres;	When in all cases the head comes with chronic pain that lasts a long time, he must use the patient's herbs and pills called "couchie", and purge of the head, ointments, and emplasters;
et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	and if one makes the cautery that we have previously mentioned, and it does not help.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit;	Prepare yourself if the head of the sick person is of strong nature, and it is not too cold;
adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	Therefore perform cauterization on the same place as we have already said about.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»;	After performing cauterization on each corner of the head just where the bone is, as we have said before, and perform cauterization to the one that is called "vessel".
et est I leus en coi on met ventouses;	and it is often done in which place they put ventilators;
et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os:	and tie your hand so that you do not hear anything just where the bone is;
li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors;	the patients feel too much more severe pain in this cauterization than in the others, and I will speak about it later;
et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	and it is fitting that cauterizing of horns are more subtle than those who cauterize the middle of the head, and this is the form:
dou cautere dou chief	Fire cautery of the head
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie:	When in one part of the head comes sudden pain and the disease spreads up to the oil, and the joints are purged with medicinal powders, and other treatments that I have said in dividing the diseases, do not benefit.
adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	and so it is necessary to perform cauterization in two manners, that is to say, according to the method of cold medicine and fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir;	The cauterization of cold medicine is that you take a dose of alum, and remove the scab and scrape it up with two fingers, and then make an incision at the temple where the pain resides in such a way that you can replace the dose of alum under the skin.
et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres;	And when she is reset, if the ligaments are tied tightly and left so for 12 hours;
et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III;	and then the dressing is made with hot wood ash and vinegar, and leaves the wound for 2 days or 3.
puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	then puts a cotton plug in butter until it stops the discharge.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	After the treatment of ointment, until he is safe.
et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	and if you see, do as I have written or prescribed for any medicinal substances that burn.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The iron cautery is done according to this method.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Heating the cautery of this kind is thus the form:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance;	And it is called "closet" because the head is shaped like a hole or has a little bit of bird (feathers), and in the middle, there is a small appearance;
et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse;	And put it on its proper place of pain, and hold your hand and turn the fever a little lighter, until the moisture of the passion that kills is burned.
et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	Hold your hand so that the arteries do not burn, which is in front, and there is an abundance of blood.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par III jors;	Put cotton on it to dress a wound, and put it back on its proper place for three days;
puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	then put moist cotton with butter on it, and then treat the wound of ointment until it is healed.
et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	and if you want to cauterize this migraine with the cautery called "cultellare", at its entire tip, and keep the artery covered in this migraine which is not ancient.
de emigraine	of a headache
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans;	When you treat a migraine in the manner we have stated in our divisions of diseases, and do not benefit from it, and see that the fire cautery was previously mentioned by physicians regarding medicine and iron did not suffer, then it is necessary to cool the cautery called "cultellare" until it is white;
et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os;	And thus, on the left, strike a line of half an inch deep with steel, and hold your hand tight once, and strain that you do not cover the artery and will not be born to the bone;
et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez;	And guard the jawbone so that it is mute when one chews, and the nerves have no sensation but pain and spasm will come to the patient, and guard the corruption of the artery when it is cut, or if cutting has great fear and also harm to oneself, who is not a student or an expert;
et laisse l’uevre em mi voie;	and let the wound heal in its proper place;
mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	but I will tell you how to bind blood when the artery is cut, and I will show you in this book where it occurs.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee;	But if you see that this cautery does not suffice for the disease, and the patient suffers much, cauterize them also on the head as we have said, and treat the wound until it is healed.
et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait II coutelz;	and if you see, administer the cautery that we have said or the chapter of the extraction of the artery, with the cautery which has two cuts;
et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	and this cautery is better than that one and more helpful.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	of ear pain from cold.
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When ear pain comes from cold, and you have tried medicines that dissolve and other treatments that we have said in the section on division, and the pains do not subside, then apply this cautery which is called "pins", because it is the form:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les II se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche;	After pricking all around the diseased ear, or near both if pain remains in both, and you move a little towards the root of the ear after marking it with ink;
et ait X poins entor chescune oreille;	And have 10 points for each ear;
aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the treatment, let him be sane.
de la torture de la bouche	of the mouth's torture
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie;	Tortures that must be cured by cauterization, except those caused by swelling, as we have said in the divisions of diseases;
et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	and do not perform cauterization on those that come from swelling and pus of the skin.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de III cauteres:	When you treat this swelling of a torture that swells from inflammation and purging of the head and gargarete, and since these are not considered, then it is necessary to cauterize the patient with three cauteries:
l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des II levres;	one in the root of the ear, and another near the temple, and the third at the junction of the two lips;
et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce;	and place the cautery in the healthy part that is opened up, and let them apply cautery directly to the forehead above a little below the eyebrow, and another one on the temple as long as an inch.
et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse;	and let it burn so that the moles on his face are burned;
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	and this is the form of cautery:
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros;	And it is like the form of a knife that we have shown before, but it is slightly more subtle and must be that the knives be slightly thicker;
aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	after healing as I have said, until he is whole.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai IIII cauteres:	When apoplexy is ancient and you cure it as we have said, and he does not recover, and the patient has no fever, then let him do four cauteries:
II sus les II cornes dou chief, et I emmi le chief, et I ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac;	In the second part of the head, and in the first ear, and on the one that is called "wazel" as we have said before, apply cautery to the mouth of the stomach;
et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	and treat it as we have said before.
de litargie	of lassitude.
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil;	To this illness, it is fitting to give the patient large and pill-like medicines for the brain;
aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres;	After applying the head of the patient to all of them, and putting on the ointment of fennel in the back of the neck, which is written in treating ointments;
et c’est li maniere dou cautere:	and this is the manner of cautery:
si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	as I have said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est;	If he is thus healthy, then good is;
et s’il ne l’est, se li fai III cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere I doi de gros;	And if he is not so, then do three cauteries on the head near the neck, and space one thumb's breadth between each cautery two of great size.
et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai I cautere en mileu;	And the treatment as the others; and if you see a lump, then do one cautery in the middle.
et se mestiers est, II autres sus les II cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	And if it's wise, two others above the two horns, and the treatment until he is healthy.
et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	And let it be the cauteries which are called "olivary", as I have said before.
de la froidor dou chief	of the coldness of the head
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit;	It is fitting that the head be purified with years and what we have previously said;
aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et I derrier et III sus l’espinee dou col;	After the illness the head of the patient, then cauterize in the middle of the head and on each horn, and on the third from behind and above the spine of the neck.
et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai IIII cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos;	And if you wish to do more, and the body is moist, and the patient suffers greatly, and the disease is severe, then cauterize four times on the spine of the back.
et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main;	and let it be left until the greatest wound is cooled, and lift your hand;
aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	after the cure until he is healed, and apply what is called "olivare" which we have previously mentioned.
de l’epilempsie	From the epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	The epileptics should only use fire cautery on those who are flaky, and it is fitting to first soften the brain with years and other remedies that we have mentioned in the division when the patient is great and suffers from many of the medicines.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes;	And if it is an infant who cannot suffer, then make gargarism and mastication of a poultice that moistens the brain often with raw meat.
aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai I cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et I cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne;	After the king's head is removed, and he undergoes the fire cautery according to what we have said before, and undergoes the cautery on his neck, and on each horn;
et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	and if the patient is very strong and suffers, he undergoes fire cautery in the same way as I have said to him who has paralysis and softening of the body, on the spine of his back and throat, and should be cauterized olive according to the manner that I have said.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai I cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the patient is sick, if he does fire cautery subtle according to this manner:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When because of melancholy there are superfluities or corrupted moistures and a great flux, then the fire cautery on tender parts as we have said to him who had paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if the superfluities decline due to melancholy and the body of the sick person is moist, then let him drink something so that the intellects be clarified, according as it is beforehand in the division.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide;	After the king's head is given to the patient;
aprés fai I torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com I cercle, si le met emmi le chief;	After make a cloth of linen well made, like a circle, put it on the head;
et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars;	and let them be tied in such a way that they are well crossed, and held in all parts;
aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien;	After presenting the thread, take up a bandage of wool grease.
et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir;	and let it be heated by fire temperately, so that the wounds may bear it.
aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier;	after draining the circle from within the head, let it cool down;
et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and do this for the patient each week once with good governance, until they are healed.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	If you see someone being cautered while making many pricks all over the cautery.
Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument;	This method of cautery is more suitable for the brain;
et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	and then put on a wet cotton cloth in lard and fatty meat.
de l’awe des eulz	of the eyes.
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When the eye comes first in this way by the signs I have said in division, then begin and do give the patient something that cleanses the head, and guards against all moistures, and make it sweat or take a bath several times daily.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai II cauteres sus les II temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as II eulz ensamble, ou en I se li dessendemens est en I;	After he is commanded to put his head back, and he does cautery from the inside of the head, and does two cauteries on each temple if there is a falling out with both eyes together, or if one is affected alone.
et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple;	And take care of all the cautery on every vein and artery that is under the cheek, and be careful to cut them long according to the size of the temple.
et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	And be careful of the decomposition of blood, and if you see too much blood coming out, then stain it with a little strength just like how you did.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras;	And I will teach you in the extraction of arteries and incising, how to carefully do it;
et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les II os derrier.	And never perform a cautery or haterel (likely "hatterel", an old word for "copper knife") under the two bones at the back.
dou cors des larmes	Of men of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors;	When the eyelids are old and accustomed and are over the veins, or under the arteries that appear on the surface of the cheek.
et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz:	and then we see that it is the swelling of cold phlegm, therefore, let the fire cautery be done which I have said at the beginning, descending to the eyes:
I cautere emmi le chief, et II cauteres sus les II temples, et II cauteres ou haiterel desoz les II os;	Cut cautery on the head, and cut on both sides of the two temples, and cut under the two bones;
et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout I petit cautere.	and if it is a more serious condition, then the cautery should be done in the same way above the eyebrow to all the little cuts.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	Out of the flesh through the eyelids
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide III nuis cochies;	When you give medicine according to what we have said in the division, and it does not help at all, then let the patient drink three poisonous substances;
aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire;	After the king has been done for the head, and let there be a cut in the middle of the fire olive cautery;
et fai II cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les II sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous;	And do the second fire cautery on the two wounds called "clavilis" under the two shoulders, a little below.
et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	and watch out for the artery that you do not cover.
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And this is the form of the cautery called "clavilis":
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare».	When the paper of oil is softened by disease and moisture, then apply the cautery called "olivare".
de coi ci est li forme:	Because of this there is
Et se tu vues si fai II cauteres sus les II sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont;	And if you see, do the second fire cautery on the two wounds as long as the wounds are.
et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	and do not leave off the hand, except until the third part of the paper is burned, as I have said.
dou poil qui point l’oil	One hair which touches the oil
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc II manieres:	There is never a case where the hairs of the ointment are converted into pardaens, and they prick, and then one does fire cautery according to two ways:
c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	which is to say of fire, or of burning medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals;	Instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even;
et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain;	and when they are long and even, then put the patient in a safe place;
aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz;	and then mark the paper around the eyes with a figure such as that of the flame of myrrh, and just like the beginning of the sign of the hair.
puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	then put cotton soaked in beeswax and musk of pyrethrum on the oil, and then apply the cauterization with this shape:
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit;	After cauterizing on the figure that you have marked, slowly apply heat a little at a time, so that the color is fixed in the right place.
et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil;	and when the signs of health of the eye are that you see the parchment withdrawn, and the hairs raised at the tip of the nail;
adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi III jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee;	and therefore lift your hand, and let it be thus for three days, then apply cotton moistened in butter until the swelling is drawn.
aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	after treatment of ointment until he is cured.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers;	And if after this the hairs come back and the parchment is softened, then resume the cautery on that very same place, just as you did first;
et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	and if the hairs are fallen out, then cuterize until the parchment is raised to its natural place, and even, and does not prick at the hair anymore.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte;	The fire cautery is that you instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; then make a parchment shape of the form of myrtle leaf.
puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien;	then take some French soap and live charcoal, one of each, Z., and grind them together well.
et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz;	and make it hastily, if it does not cool down, then place it on the form as you have made like a myrtle leaf, and put paper over the eyes;
et se li maladie tient en I oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en I, et se en ambedous ausi;	and if the illness is held in only one kind of oil, so it must be applied to both.
et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef;	and put the oil-soaked cotton cloth in an earthen vessel;
et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse I poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	And the head of the patient should be in a healthy state, and show its pain above the medicine, and press it firmly on the muscle every time the patient feels sharp pains from the medicine, for he feels sharp pains just as from fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have done this for a long time, if the medicine has come to your death.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision;	And when the sharp pains have passed, if you lift the limb, and make sure it is warmed up as if it had been warmed up by constraint of fire or incision.
et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	and so he will be well.
Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point;	If not so, then put back the medicine on the limb or if it has not worked yet, until your work is equal and your eyes are at their right place.
puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then put on cotton soaked in fat until the wounds have closed, after curing the limb with a dressing called "diaphenis" and others, until it is completely healed.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	And if necessity requires that you guard yourself well on your work by great care, so that the wound does not occur again.
Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant;	And if the paper becomes wet after that, and they prick at the hair in the oil, then resume the medicine on that person who has been softened by the paper properly, as you have done before;
aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	after the cure until he is healed.
et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	and this is the form of the mercury mixture:
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens;	And so one must know that the eyes of men are different in size and proportion, and according to this one's complaints;
et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	and do not be replied that the correct way is for him who has studied this art.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	Of the cauterization treatment of a fistula.
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you cure a fistula as we have said in the divisions of diseases, and your treatments do not benefit him, then it is necessary to cauterize him according to this manner.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain;	Instruct the patient to put his head on a clean cloth;
et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief;	and let the barber tie his head between your hands in such a way that it does not move.
aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil;	After the application of a moist cloth or persil juice on oil.
aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz:	After applying heat to the cauterization which is divided:
et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere;	and it is shaped like a bird's beak as it resembles the cauterization;
se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente;	if it is pointed from the top to the bottom, and if it is so as a tent;
mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	but all of this is worthless for your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche;	After pressing the abscess until it bursts and pulls out its pus, and dries;
et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe;	and if it is closed, then the operation is performed, and fire is applied to the bowels;
aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie;	After the fire cautery is applied to the skin, hold the cautery hot on the area that needs healing, and keep your hand over the cautery at the place of the wound, so as not to cause madness.
et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	and put the cautery in the grease of the oil, and corrupt it.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	If you come to the beginning of cauterization just after the bone, it would be well.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors;	If this does not work, repeat the cautery once more, and if it is necessary again, leave it for three days.
aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers;	After that, put a wet cloth in butter on the wound, and apply a drying ointment until it is healed, and after forty days if it has not been healed, put on medicine to dissolve the bone.
et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	and he will do according to what comes in his chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	And there is a way of cauterization for an abscess that none of the ancients mentioned.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu;	Let an ulcer, and cut off the finger;
aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	After putting in the incision of a small hook so that it is the form:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc;	and make to the quantity of one and half fingers' breadth;
et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil;	And hold your hand firmly on the hook so that it does not move at all, until the poultice is fused and does not run to its own blood;
et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe:	and it is fitting that one puts on the poultice moistened with water or oil on the patient's skin in linen.
li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	the poultice if made on the finger of an ulcer, and makes the patient sound in marvelous health.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	And if the fistula is healed by the cautery that we have said, it is good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	If this is not the case, it is necessary to administer pus into the wound and return the fistula to its proper place in the body as is suitable for each individual.
des crevaices en levres	of fissures in lips
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Often fissures occur in the lips that are called "poils", and likewise in children's lips.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe I petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you treat these crevices of what we have said in divisions, and the cure does not benefit, then apply a small cautery surgical according to this form:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font;	And then puts it immediately into those crevices until it comes out at the same place;
aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	After cure the shoulder joint is stable again.
de l’aposteme de la goule	of the abscess on the throat.
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule;	When an abscess comes to the root of the neck or in the cheek or at the roots of the teeth, after being putrid and rotten and dried up and becomes a fistula.
et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie:	and you cure it as we have said in previous divisions, and it does not benefit at all.
adonques covient il que tu aies I cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule;	therefore it is necessary to cauterize according to the size of the fistula.
aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu;	after the dressing or removal of the fistula, and hold your hand until the iron comes alive at its tip, and draw the pus out.
et fai ensi une fois ou II, aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and do so once or twice, after the treatment as we have said for cures, until it is stable again.
et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin;	And if he is thus treated, this is good;
et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	And if this is not so, then it is necessary to discover the limb and remove the corrupted bone, according to what you will find in that chapter.
dou movement des dens	A dislocation occurs of any joint from its place
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain;	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you cure him with medicines, but this is useless, then place the healthy head of the patient on your own.
aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent;	after applying cauterization, from the shape of which will come later in this way, that you place a chain on the tooth;
et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent;	and put within the cauterization hot starch, and hold it with your hand so that the patient feels the heat coming to the root of the tooth;
aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit;	After your hand is lifted, resume the cautery according to your will.
aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	After filling the patient's mouth with a foul-smelling concoction, let it sit for an hour and burn hot fires.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in some way, the teeth which were moving are fixed, and the gums are restrained, and the moistures corrupted are dried.
de la dolor des dens	Of pain of teeth
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres:	When pain of the teeth comes from coldness, or if there is coldness in the ear, and medicines do not help, then it must be necessary to cautery according to two ways:
et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	and cautery with butter and cautery with fire.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain;	Cautery with butter if is done thus that you press butter from a vinegar-soaked cloth, and the end into a metal spoon or iron rod.
aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez;	After picking cotton and covering it with a cloth of gauze, let the paste of butter boil, and put on the painful tooth hastily and hold until it cools down;
et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus I fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	Instruct the patient to let their hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide;	The instrument for cauterization is made of iron or charcoal and must be large enough so that the flames do not reach the mouth of the patient;
aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez;	After cooling the cauterization instrument, because then it will take shape again, and you place it on the tooth and hold your hand until the instrument is cooled.
fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	Do this often, because the pain will be felt on the same day or the next day.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer;	And it is necessary that the patient fills his mouth with good butter in the haste of the cauterization, and then he rushes to cure him.
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	and this is the form of the cauterization:
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir;	And make cauterize where you wish, and according to what power you have;
et c’est li forme de la caine:	And thus is the form of the bone:
des scrophules	Des scrophules
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie;	When the scrophules are swollen with fever and cold moistors, and do not yield to digestion by medicines, then heat the cauterizing knife of such skin after which comes the form, and cut open two openings for the fumes to come out from the other side;
et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume;	and place the cauterizing knife on the abscess once or twice, as long as it is not drained from the abscess;
et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors;	and if the abscess is small, apply cauterizing according to its size, and let it be so for three days;
et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee;	and put on a moist cotton wool in butter until the wound is healed;
aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	After a cure, let the limb rest for a while until it is healthy.
Li forme de la cainne:	The form of the cauldron
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives;	When moisture prevails over the channels of the body, and especially when it comes from a cold temperament, then it is suitable for patients to be emptied first by medicinal solutions.
aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	After applying fire cautery to the root of the throat, and keep in mind that you should not come near the throat again, but only let a small amount of heat.
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant;	After applying the second fire cautery to the joint of the neck at the head of the spine, and consider the cauterized part which is called "clavicle" because we have the shape in front.
et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat the limb as we have said, until it is healthy.
de la toust	of the throat.
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai .II cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis;	When all and malady of winter are from cold moisture, and the patient has neither fever nor sweating, and is a long-standing illness, then apply two cauteries on the pulse in their veins;
et I autre cautere emmi le pis entre II mameles;	and another cautery on the flesh between the two nipples;
et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	and so it is called "clavicle" according to the shape that is described.
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles;	And if you see, apply cautery by pricking in the point where the cautery is called "points" because of its shape in the illness of the ears;
et soient li poins jusc’a XXX, ou enqui entor.	and are one thirty-third, or two thirds.
Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a III rains selonc ceste forme:	After the treatment according to what has been said, and if the cautery is applied at three points according to this form:
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais III a cop.	And because that way the cautery is lighter, because you do three of them at once.
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	of the shoulder joint.
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit;	After apply to the patient on their back and on their side;
aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre;	After the head of the shoulder, instruct the patient to lift the curvature which is inside the joint with your left hand.
et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners douqueil ci est li forme:	and if the joint is dislocated within, so inflame the cautery which has two nerves in it, this form:
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble IIII cauteres;	and cauterize the curvature so that it perforates just on its side, and comes together with the four cauterized nerves;
et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a III ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres;	and for this reason the cautery is made with the cautery that has three nerves, because the figures of the cauterization are these four.
et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a III ners:	and they are nerves according to the subtlety of an awning and this is the form of the cautery that has three nerves:
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce I nerf por coi il i a VIII cauteres.	And sometimes, you press against this nerve because it is with eight cauterizations.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil;	After set on the cautery for pearl-like bruises with thread;
aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	After resting the patient, do not keep the limbs still for a long time until they are well comforted.
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant.	And if they dislocate again, little things happen then; afterwards, make cauterization on the thick cauterizing knife, or many cauterizations in a point.
Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	For the joints are closed up, and the moisture is removed and the patients are made healthy.
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	When there is frost in the stomach and much moisture so that they extract it to its condition, and many cathartics are multiplied upon him, and all the usual treatments do not benefit him, then it is necessary that the patient be put on his back, and extend his legs and hands.
De ceu en aprés li fai III cauteres I desoz la cuillier dou pis per la quantiteit d’un doi, a tout le cautere clavile, et II cauteres defuers les II costez tant que li figure des cauteres soit a III angles, et ait teil espaice entre l’une et l’autre qu’elles ne soient jointes ensamble quant elles giteront porriture;	For this, after the third cautery I is done beneath the skin of the leg for the amount of two drachmas, all over the cautery clavicle, and the second cautery is done outside on both sides so that there are three angles in total, and each space between one and the other is such that they will not be joined together when they rot.
et soient li cautere si parfont qu’il porpreignent les II pars dou keur, et soit li figure des cauteres selonc ceste forme sens ajostement:	and the cauteries are performed to the point that they inflame both parts of the vein, and the figure of the cauteries is according to this form near the junction:
Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme;	And if you see a great cautery in the stomach according to this form;
et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l’estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d’enche;	And he who has fear of this cautery, cauterize by pricking and mark on the stomach at that point according to the quantity you see of the wound;
puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».	and then cauterize all the cautery which is called "point".
Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the treatment of the treatment we have had before, until it is cured.
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez;	When the liver comes with pain from heat and moisture and great swelling, so that it is much removed from its natural condition because of excess.
et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil;	and the patients are cured of what we have said in divisions, and they do not benefit from it, unless it is brought to be applied on its own heat.
et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient;	and a mark of the third cauterization according to this form and figure and this quantity on the liver, except for the hypochonders, where the cost is of the belly comes.
et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi;	And hold a space of about an inch between each cautery mark on the size of a dog.
et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere;	And let the cauteries be long on the body, and do not press too hard with your hand all over.
et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez;	And let it be burned only on the moist parts of the wound, and let the patient lie straight on their limbs.
et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais;	And if he cannot, so let him lie on his side, and stretch out his legs, and lift up his limbs.
et c’est li forme:	and this is the form:
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors;	And if your will is, to cauterize these cauteries on the tibia, so that you are subtle and wise in this art, and beware lest you burn all of the wound, for you would be drying out the entire body.
et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	and he shall not suffer from fever because the heat is very subtle to that place, and his senses are able to see.
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile:	When he has an abscess on the liver, and you see if it is in the flesh of the liver or on the membrane.
s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort;	if it is in the flesh, he feels a great pain but not extremely strong;
et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.	and if it is on the membrane, he feels extreme pain.
Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste;	And when this treatment needs to be applied to the patient's head, it is convenient that he should lie on his side.
et puis seigne d’enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:	and then mark the location where the abscess is, and then apply the cautery that resembles the form.
Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers;	And burn the cautery so long as the wounds are red, and it comes forth just like pus, until the infection is completely gone;
aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez;	After the healing according to the remedy for the wounds so that it is safe.
et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.	And it is not to be used of this cautery on anyone who has not thoroughly studied the art of medicine, for by which hands these diseases have been cured no one.
Adonques puet il hardiement ovrer, et toutevoies il me semble que mues vaut li laissier.	And so it can be done with great courage, and I think it's more valuable to leave it.
dou cautere de pleuresin	How to treat peritonitis
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere:	The old men said that we should make purgative cauteries with the roots of Aristogeon, and in this way:
pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois;	Take a root of Aristogeon as long as you can find one, dry it, and make it just as big and just as long as your thumbs.
et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize I cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et II petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe;	and pour the fat in oil, and press it to fire, and cauterize between the warts and the neck, and make cuts one by one while descending towards the area below the chin;
et II cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc;	and cut between the fifth rib and the sixth, in a downward slant after a little.
et I cautere emmi le pis, et I autre sus l’estomac, et I entre II espaules, et II as II costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre II espaules;	and cut on the foot, and one above the stomach, between the two shoulders, and between the two ribs, where the cut is between the two shoulders;
et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	and do not press with your hand, but make an incision so tightly as in an odorant.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a I raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme;	And old men said that no one uses the fire cauterization similar to shaving, and the flint and put it between the ribs, until it reaches the abscess;
