Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis;	When the tears of the eyes flow down into the veins that are on top of the forehead of the strong, and no cure is found with medicine which we make, and you see the face of the patient becoming red and flushed, and feel a pain in the front of the legs as if from cold.
et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	and when the wounds are kept and moist so that the hairs of the paper are cut, and the papers are burnt with the heat of the tears, if need be for this treatment.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front;	And they called it the ancient "cure contuse", and then you would tell the patient who has this illness to let his hairs grow out of the forehead, then make three cuts on the forehead equally according to the length of the forehead;
et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres;	And if it is one of the incisions such that two are made all around the forehead when the head is lowered to make a new cut, and the others are two on top of the papers, and you take care not to cut the arteries which are in these places above the papers;
et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins;	And move your hand away from the continuation of the two jawbones, and make each wound to be three times as large through it.
et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	And have prepared an sponge and some bandages to absorb the blood, then apply the spatula with two parts of it is the shape:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision;	from the incision that is behind the temple, to the second incision;
et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les II fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	Scorch the entire wound that is between the two incisions, all to the surface of the bone, then make another cut from the first incision up to the other second, and then remove that spatula.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	If you prick at the base of the hairs with the "cultellary" instrument, and it is sharp on one side and soft on the other, do not prick too deeply, and this is the form:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	And place the cutting edge towards the raw flesh at the puncture, and the soft part towards the bone, and let it stay until it comes to the middle cut.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer;	And cut off all the hairs that fall from the head until the incision is complete just at this point when the blood vessel opens up, and then make another cut in the middle division just before the other opening.
et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris;	and then extract the blood equally and express it by the vessel taken;
puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne;	then put a tent of white cotton in each incision, and cover it with moist cloths made of wine and oil and ashes, and keep away the stench of pus;
et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and on the third day remove the bandage, and anoint with a great quantity of watered-down plantain juice, then with Basilicon oil and other remedies for wounds until he is healed.
dou reume des eulz	Do not move your eyes.
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees;	When some veins come to be swollen by custom, and you see the eyes turgid and red, and weak the vision, and the papers burn;
et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue;	and the hairs fall out, and in the forehead there is great pain, and the patient sighs;
adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	Therefore you should know from these accidents that those materials and the swelling do not come but from many veins, and the kind of disease there is, if it is this.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And instruct the patient to look at their forehead, then make a deep cut on either side of the forehead and another small cut.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os;	And from the cut in the left temple to the right temple, and so the incision just above the bone;
et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier;	and pull your hand back from the nerve of the temples that move in towards the head;
et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin;	and when the bone is uncovered, so that all the blood seeps into an sponge, and then sew between the two lips of the incision and put cotton wool, and try to apply linen.
puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut;	then tie over the exposed flesh with moistened cloth in wine and oil, and protect it from the heat.
quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	when it is an ulcer, so that you rub the bone until blood begins to flow, then apply the cure of excising, which make the wound dry.
En teil maniere:	In such a way:
pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre;	take two parts of wheatflower and four parts of colophony, and make an emulsion.
et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	and apply this to the wounds to dry them out completely.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Of the rupture of the ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses:	Everything that falls into the ear is one of four things:
ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer;	or dust, or dung, or stone from a mine, or something similar like metal.
ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois;	or seed, such as wheat, barley, beans;
ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	or something that flows out like pus and inflammation, and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When it falls into the ear, stone or some other thing that does not adhere to the ear or grow in the ear, if you put the ear in the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction;	If you see a stone, then take out any little bit of olive oil violet or sesame oil, and then perform the extraction;
et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine;	and let the patient vomit condensation, and stop the nose when vomiting comes, and put a piece of cloth or linen into the ear;
et estent l’oreille au desus.	and hold the ear upwards.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure;	A lot of times comes fever by this treatment;
et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	and if she does not come fever, they should perform an extraction of fine pins, for it is the form:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin;	If it comes through with the fine pins, that's good;
se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure;	if this is not so, let them perform an extraction at the nodule with a fine thread of small suture;
et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne;	and if it does not come through with that, let them make a chain of thread and pour the chief of the chain down into the ear, or through the passage of the ear very deeply, and seal what is around the chain with melted wax so that the thread cannot enter through the chain;
puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit;	then the thread forms a knot, because a lot of times fever comes in this way as we have said;
et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor;	and if it does not come by that method, so it pricks at the blood to see how much comes out, and takes out the ointment, and puts in some instrument which is pointed for this purpose, and puts a little cotton inside;
puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	then presses the glue onto the stone or whatever is there, and pulls it off.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme;	and if it should fail to work with all the things we have said, then hasten to cut off an ear so that the vein is exposed, and causes convulsions.
et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant;	and the way of cutting is that you first make the patient healthy from the head, and extract the blood according to its power, then place the patient between your hands, and turn the ear upwards, and make a small cut at the root of the ear towards the fat or as it depends.
et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche;	and so let the wound be cut as one moon, until you come to the bone, then the tooth according to your power, and suck it out hastily at your mouth;
et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and the cure until it is clean.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction;	And if it's pus that forms and inflames, then extract it;
et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	and if it cannot come out, then apply an iodine plaster subtle according to this form;
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and make an incision from that spot.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces;	But do not do this when you think the pus is moist due to the moisture of the ear, until you have made many small pieces;
puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	then draw it out with fine pins and at the incision, as we have said, so that the extraction is light.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	In water therefore it is said that one should spit into the ear and use sternutine of composites first, and fill the ear with thick cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And be careful on that same ear or in water.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	But if it bursts because of this, it's good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu;	If they do not (listen), then take many cuts according to the length of your body, and make them light and easy; and cast one piece on the fire.
et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille;	and place the patients with one or two perforations in their ear and let them sit on it; from one side of the other, with fear and pain from another stone over the ear that is in the ear.
et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer;	and cease not to make these stones into stones until the pain goes away completely, and then she will pass it all out.
et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars;	and if you see, take a joint, and pour one of the juices into the ear, and the other joint into the fire until the softer joint is burned.
puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	then make another of other joints until the pain goes away completely, just as we have said in the stone.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division;	In the extraction of flesh, if it is of a small body, like a wart and similar things, treat it as we have said in the division.
mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures;	but if it is of a large body one can feel it, so extract the pinpricks.
et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	And this is the lighter thing to be removed that is in the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil:	In the extraction of worms, anoint the ears, as you cure so we have said in the division and when treating distillations, if the cure does not profit, it is good that you look at the ear by sunlight:
s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	if there are no worms, if the throat has small pinpricks, and if they do not appear, then the chain is of this form:
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And it may be narrow from below and wide above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine;	And pourpose the most subtle head into the ear according to the amount of suffering in the patient, then let it swell throughout the entire body;
fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	make this often until all the veins have appeared.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere;	and if they do not appear to be cut, then wrap them in the vein of cotton as I have said in the pierce.
et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations;	and if they do not appear as we have said, administer distillations just like the ancients did in the extraction of worms, and you will find them or treat with distillations;
et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	and if you distill your oils and medicines into the ear with this instrument, so that it may take on the form as you see:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller;	And whether it is of silver or gold, let him take away from under at the little passages, and over the joints to dilate;
et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton;	and by pressing within the dilation of this silver well-made instrument, and if you see the rasp will catch on and pull through the tip with a cloth;
puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille;	then pour your oil or juice, and what you see of your medicine in the channel, and let that run into the ear;
puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille;	then pour into the rasp all the cloth, and press your hand temperately until the oil is distilled or comes out near the ear;
et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille;	and the patient feels it inside, and if the distilled poultice is heated by fire as well as when we dilute it in the ear;
et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	and keep her from being too cold, for the medicine would not be so good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Of the rupture of the ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles;	No child is born without any ears or damage to their ears.
et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir;	And the same thing happens in adults when there is a stoppage of blood or pus inside the ear, and this stoppage can go all the way into the ear canal if it is not treated.
et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	And sometimes the hearing returns, and one can see well again.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil;	So when it goes all the way in and one can't see it, this is often due to an increase in suffering from various conditions, and so you should put the ear of the sick person in the sun.
et regarde dedens:	and look inside:
se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	If you see the swelling around it, if the work is totally smooth because that's its form:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille;	And so it and trenches before and behind all smooth, if it does not touch the ear;
se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	if the swelling is of flesh or bone in the ear, if you have fine punctures, and cut lightly until that flesh is all bone.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the incision goes all the way into the ear, take a fine razor and light it over a small fire, then put it on the bone of the ear.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille;	If you feel the swelling where patients feel great pain in the ear, pierce lightly, and make sure not to rub the nerves of the ear;
puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	then put a tent in the ear according to the size of the perforation, and apply Egyptian powder on it;
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet;	Make this every day until the wound is healed, or take an arsement and put the poultice on with water of roses, and powder over vitriol broken.
et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	and if you see a boil in the ear, apply the arsement and move another poultice moistened with olive oil and wax until the boil is drawn out.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then heal him as soon as he is cured.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if it comes out of blood, plunge an sponge into cold water and wrap it around the ear, and apply other treatments to remove the blood that are in treating hemorrhages.
de la char des papieres	of the fat of paper.
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines;	This remedy which comes in paper when the eyelids are moist and dry, should be stretched with tongs and forceps, and shaved off with a spatula from its root.
puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	then put vitriol on it afterwards.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues;	If without cutting off, you cauterize the lenticle with subtle cautery, and the cauterizer cuts after the incision is made.
et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines;	and often repairs are made, without anything remaining at its roots;
et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	and when they are cauterized with fire, those roots are burned and do not return again.
de la gresle	of the flesh
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz;	Often come in the eyes paper some things that seem to be worms in their form and hardness, and because of this is called "granulon", and it is a collection of gross moisture on top and below.
li ovraiges est telz:	the abscesses are such:
pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir;	take care if the granulon moves from one side and the other, and it's a light thing to know;
fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Fend the wound so it is clean; then scorch from each part lightly; then take hold with pins, and cut.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide;	If you cannot cover the wound because it is too painful for the patient to feel a slight pinch, do not give him anything.
et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	And if the wound is large, assemble it with stitches and treat until it heals.
et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	And if it is small, do not put any pressure on it, because the ointments restore it immediately and cause pain.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre;	And if the gravel is falling inside the ear towards the upper part, reverse the paper, and pick up the gravel with pins, cut and press it from one side and the other.
et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien;	And if the paper is stretched by the incision, it causes no pain.
et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And when the gravel is hit, clean the oil of salted water, and treat the patient who suffers from char so much that they are healed.
de la graisse des eulz	from the fat of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz;	Exinach is a grease that gets stuck in the threads of paper above, and this has caused more deaths among children with no one to care for them, and it gives them much pain to their eyes, and they come to catharsis in the mornings, and cannot look at the light of the sun because tears fall into their eyes;
et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	and because of this they lie on their faces to the ground again, and sleep there, and their paper above their eyes is moist with the exininach that causes inflammation and appearance has changed because it opens in the oil.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press the lock of meat with your hands and feel the swelling between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain;	And the manner of this work is such that the patient puts their head in your hands;
et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li;	and then take a linen cloth, and cover it with a tent made in the shape of a circle according to its content, one quarter for each part, then place it on.
et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle;	and press with both hands from one side and the other, so that the quarts are assembled in the middle of the circle;
puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne;	then make in the middle of the moisture a small gash cutting into it to a length no greater than the wound you made on the vein.
et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach;	and let the skin into it so that you see the quarts;
et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	and many deaths result from dislocations due to a tear in the membrane, according to the shape of a piece of white fatty tissue.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars;	Remove the wound then at once to the entire piece of cloth gauze between your two hands without fail, and turn your hand to right and left until it is spread out.
et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	and keep in mind that you should not add anything to the wound, lest you come across the entire spectrum of the liver just until the oil, lest you blister.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere;	And if the tear does not open at the beginning of the wound, then cut a little bit into the wound lightly until it opens.
puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	then draw it as we have said, then apply the cloth in oil and water, and place it on the wound, and draw back the bandages.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And if there are such men who crush wool and put it on to corrupt the moisture that is left behind.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then the physician, so as to be healthy.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it comes to a joint with abscesses hot, so the cure of splinters satisfying as long as he is healthy.
des poilz des papieres	of hairs from paper.
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz;	When the hair grows back after being shaved, do not shave it at its natural growth, and let it grow for a while, so that it does not harm your eyes, and causes the coming of sorts of diseases, such as excessive sweating, swelling of the skin, and bluish discoloration, until this is the cause of eye damage;
et est li cure selonc IIII manieres:	and they are treated in four ways:
ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	or by cautery, putting fire together, or by water according to what is in front of the chapter on cautery, and being done either by incision and suturing or by tying, according to what I shall say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre;	It is necessary to place the patient's head on a clean cloth, then turn the hair of the affected part towards your left hand;
s’elle est convertie, c’est boin;	She has been converted, this is good.
se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus;	If it's not so, if you inject a needle into the upper filament;
et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur;	and if the margin of the paper or the hairs are between these hairs, and pull the filament up from above to the whole paper, and turn it with the razor;
puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit;	then cuts down from under the paper, under the hairs closest, to all the spine, from the large to the small;
puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	then pull the filament, and put under the paper a small linen tent and a drapery, then cut up the paper with an edge like the flame of myrtle, as far as you see the quantity extracted from the paper which is depicted in all its size.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie;	And if he has taken the paper to write down a great quantity of the parchment according to what the parchment is softened.
puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit;	then writes everything on the second line above what you signed, and begins large writing just below a small.
et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute;	and if one of the incisions is near the natural hairs in the size of a root, then pour some powder into one of the two corners of cut, and scorches it all.
puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce;	then gathers the two lips to a seam with an awl at all threads of fine linen, and sucks up the blood, and makes it dry on the surface of the fibers above both squares at any sticky things, as if you had seen this.
et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII;	and if this does not happen, so you do not have cure, then leave the seam and the hairs just for 3 days or 4.
puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor;	then treat the wound with sewing and binding of things dry, because the paper reappears at the moment of the wound and its assembly, but the seam is weakened (as the ancients said), and it's a work with fear.
et si a une autre maniere:	and if it has another way:
et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	and it is that you sew the paper of a figure like as the fuel of myrtle, as we have told, three times close according to the form which is here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then cut off whatever is standing above with equal force according to its shape.
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure;	And if you do not have the power to hold the tongs, and things are not even, then take an awl or if it has one thread, and poke into the figure;
et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment;	And take another branch of the great fir tree, and the second branch of the small fir tree, and equalize them between your two branches.
puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then tie your hand equally, and tie all the skin where you have stitched, just as we have said; then sew both lips of the wound together with stitches, until it is healed.
et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans;	and if an abscess comes to your incision, calm it with croton oil and similar ointment soothing.
et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit:	and sometimes it happens that the hairs of the papyrus are converted:
si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision;	so if you use what we have said about the incision;
mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	but the stitches in both places are more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme:	The care for the chains is according to this form:
et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est;	And so you must turn the paper and parchment inside according to what I have told you, and then make two chains by art, and two subtle ties just as long as the paper and the width of the measuring stick.
et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz;	and cut at both ends of both parts where you hold the thread;
puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment;	then assemble one and the other subtly above what overhangs from the parchment of the oil, and strain both chains from both parts together.
et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	and let him stay thus for a certain number of days, and the leather that wraps the strained joint will wither and dry and become more firm, till it hardens by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	If it lingers, if the copier has some strength, then treat him until he is healed.
et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil;	and when the wound has closed with stitches, and if it is lifted again, and the hairs do not pull anymore.
et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	and this is the form of two joins that you will make according to this figure, and according to this length and width:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil;	the incisions are such that you will take a very fine needle, and put in the soft and subtle thread of silk.
puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc;	then assemble the joins and needle both subtly, so that the lengths of the threads are one palm long.
puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil;	then put in another fine thread of silk briefly, and no the finer thread.
puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain;	Then place the patient's head on your safe side;
et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil;	and let the sun shine so that the wound is declared, for it is a subtle and small wound; then prick the needle all along the root of the attached hair, and pierce quickly through the skin until you bring it up over the natural hair.
puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors;	then pull the hair up to the point of the needle, and push the needle into that point, if there is one or two or three or more.
puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	then withdraw your hand until the hairs that are freed flow forth all the way to the skin with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil;	And if the needle is pulled and the hairs do not come forth with it, then pull the needle downwards to all the thread that you have ordered, until the needle comes out through the hole above and you see it by the sight of the oil.
adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus;	And so you will pull the hair and thread, and oil it and leave it for two days or three, until the hair is rooted in its place and grows new flesh above.
et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	and if the hairs are short, follow one of the long hairs from the shoulder, and let yourself be lifted along with it, until it is stretched out and then lift.
de la porriture de l’oil	of the oil's spoilage
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres:	When this illness, called "aleacrati" or porphyria, comes to the skin, it has two forms:
l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	one natural, and one unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And happens suddenly from a wound, or cutting, or cautery, and by similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee;	And in the treatment of this, it is done that you cut open the wound, and apply ointment to the lips, and put linen bandages inside, and bind it until it is healed.
et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And do not use this remedy only for curing people with dried up or constricted things.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere;	But if you make it worse, the disease will be even more severe than before.
mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic;	but for softening things, as in fenugreek.
et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	and the arse of water or ale and the seed of flax are cooked, and ointments made from frozen water diluted in any oil, wrapped in a cloth, and given to the patient.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant;	And if your remedy is valuable, that you keep it for yourself so it does not spoil according to the form in which it was before.
et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	and this work we have spoken of is not the fire that burns with a different form than its original form, that it does not return according to the shape in which it was before.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the blood which comes into the oil
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This illness that is below, truly called "axacrati", and is a natural and accidental condition.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans;	The accident comes from a wound and tearing and cauterization and similar things.
et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char;	And the vein of the body is that you prick an arrow, in which it has one double thread, and the nail in the flesh, and you make it pierce from the left side to the right, so that the thread appears in two joints of the arm;
puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	Then tie the skin above all over the arrow, and cover it with a broad spatula.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin;	And if the image on the paper returns according to what is needed, it's good;
se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere;	if that one is not, then take the razor and put it in the wound, and turn the paper, and make two cuts on either side of the paper inside.
et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»;	and let the chips of the two splits of the two angles of the incision which you have cut be there, and make one angle so that when they are assembled, the figure will be as in the letter that has no «i griesche»
puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne;	then cut the bone clean, according to the quantity of its costs that is above the paper, then join the two divided parts, and sew with a thread of linen;
puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then the cure for what we have said about soft medicines and poultices, until he is cured.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant;	And if the sickness comes from a cut or a stitch or a cautery, so that you should make a plain cut below the hairs of the papers, and according to what was said before;
puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit;	Then turn between the second and third fingers of a tent, as I have said;
et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil;	And one must perform the work according to the shape of the disease, for it is very different in form, and the skilled masters make an apparatus from any kind of poor material so that the figure returns to its natural form.
et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	and the patients themselves, according to those things that are required for the work and instruments in those various conditions.
dou soudement de la papiere	Suddenly of the paper
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut;	When this stitch occurs on the palms in a certain way, so that the paper above is soaked with white oil and cannot move or do its natural work, if it is necessary then you must put the point of a rasp over the paper, and lift it up.
et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil;	And the extent as pinches, until you apply what is sharp to the sensitive area, which is neither too harsh nor too thin, so that the patient cannot suffer if it is too harsh or causes the oil to bleach.
et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil;	And if your incision, do not burn the assembled skin lightly, so that the paper (scab) reappears according to its natural form.
et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere;	And when that assembled skin is healed, and there is no occasion for the oil to be poured onto it, but rather the swelling of water is lifted, and cold wine is given.
puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef;	Then place a linen tent between the paper and the oil, and put on the lard oil moistened in abundance of wool.
et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	And after three days, apply to the wound with a bandage and similar things until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	Of fire cautery
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres:	The joint can be in two manners:
elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om;	it is one joint which appears to be inflamed and swollen like the skin after frost, and another that does not appear nervous but seems frozen with moisture, when touched with iron and cared for as if pinched, it cannot come.
et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	and both seem to begin towards the great artery, and grow little by little until they cover all the eye and all the light and the movement of the oil.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz;	And the way of making an incision is that the patient puts his head on a clean cloth, then opens his eyes;
et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus;	and lifts the paper in his hand, then coils the joint like stitches of fine sewing, and extends it upwards;
puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort;	Then take a needle, and put some horsehair, or goat hair, or oxen hair, and tie it tightly;
et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement;	And double the point of the needle a little and sew it into the horn, so that the needle goes all the way through the horn, and tie the horn with a thread and attach the end to above, and scrape off at the entire length of the hair where the wound is located, until the red blood comes out and the black hairs appear on the hair just up to the head; then cut the remaining part in the root of the nail bed for a small distance, and leave it as nature intended, so that there does not come from the incision the flesh around the nails as is customary;
et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit;	And at times, only attach the horn to the wound and the thread.
puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	Then the scorching is applied to all the surface of what is sore, as this is the form.
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie;	And that the scab does not touch the raw flesh and break it, and that the wound is not perceived;
et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor;	and after the incision, pour some powdered salt into the oil and make a poultice on the collarbone, and let it remain until the next day;
puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then treat him as necessary so that he may be cured.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines;	and if the warts are not nervous and you cannot poke the needle in, and the wart does not take entry, then this similar appearance of a wart is cured with medicine.
et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	and they grow as I have told in the division, and if you see them cover, then apply oil to the patient, and take the spatula lightly in good shape according to this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor;	And press the inflammation under subtly, and if you see that it shrinks and the reason is pressing hard, then distill from your mouth into the oil made of litharge, and red wax, and let the oil rest for another day:
puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	then re-commence the other work according to this same operation, until she is completely hollowed out.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If there is no objection to the oil, as with an abscess, then apply the medicine and let the pus, and cure the abscess first until it is healed; then resume the operation in the same way as before, until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne;	And if the appearance of the skin is troubled by the lump in the oil with great damage, so that it weeps at night, and you lance one part of it not entirely, let there be no blood.
puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	Then distill in olive oil red colour which is made from litharge.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the fire that is born on the eyelid
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste;	Are there some men who are born without red hair, and cover their baldness with a wart, and restrain themselves against the paper and the thorn; and it seems like a rose on a bust.
et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force;	And the ulcers are so that the patient puts his healthy head on it, then opens the eyes, and stitches all of that with suitable threads to its shape, and supports it with strength.
puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige;	then cut the first one off, and go to sawing until the end, and be careful not to bleed on the wound.
et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre;	and if the incision is with spatula as we have said in the incision of the warts and with small forces because one is unable to remove it soon, like the shape after this chapter shows.
et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut;	and when the incision is completed and all of the char are removed, then apply oil from a broken twig or distill it with colored wine and similar corrosive medicines, and place on the affected cotton wool with beeswax, so that it be secure at the abscess.
et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut;	and if it does not improve and the affected area is covered with a scab, and you doubt that it has healed, then leave the oil and let the abscess be soothed.
puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	and then return to your work until it is healed, and similarly apply the char to the affected area in the oil by this similarity.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil;	But for all cases, it is necessary to lighten the remedy of each weak oil by the natural way.
et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer;	And of the accidental vein, when working with iron;
et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	and do not press my hand on any of these wounds until you see that this member is suffering from the wound.
des voines des eulz	of the eyes.
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	These eyes are red veins that are covered on the surface of the eye, and they tolerate their treatment on the eye and weaken them every day.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel;	And then is the art of first looking at whether the oil is hot, cold, hard, or soft, and there is no other disease but the hardness.
adonques le coil en teil maniere:	and therefore bind it in this manner:
comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	instruct the patient to put his head on your clean one, then tie those veins all over according to his wisdom, and let the subtle ones double up according to this shape:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en I cors selonc ceste forme:	And let them be two times one by degree in the form of a circle:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil;	and then bind tightly those subtle veins, and suck out the sore hour after another, until you see that the hot veins have been removed from the oil.
et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes;	And be careful not to prick the oil with the points of the lancets, and do this work at noon in front of the sun, and be very hot in your work so that you only suffer what is due to women.
et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	And when you have done this, if you dilute in the oil a yellow and green vinegar and red for to corrupt what is remaining in the swell.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez;	And if you do not have power to remove all of this in that one hour, then apply on the oil soothing things for the eye's pain and leave it for some days until the pains are eased and be sure of having removed the abscess, then resume according to this manner as long as he is healed.
et c’est li forme des forces:	And this is the form of the forces:
de la fistule de l’oil	Of the boil of the oil
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule:	The mire so named "arissati" fistula:
quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	When you cure it with cautery and medicine hot as I told you, and it's not healing, if there is an infection in it, then you must cut open the abscess, at that place where it may die, and remove all the moisture that is in it, until the bones are exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme;	And when the bones are exposed, and you see the corruption and blackness, if that is the shape;
et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a I chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	and it is called "aspere chief", and it should be made like iron in that chief part, and you should pierce it like a file like as it is in the present shape:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese;	And put the new bone on top of the corrupt one, then turn it between your two hands, and press your hand onto it slightly until you feel that corruption is removed;
et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	and do this whenever you want, then restore him to his former state of medicine.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez;	but if the liver is inflamed and so is the body of the bowel, and they remain like that for 40 days, and he does not recover and there is no discharge or inflammation, then it can be said that he is cured.
se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme:	but if this is not the case, then there is no other remedy but to bring the fistula back to its original position according to this form:
et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	and that you uncover the bone the second time with iron, and with sharp medicine, and when he heals from uncovering so it is punctured according to this form, and let the clavicle be fixed in three angles, and the fistula be softened until just above the head as you see.
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif;	Then put it on the bone near the cartilage, and pull your hand away from the oil for a little while, then turn to all the forest until you penetrate the bone and the patient feels it with what comes in this way if he holds his hand over his neck.
et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif;	and then restore the patient to a healthy diet of dry medicines as I have instructed you, and when he bears and hardens his limbs, let him eat this material on his neck.
si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	if it is a lighter thing for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	From the issue of oil
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide;	When the eyes are open all the time, and it does not come to relieve the head, or softening, then you must tie up the patient.
puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz;	then he heals, then you put ventouses or haterel near to pierce for relief, then put on the oil which is made of ice and aloe and incense and sarcocolle, and then strain the oil, and apply it with plaster of benedict and strips.
et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier;	and the manner of dressing wounds is that you take soft bandages, and wrap each one four times, and then put one on top of the other according to how many there are in need;
puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir;	then tie under a hard bandage to form, and then resume the suckers to draw out with pain;
puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout;	then remove the suckers and let the oil tie him tight day and night, and if it is tied too loose, so that you tighten more;
puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin;	then remove the tie after day and night, and if you see the oil repairing, that's good;
se ce non;	if not;
si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	so you resume the poultice and bandages, and the tie and suckers until he is healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	Discharge of the pupil
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir;	When disruptions come to the eye, it opens, and there comes forth from the papers as if grains of resin, and it is astonishing to see;
adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier;	And therefore if you cover the eye, the wounds are such that you put a needle in the root of the part below where it is just above, then put another needle where there is a double thread from the part of the eyelid;
et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition;	and pierce it, and let the first needle according to its position;
puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef;	then cut the vein of the double thread and tie a part of the eye shut, and tie it well, then pull out the needle and apply olive oil moistened in abundance to the wound;
et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee;	and let it stay until the threads come together with the eye, then treat the olive oil on comforting things until the wound is healed;
et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And sometimes the wound is bound up with a cloth around every quarter of a circular bandage until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost;	And if the eyes appear swollen, then prick at the spot with a sharp needle that is submerged in olive oil and wipe away the moisture so that the swelling goes down and enters it immediately.
puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then extract as much of it as can be made whole.
de la bowe de l’oil	from the oil of the bowels
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue;	This disease called "alcunnati" is only caused by a bowing that is assembled in the oil, similar to the flow of water downwards, and it's not actually water.
et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz;	and if the appearance of the wound is such that you make the patient sit upright on a specially prepared bed, then take hold of his head with both hands of two parts, and push it until you see the bowing coming to the top towards your eyes;
puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit;	Now it is moved, and does not descend or break away; and see how the light shines on the patient's things as they usually do.
et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	and if it does not descend below, you know that it is sick, and the movement of the bowels is not prepared as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse;	If you sit the patient between your hands, then take a fine knife and do upwards on the thin membrane in the corner of the eye with the continued stitching of the membrane and the crown, as long as the bowels are loose.
et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and when it has been drawn out, if you distill it in hot, sweet oil mixed with honey or boiled fenugreek and honey, then the patient is cured from another cure until they are healthy.
des aigues de l’oil	of hot oil
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier;	We have the same symptoms as blood in the division, and what is needed for piercing;
si en oevre selonc la santeit.	as according to health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort;	It is necessary that you make the patient sit between your hands, cross fire of the light from the sun, and tie the healthy oil very tightly;
puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres;	then place the paper of oil on your left hand if his eyes are to the left, or on your right hand if they are to the right;
puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre;	then grasp in your right hand if his eyes are to the left, the instrument called "almagda", or in your left hand if they are to the right;
puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide;	Instruct the head of the instrument to put its point on the crown by the growth of an arrow in that blackened oil droplet at the less tender part; and then pour the instrument which is called "almagda" effectively, and twist your hand so it penetrates into the blackened oil droplet, and feel when almagda comes to life in what appears to be empty.
et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour;	and it is necessary that the measure of the almagda instrument be exactly one finger's breadth from the root of the nail to the end of the dark spot.
et c’est li corone de l’oil;	and this is the crown of the oil.
si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	if you see the bone through the paper due to the clarity of the eye's cornea, and then put the instrument exactly at that spot where the water is, then press downwards in one direction after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If the fever has come down now, so he sees the patient in front of him and the instrument on his table.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc;	After rest for a little while, and if the pain comes back in the second way, put force with the instrument, and when it is set and does not come up again, gently pull slightly by turning your hand now and then;
et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	And then put in the water a little piece of silk gauze, and take out the oil within.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then put in place the oil-soaked cloth or a moist linen soaked in rose oil and plenty of rue, and tie it with pure oil.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	Also, and those of our time, let us use a common broth with plenty of rue.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the powder cannot be inserted into the oil because of its hardness, since there are many men with very hard eyes, so you should take up the instrument called "alberit", for it is in the shape:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit;	And therefore prick only the conjunctive, and do not go too deep, but make it subtle, then put in a little oil, as we have said;
et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous;	And when the work is completed, the surgeon will come to attend the patient in the dark chamber where he lies on his back.
et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor;	And be careful of all movements, and give gentle food, and do not move his head or right arm or left arm, and bind him according to his disposition just as if he were tied the day before.
puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor;	Then take him to the same dark house, and let him see his vision, and make him look at some things, and then put the limb back in its place seven days.
et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And it is not necessary to do that in the patient's room after the incision now, but it is necessary to alleviate him, because his illness rises rapidly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme;	If an abscess forms on the wound, you will dislodge it seven days after that, and address the one who cures abscesses.
et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	And when he is appeased, dislodge his eye and put on a linen face to cover it for one day, and be taken back to that dark house.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas;	And then he will come from the house little by little, and will turn into his case;
et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	and knows that no disciples should intervene in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens;	And then one came to us who was from the Irag, who told us that in some far-off lands they practiced a certain kind of operation, by which they treated the water, but I have never seen it or heard of it in any book among our people, nor did we know of it.
et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	and perhaps this is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie;	And these are the likenesses of the forms of al-magd, because those who do not know them see them.
et soient d’arain proprement:	and they are very clear.
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	And the head of arsenic from this same subtlety, and the lower parts are in threefold angle.
de la char sor le neis	of the shoulder bone on the neck
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez;	No limbs are ever born with uneven or misaligned feet, because it is so that some seem like scorpions by a multitude of points.
et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	and if it is some such limbs where the bone is thick and blackened with red flesh, and some have bone soft of white color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil;	In such cases of those limbs that are soft and not thickened, it is necessary to sit the patient between your hands against the sun;
et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers;	and cover his nose, and pour on the salve to those limbs, and let them burn;
pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	till you can bear to sustain it on a small, fine, and subtle spoon, for as long as you know that limb is entirely bled out.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien;	And if there remains any part that cannot be covered, then apply all of the subtle signs to lightly.
et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient;	and if there is no wound or abscess, then cut as it seems to be.
et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	and if it's malignant abscesses, then hasten and cauterize until the sinew is stained and all the cartilage is cleaned, then give or give as you wish, hot water or vinegar, wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez;	If the medicine overcomes and moisture comes into contact with the place just above the throat, they know he is cured.
et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier:	and if moisture does not penetrate as it should, they know there is a bone hidden in the above os, for which the signs do not come to cut.
adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins;	And so it is necessary that you put a small thread of flax into the wound, and let it be bound by hand with a knot, and there should be no space between each one, it must at least be.
et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche;	And put the patient's head into the flax thread so that it gets into some pain, and treat with an odorant until it comes out through the nose inside the mouth.
et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire;	and many times do it this way to children in school, and that is a light thing for the one who has to do it.
puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	then hold the head that comes by the nose with one hand, and the other head that comes by the mouth with the other hand, and check one after the other while we are in the flax.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant;	Do as you wish to know that the flesh has not been corrupted by anyone else, then take the child, clean the wound, and anoint the infant with Egyptian balm, and set them right upon the fire if it is before.
fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char;	Do as you wish three days or more, until the balm has corrupted all that remains of the flesh.
et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use;	and then put a poultice of horse dung for several days until they are healed, and if it needs to be made from dried medications, then use them.
et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	and this is the form of the instrument for purging the head, because one distills the oils and the medicines or poultices:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi;	And it should be of silver or lead, resembling a lampshade, like a poultice, and conduct it similarly;
