et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief;	And if you see, then make a bandage tight, and let the discharges plain so as to cleanse the head.
et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And put some oil or any liquid on the head to keep it moist.
de la char sor le neis	of the shoulder bone on the neck
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder;	Often the head swells with pus because of a disease called "telul", and it grows and becomes large abscesses, until it is filled with something to be seen.
et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant;	and therefore it is advisable to make a poultice at the beginning, and let the bone all burn, then put on him the cautery or the hot medicine.
et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens:	and if it is delayed in being poulticed until it has grown large, then take care if it is hard, of the fresh flesh, the poor sense.
si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide;	If it touches him with iron because it is an enchanted abscess, for when he strikes once, so much evil comes to the patient;
et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	But if the abscess is touched with a soft touch, not iron or harsh color, and you see whether it can be fully covered, then open the patient and strike with fear, and treat the wounds with drying substances and restraining.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	When the nails are struck and scratched
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Knowing that when many solutions continue to come into one of these old cartilages, little profit is obtained in some men.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc;	It is therefore necessary to see whether such an event occurs again, when you examine if the wound is fresh and all of its blood.
et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	and therefore add two stitches to the wound, then treat him until he is healed.
et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet;	and if the lips are cut on one side and the other, it is necessary that you scrape all the parts of their wound until they heal, then reassemble the two stitches, and bind them, and sprinkle above with powder of dragon's blood, and burned incense.
et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	and put on the powders a piece of plaster made from strong or other kinds of resin, and let it dry until it hardens, then treat with binding until it is healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution:	The manner of sewing if you have assembled the solution:
ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre;	or with needles, as we said in stitching around the navel.
ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	or with thread, as I have told you.
des apostemes des levres	of abscesses on the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant;	Inflammation inside the lips has occurred like pus in abscesses, such as grains of sand, and smaller and larger ones.
adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie;	therefore it is necessary to return the lips, and split each one open, and take out with pinches and cut into each part.
puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	Then apply the liver to the wound after the vitriol incision is broken, until it is stained.
et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then apply the liver of onions, and treat the liver with dry things until it is healthy.
de la char des gencives	of the flesh around the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»;	Many times they grow on the gums next to the teeth that the old people call "albulus".
si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc;	if it is fitting to hold it with the tongs, and cut at its root, and let the blood flow or the vein.
puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives;	then put on the liver vitriol broken, or other restraining and desiccative powders;
et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize:	and if that one returns after the incision, and it often happens, if you cut it a second time, and cautery.
si ne revient mie aprés le cautere;	if it does not return to its place after the cautery;
et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	and these are forms of ulcers that cover.
des sordens	from sounds
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres;	There are no times that they gather at the head of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, scales which are ugly and rough;
et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant;	and no time do the teeth turn black and yellow and wormy, until corruption comes to the gum, and the teeth stink;
si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien;	it is advisable that you make the patient sit between your hands, and his head be on your lap, and reset the teeth or scales as soon as they appear, until nothing stays.
et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees;	and do the same for blackening and greenish, yellowing and other discolorations, until they have disappeared;
et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin;	And if one has removed what is at the first reason, it is good;
se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis;	If this does not work, then repeat the operation on the second day and the third day, until you have completed all.
et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens;	And know that the teeth have need of various forms of instruments to cut and file, according to what the work shows, because those who use razors to avoid damaging the teeth have other forms than those which are used between the teeth;
et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	And these forms and others be prepared with you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire;	It is fitting when you treat the tooth that causes pain that you delay treatment for as long as possible, because it should not be delayed.
car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	Because it is a highly flammable substance, just as, therefore, you should have no excuse for delay.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Therefore when the patient is constrained to treat it, if you wish to be certain of the tooth's swelling.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent;	Many times does the pain come to the patient, and he thinks it is due to a tooth, and he has the good tooth treated.
et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors;	and it does not depart the pain completely until the evil one is removed, for we have already wanted to do this at those healers.
et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars;	and when you are sure about the tooth that is causing it, then it is fitting to burn around the tooth entirely with a small spatula, very hot, in order to protect the gums from all sides.
puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles;	then the teeth are scraped with your two fingers or fine tongs at first point by point, until they are well exposed, then firmly close the tongs.
et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	and let the head of the patient be in your hands between your two thumbs, and so tight that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After extracting the right tooth directly into the broken place, and if it does not spring forward, take out any of these instruments and put them inside each part lightly, and move him as you did first.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont;	And if you see the teeth are broken and bleeding, then it is fitting to fill them with cloths, at the places where they are torn.
et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre;	and if you gently grasp with tongs so that it does not break while grasping.
et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	and it is fitting to carefully put oil over the gums in order to dislodge the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And be well guarded that you do not break it, and keep one part remaining, and tell the patient again by the malice of the root for greater pains from the first.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit;	But beware so that you do not do as the unskilled servants of the lord who, by their haste and boldness, break the chariot every time and do not bring me such things as we have told.
mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut;	but sometimes they bring about this great illness by the root of that disease remaining, or by breaking the chariot as we have often wished.
et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil;	And when the teeth are three, so wash the mouth with wine or ale and with salt.
et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet;	and if blood comes from the wound, which often happens, then apply the vinegar of Vitriol.
et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And if that does not work, then cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent;	The forms of the abscesses are in that manner because if you mute the teeth first, they have long points and thick roots, which do not double up when you pull out the tooth;
et ce sont les formes:	And these are the forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And are broad branches so that they do not fold up when pulled; and are made of good iron well-made, and are pointed to hold the tooth.
de la racine des dens	from the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou II, tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne;	When the root remains after pulling, it is advisable to put cotton soaked in butter on the wound for one or two days until the pus is melted, and then take out the tongs called "algefri", because the flesh seems like a sore.
et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	And let them be done in this way as a lime, and it is the form:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out from all these ties, so it is fitting that you uncover the entire chariot around the root, and put in the instrument which is called "althali", that is to say, a lancet, for this is its form:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin;	And if it's a great cut and large, but not so that it breaks apart, and the root bursts out from this, then it is good.
se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	If that does not happen, then take all the roots, so that the forms come after.
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you help yourself with this instrument that has two blades, for this is its form:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other instruments that are in front of the reason of the teeth, and of this instrument which seems like great pincers, for this is its form:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont;	And if this root is strong so that it cannot break, and you have taken much of the roots from there.
et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez;	and also of other roots, which are not counted.
et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	and the wise masters cleverly treat themselves with their own instrument, according to what his works and illnesses show, because there are some of these diseases that the old do not teach instruments for the variety of them and for fear that it will break or on other bones, or putrefy, if he seeks the roots that it is needed, as I have told you, and aids with movements, so that this is the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster;	And let them be large and well-held to hold the bone, which does not slip away but can be held and removed;
et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	and then restore the person to their proper medicine, if it has putrefaction in the bone and it is small, so that they can use all this instrument;
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer:	When the teeth appear not according to their natural form, and the shape is ugly, especially in young women, it is necessary that you know whether the teeth are new after the tooth, and not in its proper place, and one cannot be satisfied or fixed.
adonques lou raie;	so the cut;
et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	and if it is swollen with the tooth, take that instrument which has this shape, and is like a small beak, and is made of iron very sharp in some way:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the file is held in hand for a few days to soften the hardness of the tooth, and because one does not move the other teeth, and if it appears that we can fix it, take a small amount of lime as much like this shape.
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles;	and is also as when one makes the flint into needles;
et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece;	and by striking the flint in small points and hard blows, as long as it does not move
puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	then the blade is flat by the end and does not remove anything; if its edge is too sharp and it bites the tongue, then it should be honed until even so that it does not bite the tongue and corrupt the speech.
quant li dent lochent	When the teeth are loose
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut;	When the tooth is in front of a wound, either by percussion or by falling out, and the patient cannot press on it because it hurts so much that he cries out.
si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques;	so it is advisable to bind them with a thread of gold, because the silver threads become green and rotten, but the gold never moves.
et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens;	And so let the hairs grow long or too short not too thick nor too thin according to the space between the teeth;
et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part;	And if you see the teeth directed towards each other, take the file and put it double between two healthy teeth, then insert the clamps between your teeth, one by one or more, until you hold them securely to the sound tooth on the opposite side;
puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point;	Then resume the covering as you started, and strain your hand carefully until it does not move.
et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	And if your ligature is tied to the root of the tooth so it cannot escape;
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue;	Then bind the clamps with the thread to tongs, and tie them together, and place them so that they do not bite your tongue;
et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil;	And then he lets it remain thus constricted as long as it can stay in place; and if it is loosed, or the child cries, so that another child may be stretched.
si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	if it remains and serves thus for all of its time, and this is the form of the bones and the shape of the two sound teeth, and the two missing ones, just as you see.
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit;	And when a tooth falls out, it is placed back in its proper place, fresh as new, just as we have said.
et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	and do not put it in the place of someone who is untrained and unsound; and never make a tooth of raw bone, and place it back at the place where it was defective, and fasten it as we have said, so that it remains and serves for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	to cover the joint of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi;	No cases occur when this joint comes from below the tongue or by nature, so it is born thus;
ou par accident de plaie soudee;	or by accident of a seared wound;
et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue;	and the wounds are such that you open the patient's mouth, and hold his head still, and lift the tongue;
puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement;	then cut the nerve in the neck, until the tongue is loosened from its place, and if it has hardened or another wound, and this happens suddenly from a blow, then inject the vinegar and cut deeply at the joint;
et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz;	and guard that the wound is not too deep, lest there be injury to the artery below;
et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin;	and when you have done this, lift the patient to fresh water and asepsis, or cold water, then place under the tongue a linen bandage;
et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	And the patient with each night the disease will suffer, so the limbs cannot heal.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet;	And if they come from blood clots, then apply vitriol on the limb broken.
et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu;	and if they do not swell, then cauterize with fire at the same time as before, which is good for them.
puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	then the doctor will try another treatment until they are healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre;	and if you see a foul odor or red or black flesh, so the patient does not feel it, and do not touch anything because it is a chancre.
et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre;	and if he leans to one side and there is moisture, then pour the pus, and gently remove it with a spatula from both sides.
et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer;	And if they are not careful at their work, so that the glass is broken and cuts until it is stained, then return to your work as soon as you treat all force.
puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then lift the limb up high and straighten it out, and treat other patients until he is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	The swelling of the throat.
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde:	There is no occasion for the throat to swell, which are called "godath", and the proper name is applied to both sides, and when you treat them, as we have said in the division, if they do not heal, be careful:
se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	if it is thick pus of small sense and flesh color, do not touch it with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc;	And if it is red and the root is large, do not touch it with iron, for fear of its hemorrhaging.
mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi;	But let him wait until he is dead, and then you will have to take him apart, for it would break by itself.
et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if his flesh is of white color and the roots are subtle, then have prepared the instrument to cover him; but first look whether the abscesses have closed and are calmed.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme;	Then place the patient in front of the sun, and his joints be sound; and open his mouth and press the linen between his hands, and push the tongue beneath all the instrument, for this is its form.
et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	and it may be of silver or of subtle tin like our scales.
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues;	Can you push the tongue to all of this instrument, and then see the abscess, if take the lancet and make a puncture in the almond, and pull it forth above what is possible.
et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces;	And take out any threads or yarns with you, then cut at the instrument, for this is the shape that looks like one of the forces;
et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	And the head is curved in both places, and they are very good, and made of iron or tin.
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument present, then use a pair of tongs, because that is the form:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom;	It is pierced from one side and the other side as well.
et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	And when you have pierced one of the almonds, pierce the other in the same manner, and after the incision, gargle the patient with hot and cold water, or cooked grape skin, or myrtle flowers, and similar things, until the wound is closed.
puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then the cure will be complete when he is healed;
et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	And sometimes there are abscesses born in the throat besides the two almonds, so if they are filled then like the two almonds binding.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens;	And I treated a woman with an abscess that was near the throat, which is to say the small abscess.
et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	and had it very close the throat so that the woman could not breathe through the constricted passage, and could neither eat nor drink, and was dead if she remained like this for one or two days.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscesses are standing so high that they have been filled with two rains through the two entrances of the nose.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe;	I therefore immediately took action, and placed in one of the incisions, then poured forth fire, and a large portion of sulfur.
puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue;	and then fixed another incision on the other perforated side of the abscess, and held open the mouth and pressed the tongue.
aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc;	After applying the cautery to those abscesses, and cutting off a part of them, only a small amount of blood issues.
et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens;	and then they cut off the conduction of the throat in the woman, and now she began to drink water and wine, and did not cease cutting at that abscess for a long time.
et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros;	and the abscesses reopened again, and filled up what I had previously drained, until it became very large;
adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge:	so then I inserted it and cautered inside the throat:
ensi demora sens croistre;	then he remained without growth.
et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	and I separated from those parts, and only God knows what was done after that to him.
de l’uve	of the eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»;	When it descends into the hole and falls and is extended and lengthened, then it is called "perpendicular".
et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	and if she is too large and rounded, then she is called "vein".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes;	When she is treated as we have said in the division, and the cure does not benefit from it, and you see that the swelling of the abscess subsides, and she is subtle, then it is wise to copy her.
et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe;	and those which are rounded and assembled do not grow longer;
et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	and if she is red or has a bloody color or black, then it is wise to close the incision.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	Because there is great danger for the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant;	It is then advisable, when you see it, according to the manner I have said, about its size and length, that you sit the patient in front of the sun, and press his tongue with the instrument we have mentioned earlier.
puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	Then cut off the appendix at the root, and pull out the tumor, and strike it with a blade on the two struts that I have mentioned in the incision of the two almonds.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil;	And it is necessary that you do not cover just the surplus, which is beyond the natural limit;
car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle;	because if you cut more than that, it will grieve your voice and speech.
et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and after the incision, use what we have said about the two almonds, and treat it until it is healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patients have fear of cutting, it is necessary that you use an engine to cauterize the fearful senses.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the manner of cauterization is cool water.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere;	And the patient puts their head on your healthy one, and then presses the tongue with the instrument that we have said in the fire cautery, and binds it with hot vinegar cloth, so that it is not too thick nor too clear.
et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And when using this instrument, so that there is the form:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve;	And put on the chief either a hair or an ointment, just like the dressing of a spoon, and place the instrument all over the medicine on the wound.
et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece;	And the patient is gouty on his chest, so that the sweat and mucus run from his mouth onto the medicine inside, so that it does not descend to the throat, but to the bile;
puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie;	Then hold your hand all over the medicine and press on the wound, the quantity of half an hour's time, until you see it congealed and the pain from the medicine is assuaged;
et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve;	And if you see that, take cotton and unfold it over any instrument, and moisten the cotton in the medicine, and pour the instrument into all the cotton in the tube above, until the cotton sticks to the wound;
et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V.	and do this often, until the fire cautery is complete, then let it dry, and cast after four days or five.
Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine;	And if you have need to restart the fire cautery of the medicine, so that it is restarted, and after the cautery has dried on the wound, with cotton stuffed in butter, and clean what is around the medicine.
et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	and let him be raised with cold water, and let him be cured of gargarisms until he is made whole.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere;	This cure is safer than the incision, whether it is a cautery.
s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir;	if it is cured with fumigation in this manner, take celery and hyssop and origanum and rue and chamomile and avronne and similar herbs, and assemble them all or some of them in an alembic, and heat them.
et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	And let the wounds be closed with strong glue from hard earth, and using this kind of instrument on your head.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie;	And it can be made from either lead or arsenic, and one of the fingers pounded into the mouth of the sick person until the vapour rises to the eye through the wound, until the eye is numbed.
aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent;	Afterwards, repeat the operation many times until the eye dries, and make sure you do not perform this at the beginning of the incubation period of the abscess, for more things happen.
et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	and do not perform this unless at the point of inciting an abscess.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut;	And if that instrument is not present, take a needle and put it into the head of the wound, so that the mouth of the patient does not get too hot;
car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	For the fire cautery does not help with milk or cream because the vapor weighs down the mouth, and this is a good cure together for salvation.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose;	Many times it happens to the throat when an arrow or a fish bone is swallowed, or nothing at all.
si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose;	Therefore it is necessary to treat what you can see, and press the tongue on the sun at all the instruments, so that you see if the thing moves.
et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac;	And what is not apparent and returns to the throat, it is necessary to make the patient vomit, so that the flesh be cooked in the stomach.
par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement;	In case if the thing becomes exposed by vomiting;
ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec;	Or if the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of onion, or a root of lettuce, or a piece of dry bread.
et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse;	and tie the sponge to the finger, and then the glutens.
et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer;	and when it arrives at the elbow, if you feel pain, and then pull out the arrow.
et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	and if it does not come from what we have said, take an instrument of splint according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit;	and let the curved instruments be at the head so that they can more easily enter into the throat, and lift the head up high.
et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens;	and be careful not to touch the epiglottis, lest it die, or press the bone into the throat.
et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse;	and make sure that the patient is pressing the instrument, because he feels it sharp or rough.
si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	If the boil erupts, or if he treats it with force to all of the instrument equally, until it is forced.
de la sansue de la gorge	about the cutting of the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines;	It is never cured without the help of medicine, as I have said in the division, by the cure of medicines.
et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	and when it does not benefit him, then look into the throat of the sick person towards the sun, and press the tongue with the instrument that I told you.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the wound open, then when there is just one small incision, or with fine tongs that are worth it.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if this is not worth it, take a small hairpin, and push it into the throat of the sick person, then pour or give some warmth to the body.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if the patient is afflicted with fever every day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent;	then take a full glass of cold water and open the mouth, and let it flow in towards the senses to be swallowed, and move it with your hand often.
et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	and if as soon as he begins to feel the water in his stomach, he vomits.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve;	and if he does not vomit as we have said, then submerge the sick person in boiling ash, with the instrument that I told you in the process of smudging the wound.
fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	Do this many times, because she will fall more often.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument;	And the manner of fumigation if there is a vessel with charcoal inside, and it is covered by a cord pierced in the middle, and with that pierced part are the joints of the instrument.
puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue;	then I will take the fumigation, and the patient puts his head in a cage and closes the mouth, so that the smoke does not enter, but comes from above.
et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois;	and now the snake will fall, and if it does not come out, then continue the fumigation many times.
et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue;	and the patient suffers from thirst, eats foul and putrid things, and does not drink any water.
et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	and then thus the art of surgery is most suited when it happens through this governance.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge;	And the form of the instrument with which one treats the wound, if it is so that when one sees it, resembling curved tongs to enter into the throat;
et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier;	and has the appearance of a snare, and has roughness like lime, so that what it takes will not loosen.
et vez ci la forme:	and thus there is this form:
li chapistres des apostemes	The surgeons of the abscesses.
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille;	Many signs of an abscess are, according to what the memory comes after in this book, and differ in perforation and size;
et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	and it is in two manners, one of which is similar to the other, and because of its moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second manner is for those that are within them or in their body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	because the abscesses in the head are different from those in the cheekbone, and the abscesses of the shoulder are different from those in the joints, and each has its judgment in the book.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement;	And if we do not pierce an abscess when it is not ripe according to its completion;
et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And if there are such abscesses that it is necessary to pierce them when they are ripe, and do not die according to their completion, just like abscesses near joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	When an abscess comes from between the joints, and it is left until it is putrid in the meantime, by chance if the tissue and nerve of the joint have decayed, because that is the reason for the contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil;	Where the abscess is near a principal member, and if you delay the perforation until it is dead, it will harm the principal member.
ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs;	or if it is near a foundation, and pierce it so that it becomes dead;
et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule;	And it is not necessary to pierce an abscess when it is ripe for digestion, but rather that you pierce the one near a foundation, so that it does not burst from within and become inflamed, and form a fistula;
et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	and cannot heal in great time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes;	and it is wise to know the nature of the perforation of an abscess, which is dead according to completion, and this is when the pain is alleviated, and the departure of fever, and the lessening of pain and redness, and of swelling and of the dullness and sharpness of the abscess head, and other signs.
et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues;	and it is wise to sit down the perforation where it is more dependent on the abscess, and in the place where it opens.
et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	and if the perforation is at a long distance from the body, and when the abscesses are in hands or feet, joints, nails, arteries, and on all those equal places where there is no pulsing.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	When the limbs are swollen, by some cause of inflammation.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when an abscess is in the groin, if it needs to be let out, leave the perforation open until the inflammation is completely resolved, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure;	If you pierce him in front of this, so it goes away by letting loose the body from the poison of it, and is filled with a great amount of filth;
et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	and by chance they harden the lips and the deepest part of him.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if an abscess is pierced according to the size of the body, according to what the limb has need.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus;	And it is necessary to bring in small pus-filled wounds, small perforations;
et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme;	and in large pus-filled wounds, large perforations, and many cuts according to the similarity of the size of the abscess;
et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper;	and if such an abscess has formed in which it is necessary to cauterize the wound and cover;
quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes:	when it has become like the bandages, and is muffled, so it is necessary to do the same as they do with the buboes;
et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres;	And if there are those that are split into three angles, and if there are those who have cuts like the wood of myrtle, just as abscesses from Angers;
et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	and if there are those where they make a round cut, and other sizes and similar cuts.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement;	Those who do not have a head, as if an abscess is superficial, it is fitting that you pierce it cleanly;
et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie;	and it is fitting when the abscess is large and has accumulated great swelling, and you pierce it, so that not all of the swelling is removed in one hour, but only a part;
puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief;	then stop the abscess just as it is, and on the following day do not remove any of that;
fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute;	Do this repeatedly over time until the bowel is whole.
meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	Even if the patient is weak, or a woman in childbirth, or small children, or old men who are decrepit.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	But if you expect that the patient will be saved every time with the outcome of the pus, then you will not be disappointed.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite;	Therefore be careful with this chapter, and when you have pierced your abscess, if the wound is present, and look to see whether the wound from the abscess is small;
et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton;	and if it's a simple incision, then apply tanned linen or old cotton to it;
et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre;	and if it's a great abscess and there is much pus, it is advisable to apply one tanning on each side so that they meet against each other;
et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor;	And if you have pierced in the abscess a part of the skin, and you have stitched it inside, so it is necessary that you fill it with old cloth or with linters of linen without moisture, and tie it to this point every day;
puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then the bone, and the physician of ointments until he is healthy.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if you come from blood, bring anointing with cool and clear water and cold oil, and wrap it around the limb covering it many times.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut;	And if the blood flows persistently, so that he is governed and cured, and the poultices which I have in my hands in this book, and if it is in winter, and the pus is very hot, then it is necessary to put on tentes and wet cloths in wine and in lard.
et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit;	and if it is in this state, and the pus is charred, so it is necessary to put on wet cloths moistened with water and oil, or wine and oil frozen, every day, as we have said;
et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then remove the abscess and clean it up and treat the patient if necessary, as desired.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes:	And this is why one must investigate universally in treating abscesses:
or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	Or you have said how to go before starting the treatment of abscesses, and this is where the chapter begins.
des soros	of sorrows.
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	Where small abscesses come from the head, and are like threads, just as a spider's web, or like the wool of a goat, there is also much resemblance.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz;	There are some fatty ones and swellings as well that get worse with moisture just like boils.
et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	and some that are hard and stone-like to cut, with no doubt when the arteries are cut, and they do not cause any harm.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the marks on the neck are such that if you know how to use all the instruments called "entremoissoires", because of their shape they come after, what kind of thing it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, then they do it on top of the long one.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien;	And when the moisture is empty, if it scours without leaving anything to remain of that skin which contained the moisture, for it returns again when nothing is left.
puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens;	Then plunge cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment into it if present;
se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor;	If not, plunge it into water and cloth, and apply the wound until the next day;
et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And let those who are left behind sleep at night.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit;	And then resume the cotton, as before, on the second day, and the bandage, until you know it will not stay in place at night;
puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat the wound with ointment as it suits, until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc;	And if the abscesses are tight in not to be grasped, do it according to this shape, for a long time;
et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist;	And I shave all your hair, and the scab from every part, and place all your care to treat for the chest where it is.
et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if they cause contractions, do what I told you afterwards.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And do also thus with the abscess if it is pus-filled, and to cut it open and to cure as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And the size of the pus-filled abscess will be cut and drained if it is lighter, because there is little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme;	And if some of these abscesses or swellings are not due to moisture, and some that I have copied or extracted from the swellings of an old woman.
et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier;	and I found the abscess like a stone hard, sharp and white, that cannot break.
et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	and if any had been burned with it, one would have done the same wound as with a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe;	In other abscesses that come or swellings, whether they arise on the head of children and the roots of the ears, cut open so as to reach the lowest part, to make the bowels emerge;
et les cure si com il covient.	and the cure as it requires.
des scrophules	Des scrophules
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times abscesses occur in the neck, and under the armpits, and near the liver, and sometimes they appear in other places or at the joints, and are very painful, and often joined together one with another.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit;	And each ulcer is properly within its own coat, just as the navel and apertome of the head, as we have said;
et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	and the similarities to these ulcers are many.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are those that contain moisture, and those that are malignant, and they do not wish to obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde;	in which you see the good condition of the bone at the elbow, and is like the color of the body, mute on all sides, not irritated at any part nor by the nerves of the neck or artery nor in the canal, and is not deep.
si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief;	so it is fitting to copy it over, and scrape off the flesh from each part, and leave the two lips of the wound as if cut with knives, as we have said in apertomes of the head;
et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	And let the touch of fire command the patient to let his hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie;	And if you cut the vein or artery, and it does not stop bleeding, apply a plaster of vitriol to break it up, or some powders that will stop the blood, and bind the wound.
et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	and let it remain until the abscess is allayed and the wound is mollified, and begin to discharge.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses;	And when the blood has been drawn off, return to your work until you have completed it.
puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	then seek to know if there are any small swellings that will remain after you cut and lance.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement;	And if he has much blood in the neck of a scrofula, so that it cannot be copied there, but only tied with a strong double thread, and left to fall away with pain.
puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	Then use the dressing of old cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment, and then apply a cure.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	If you cover the whole cranium, it is advisable to assemble the two lips of the wound and now sew them, before any swelling remains from the great size of the skull.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	if it is advisable to treat at the root of the, and apply force, and sew as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure;	Those scrofulas that swell above, cut into whichever place they open and bleed.
et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption;	and cut it in such a way as is said before, in dependence, and then put in tenons with ointment and similar things, if it infects what remains of the infection.
et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and when the wound is well cleaned, apply ointment in jars, until it is cleansed.
de squinance	of inflammation
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge;	The ancient men spoke about the cutting of the throat;
mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	but I never saw anyone in our land do it, and this is the writing of their word.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee;	But for those who have been strangled, it is to be believed that the cutting of the throat known as "epiglottis" should be avoided;
et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	And do not help them by that, because all the veins and the swelling of the patient are at those who have had sharp wounds in the mouth, or throat, or two fingers.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the sickness is in the channel of the small part, it is necessary to cover the epiglote to escape the destruction that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige;	It is therefore necessary, when we wish to cut the epiglottis, that we cut it outside of three circles or four small cuts across, between the two circles or according to the quantity of the incision through the tissue, not in the cartilage;
et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	and those who have this condition are suitable for section of the epiglottis because there is no cartilage, and the vessels are long to enter.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil;	And if the masters are doubtful, then it is fitting to stretch the skin of the throat all the way down to the chin, then cut through the scarred spot until it comes out on the surface.
et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit;	and escape the vessels of blood, if you see any, and then strike at the superficial part, as we have said.
et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix;	and it is demonstrated by the section of the tongue of the chin which bursts forth from the jaw that is broken, and by the failure of the voice.
et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	and let the wound be covered with a piece.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige;	And when the hour is passed because of which one doubts strangulation, assemble both lips to the wound from above with the tongue so that the entire tooth may be taken out.
puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then administer medicines which make flesh swell, until it is well.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	But it should not be done until the throat is completely frozen, and the patient is judged to be dead, and the disease spreads.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort;	Therefore cut the epiglottis because the patient cannot swallow, and he breathes through the wound, and thus is kept from death.
et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee;	And the ancients ordered that the wound be left uncovered for as long as the malice of the disease has passed, and it has passed in three days or four days. And then they ordered to sew up the wound and treat it, until it was cured;
et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	And I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon;	I saw a young woman take out a knife, and she stuck it in her throat, and cut off part of her neck.
et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	and I was summoned to cure her, and I found her in the same state as dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I uncovered the wound, and I found the blood that had come out of it, and I realized that she hadn’t cut her vein or any other vein by chance only through the throat, and the blood came out through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee;	I was about to leave, and stitched the wound, and cured her so that she became healthy.
et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition;	and it happened to the young woman that she was red in the throat, and returned after her recovery.
por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	because of this I thought that there was no fear in the larynx.
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat.
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes;	This swelling is called "gullet hernia", and it's a large swelling the colour of a hazel nut, and it occurs greatly in women;
et est selonc II manieres:	And there are two ways:
naturez, et accidens;	Nature (cause) and accident (happenstance).
ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	Where there is no natural cause.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere;	And the accident is according to two ways, because one is like a lump or swelling, and the other is like an abscess that comes from an artery;
et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire:	and it causes fear, and it is not advisable to apply fire to burn with fever only in those who are small, and he examines and seeks at the surrounding area;
se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point;	if you find it as if there is no lump, and it does not cause pain in any way, if you cut it, as we cut the nose, and you show all its face, unless there is anything else.
et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And search well all of them, and the physician as it is required, until they are perfectly cured.
des nous	From us
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances;	There are many ways in which it happens, of which I will tell you all the similarities;
et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	and as for this is what I am going to say, the difference between not and wound.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture;	I say that when it is an abscess and fever remain, until the boiling is done, and it is completed with putrefaction;
adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	and then the fever and heat rest.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros;	With the wound there is no heat, fever, or pain, and it contains a sac, which is its own sack and resembles the color of the flesh, and begins to swell just as a jam does, and becomes larger.
et sont selonc II semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	and are according to two types, or wounds, or moisture, and much of color are like what I said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to the treatment of no one, that you examine and inquire first about all the instrument called "entremoissoire", as its form will arise or chapter that follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme;	And the method of examining abscesses is that you prick or moisten it more than what you find in the abscess, and twist your thumb a little bit until you know when the swelling has pierced the skin, so that this becomes according to the size of the abscess.
puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	then remove the middle part, and be careful that it does not splinter.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes;	If the abscess is moist or has dried up, then cut it in such a way that its color is like what I said about other abscesses.
et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout;	and if the middle part does not come to be moist after, know that it is fatty, so cut it in a cross, and take hold of it with pincers, and lightly scrape off each part, and wear a protective cloak where you feel it, until you bring out the wound clean with the needle.
et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	and if you cannot treat it well, then cut it to pieces so that it does not stay there.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois;	But if it stays, it will come back again many times;
et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if it stays for just a little while and the pain is not severe, then apply the wound with some corrosive powder or poultice, strap the wound tight, and put on soothing things like cauterized leather, and treat other treatments until he is healed.
et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	and if the pain is great, then cut off both cheeks of the wound, and treat the one who causes inflammation.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc;	and if the veins are swollen in opposition to this or something else, and you hasten and apply the new vinegar solution, break it into three parts, let it lie for two or three days, until the wound has stopped bleeding, and the inflammation subsides.
puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	then comes back to cover what is left behind where it has been forgotten now.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres:	Behold here are the forms of internal humors, and they are three kinds:
grans et moien et petit;	large and medium-sized and small;
et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres:	and in it are three quarters which are called "albares", and one which is called "brebe", and they come in three kinds:
grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule;	large, medium-sized, and small, for to encircle the abscesses of a fistula;
et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule;	and are also like the needles with which you cut the sources, and they are of yellow citron-iron, or iron, or silver, and move well those who are yellow, and are more suited for penetrating into the black pouch of a fistula;
et sont de III manieres:	And are of three kinds:
grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	Grans, moines, and small ones, according to the quantity of the size of the wounds.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci:	The forms of ulcers are like many similarities, as you can see here:
grans, moiens, et petis;	great, small, and medium;
et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi;	and if there are ulcers that have two hollows of three kinds also;
et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres;	and if there are ulcers that have three hollows, and are also of three kinds;
et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres;	and if there are ulcers that have two hollows and ulcers with only one hollow, and are of three kinds;
et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	and all these are necessary in their own turn.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf;	The head of these is cut off because they are pricked, and from such ones there are those who do not cut much more than from one side, where the skin burns, so that the vein or nerve does not bleed.
et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes;	And those who are inserted with foreign objects have the membranes returned in their hands, so that the patient does not lose them when opening abscesses.
et sont de III manieres:	and they are of three kinds:
grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois;	great, small, and medium, as you see.
et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus;	and do not use it more than in the joints, such as knees, arms, and elbows, and similar places.
et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	and at times another small instrument is made, resembling the skin of fistulas, according to this form, in order to stain blood:
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and put it in no place at all, for whoever has performed operations on the veins and arteries, and in no case returns to this great form.
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme;	Never do the breasts of some men swell when they start to be corrupted, until they resemble the breasts of a woman;
et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	and remain swollen and inflamed, and whoever wants to cure them, if it seems proper according to this form in this line from g to g:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then burns the fat, and applies medicine to the wound with charcoal, then brings together the two lips of the wound to the seam, and cures until it is healthy;
et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures;	and if the breast swells downward, and is swollen for its size as in women, then cuts through two seams on top, according to two similar incisions;
