de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.;	so that one is attached to the other at the end of each, so that the larger line contains the smaller according to this form from g to g;
puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then scrape the skin that is between the two lips, and extract the fat, and apply what we have said about clothing and powder, and what is necessary for the treatment, until he is healthy.
et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif;	and if he is not healthy, or the incision is not entirely made, because the patient does not want to rest, or due to the congealing of blood, so it is fitting that you fill the wound with wet cotton in a corrosive dressing;
et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	and let him wait until he has consumed the remaining and fat, then treat him until he is healthy.
des apostemes des asselles	Of abscesses from the arrows
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	Abscesses that come from under the arrows are hard swellings or have ribs, and when there is much moisture in them.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	These then that contain moisture should be cut according to this shape, from the line 5 to the line 8:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the entire bow that is in the abscess is empty, apply the wound with fine cloth, and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cloth, and treat with ointment as much as necessary until it heals.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess is like swellings of scrofula, treat it as we have said for cutting into swellings, and if the wound has an arrow sticking in it, apply cauterization as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	Of the cut of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme;	When the artery is cut, and the skin is burned which is above, if it brings many abscesses, and it happens just as often that it comes back in from the vein.
et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont;	And if the abscess is near the artery, so it is long within it.
et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement;	and when you feel it with your two hands, you will sense a disturbance.
et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans;	and when it is because of the vein, if there are red marks around.
et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	and this is madness to cover up the abscess, and especially when it is under the armpits and around the neck and in other areas, and it is very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc;	It is therefore necessary to abandon the iron treatment, and those who have head problems must also give it up, and for those with swelling of an artery, cut through the skin on a long bone.
puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte;	then cover the area around the neck with linen, and carefully expose the artery in the webbing, until it is uncovered.
puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples;	Then pour the wound with a needle from under the one, and pierce it on the other side, and tie the artery with two threads in 12 fingers, according to what I have taught you in extracting two arteries that are in the temples.
puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme;	Then point the arrow that is between the two threads of an inserted instrument until the space that there is, and release the abscess.
puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient;	Then apply a dressing on what hurts so much that the wound bleeds.
puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then treat this infection until it is healed.
et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit;	And if the abscess is by the size of the vein, so it is fitting that you dye with your hand what you can from the abscess onto the skin, then pour the needle from under the wound that you hold in your hand, and pierce it, and tie a double thread, so that you pull it from the other side.
puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil;	Then tie the bandage, just as I told you, or tied to one of the two parts with two fingers of the hand.
et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus;	and if you doubt that the thread will not be produced, tie an other needle to all of II threads below the bandage at the incision of the first needle, and tighten the threads in IV fingers.
puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez;	then cut the bandage so that the excess falls out, then cut the excess of the same measure and leave what is tied.
puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then put on the moist bandage in vinegar and oil, then apply treatments for tenements and ointments until he is healed.
des apostemes des ners	They are abscesses of the fingers
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	And abscesses come to the artery and vein, they come to the fingers when they are swollen, or by too much work, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor;	And this happens more often in the joints and in the toes where there are fractures, and it's an abscess, and its color resembles the flesh of a corpse, and is worse than other conditions with pain.
et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur;	And when they are constrained forcefully, then the patient feels pain, and it is not felt deeply in the body, but beneath the surface.
et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer:	And he is mute from every part, and does not move at all, neither forward nor backward, nor below or above, and one who is in a joint cannot be covered with iron:
par aventure i vanroit contraction;	in case he suddenly contracts.
et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	and those who are in the head or on the forehead, cover with gauze or a cloth.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine;	If the abscess is small, if he has nails, and you cut them at their root;
et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if it is large, if he has the abscess to open, and scorch, then the bone, and he sews the wound to the ribs, and the patient should be cured as long as he is healthy.
des grosses boces pendans	of great boils hanging down.
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros;	Nothing happens to the abdomen and no other part of the body except for this one, it is a sickness called "fungue" because of its resemblance to an abscess, and has subtle roots, and coarse bones;
et en i a de petis et de mout grans;	and in it are small ones as well as large ones;
et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	And I saw a man who had two large abscesses in his abdomen which were very similar to fungi and there was no other difference and they were white and had small roots and had been broken open and were rotting due to moisture.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine;	I copied them and found that one weighed 18 ounces and the other 6 ounces, and the wound from the incision was such that if you look closely, the patient is moist, and the color of the armpit is white and moist with subtle roots;
si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	If they prick at the base of their nose, hold your eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer;	For when cutting comes, there are often great flows of blood, and if you do not wait, then quickly apply the cautery.
et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors;	And if you see the patient experiencing fear and anxiety from the incision of the iron, prick the pit on the back well done, and tie the artery as we have said, and let it remain two days.
et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail;	and then restrain it, and do not cease to tighten the pit on the back until he pricks the artery, and pierces through with it, feeling its work.
et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne;	and if the roots are large, then fear yourself when cutting at the same time for the abdomen, but you can well cut off half of it, and then cautery so that it does not return.
puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	Now cure the wound, and make sure that you do not cover the place where the blood flows red and poor in sense and from the eye.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	It's an enchanted wound, and I came to this cure for chancres afterwards.
quant li boude ist fuer	When the boil is formed.
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit;	If the appearance of a boil comes from cautery to a wound or a laceration of sinew, and is on the belly with some boils, as happens in other routures, or when blood cuts through veins or arteries according to what is before, or from windiness.
et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	and if it is from the wound of sinew and through the boil, and the color of the abscess resembles the color of the flesh, and there is little pain and a large opening with various issues.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is from the intestine, then it is more diverse, and when you press on both sides so it returns, and then comes back, and by chance, if it has scarred, and becomes larger at the entrance of the bath and for great effort.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie;	And if it is due to moisture, it's a light thing, and opens well when you press with your hand, do not constrain it.
et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit;	and if it's for pain relief, then open with these signs of a large and hard abscess, and stitch according to its size.
et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	and if it's for ventilation, then if the patient is soft at the chest, and the wounds are examined so that you look at whether the appearance of the wound is due to the blood of the artery, or the vein, or ventilation.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	If it's necessary to leave the treatment.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	Because there is doubt and fear, as I have told you in the chapter of apostemes for the artery and vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude;	and if the appearance is due to the intestine or the stomach, then it is fitting that you instruct the patient to tighten their belly, and extend themselves straight, and stitch all around the wound.
puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine;	then command the patient to lie on their back between your hands, then go around the injured area that you marked, and stitch half of the abscess above with all the long stitches.
puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz;	Then tie him to a strong thread, or a cord of very thick silk firmly, and make sure the wound is closed.
puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine;	Then spread half of the incised area over the wound and put a poultice or an application on it.
se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre;	If you find the thing tied to the wound has been removed, then put an intestinal poultice outside of the belly.
et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit;	and if you find the wound, put it in its original place and take away the surrounding swelling.
et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier;	and if the artery causes harm or pain, go calmly around it, then return to your work and take out two arrows, and put two strong threads in them, and put the two arrows back in the place where you made them pierced.
puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi;	Then strain the abscess four levs above the arrowheads, and if you see it, pull out the arrowheads, and let the wound heal as long as it will, and chip away at dead flesh by itself;
ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit;	If you cut it when it is slightly open and has begun to heal, then treat the one that needs it, and follow what we have said;
et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	and drain the blood or the moisture that you find, then treat the wound with what it needs, and close the wound.
dou chancre	A skin sore
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer;	We have said in the division regarding similar sores and how one must treat with medicine, and how one must avoid using iron treatment;
et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement;	and say the sore inflames in the marrow, and take great care with treatment, and the ancients said that when sores are on a person where they can be scraped off like a sore on the nipple, or in the groin, and similar places, and it should all be removed at the beginning;
et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner;	And when he is great and old, so it does not suit that you approach him, because I have never seen a sicker man;
ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	None of them have ever been saved in front of me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire;	And for the ulcers when he is in his own bed or can be taken out, as we have said, it is that you do not purgate the sick man of black bile at all.
puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide I boin leu por faire l’ovraige;	Then make him healthy if he shows signs of overeating, and afterwards make the sick man lie down to work on the ulcer.
puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier;	Then throw out your ulcers or cankers, and scrape the head of all parts, and leave nothing behind in the bone.
et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	And let the blood flow freely, and eagerly examine well by hand or by anything, and if it causes a counteraction of the incision of an artery or vein, then cautery as long as there is no bleeding.
puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then instruct the physician to proceed with another remedy until he is healed.
de ydropisie	Of dropsy (or edema).
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer:	We have previously discussed the symptoms of dropsy, and in what way the assembly of water is made, and the signs of each one, and the remedy that is done with medicine, and which one is healed by iron.
si est eclites soulement;	if it is swollen only;
et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances:	and one should not touch iron in these two similarities:
c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose;	that is to say, tympanites and yposarches, because it is a mortal thing;
donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses;	Therefore when treating this similarity of dropsy called "eclites" which the physician does not profit from, and the patient is weak or has another illness besides dropsy, as if they have stomach issues and similar symptoms;
si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance;	If you do not touch with iron, because there is doubt;
et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer:	and if you see a patient of great virtue, and he has only dropsy alone, and he is neither too thin nor too tall, then do thus operate:
lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	lift the patient upright over your hands, and let the ministers press the abdomen towards the lowest part of the foot, then take the spatula with a spike according to this shape:
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And let them pluck from two parts.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier;	with a point, and it should not be so deeply inserted that it can come into the intestine when you insert it, and it cannot be withdrawn.
puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines:	then look to see if the dropsy is stuck near the intestines:
si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil;	If you must break open the abscess, do it on the third day because on the fourth day the poison will go deeper into the bone.
et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois;	and if there is a drop of pus on account of liver disease, break open on the left side of the abscess on the fourth day.
et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu;	and if it is caused by the muscle, on the right side, and you cannot tolerate that the patient lies upon the wound so that the superfluities do not run to the weak part of him;
puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor;	then pierce all the skin with the instrument, and pull it out, and raise your hand to the whole strip of skin between the skin and the sac so that when you scrape off as much as an acorn or less.
puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	then pierce the sac so that the strip of skin comes back to its place, and this is the mark of the water, then pull out this instrument from which it is the shape:
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus;	And it seems like a silver chain bound tightly, and is made of iron or arrows light, and in the lower part there are small holes.
et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus;	and on the other side, three more holes.
et II d’autre part, et I d’autre;	and two on this side, and one on that side.
et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	and the nails are cut like a reed, and this is the shape of the incision that the scribes write on the reed:
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument;	on the top is the alhemel, so that when the instrument comes to the water, it now goes up on the instrument;
vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort;	now you should empty one-third or more of the blood, because if you take away more than is necessary at this hour, by chance the patient may die from the resolution of their spirit with the arm, or they will faint, or death will approach.
mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz;	but according to the amount of his virtue, and according to what the disposition of his virtue signifies in the sick person, and his feet;
puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere;	then hold the instrument and retain the water, and it is now retained by the membrane which stops the pus that is on the surface of the ulcer, as I said, so pierce according to this manner;
puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit;	then resume the instrument another day, if you see the sick person suffering from it, and take a small quantity of water;
fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	do this day, and beware not to become foolish until there is but a small quantity of water left.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre;	and if you doubt the patient, and take much water from him, if the remedy of burial or hot salt is used, by sweating or bath, and in the sun, and if they drink.
et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	and the healer of medicine desiccates as much as it is able to heal, and cauters on the stomach and on the liver and on the spleen after extracting the water, just as I said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	of the stoning of the genitals
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	There is never a child born without some kind of defect in the genitals, or if there are defects, they are small, or it is not in its proper place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	If you want to proceed quickly so that he can pierce all the small spots very subtle according to this form:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet;	then put or pierce a subtle bone from the bottom, and tie it in this way for three days or four, and when he wants to make urine, then open the cleft, and let him urinate, and then set him.
et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	and in case it does not come out at all, because the urine that comes is not allowed to be closed.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	If a broken bone is of the foot, then it should be treated with poultice made from broken bone, as we have said, if it swells.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut;	Those who do not have the puncture in their own flesh are blackened, because no one is born who has a puncture at the head of the penis, because they cannot urinate before lifting their penis up.
et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	and they cannot be cured because the matter cannot come to the marrow, and this is a great sickness.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient;	And the manner of treating it is that the patient lies on his back, put a stick through the head and cut as wide as the width of a grain of barley, so that the punctured piece comes out, as it seems to be.
et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	and be careful not to increase the bleeding that often comes out, and if it does, stop the blood flow and treat the wound until it is fully healed.
des pustules de la verge	of swellings on the penis.
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide;	Often there comes an abcess on the vein, and it is an ugly appearance.
et en i a malignes et non malignes;	and some are malignant and others not so much.
si covient que tu les preignes a I oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien;	If it is necessary to press them at one time subtle, and strike all around, then put cotton moistened in Egyptian salve.
puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	then the ointment is applied diligently until it is pure.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	And if the bath is malignant, of foul color and odor, it is fitting that you apply cautery.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier;	When you have struck it, and the skin is torn when cutting, with part of it inside the flesh and part outside, if necessary, then remove the part that is inside first.
et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	and if it is sewn, the ointment.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion;	For when you cure the entire thing together, if not assured that the cut of the vein is perceived, and blackness and corruption come to the vein and the wound.
si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	When it is appropriate to shave everything that is black and rotten, then put a plaster made of honey and flour on the skin, which is made from pomace of grapes and figs, and apply other remedies until they are healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	If they come with blood, then administer lunar cauterization according to this form:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble:	Fire cautery helps in both good and bad conditions:
c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption;	which is to say, when there is decay or corruption.
et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi;	and if the root of the twig is corrupted and withdrawn, it is advisable to insert a wooden dowel into the opening and let the patient urinate.
et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars;	and when the hair grows back to the head of the twig where those who have not been circumcised have wounds or abscesses, it is advisable then that you burn it with a needle instrument, until the ties are loosened and the root of the twig is released from all parts.
et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil;	And if this is a grievous injury to be treated with cautery, then it is fitting that you burn at the spot on the cheek of the penis and around the foreskin.
puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	Then serve it up gently between two and one inch, with some fine linen soaked in cold water, so that he does not burn himself.
de la circoncision	About circumcision.
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies;	Circumcision is no less a hindrance to continued bleeding as other wounds;
toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	all the way that we have done this work with our own will and properly for children, since it is to their best interest and easiest treatment.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	The ancients did not speak of circumcision for their children, because they did not use it in their law, and we have only what we have acquired by experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor I dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule;	For I have wanted the greatest part of the masters and doctors who performed circumcisions in the past, especially those with great experience and skill, as well as those new to it.
si fuioit li keurs car il i a II toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	If it is cold outside because there are two full moons, and by chance if someone is struck above and does not move below.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre;	or the wound heals over again and there is great pain, and with the mutilation that is not assuredly fixed to the point of the member;
et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	and to the inflammation of an ungainly wound by chance the iron escapes and the wound heals, and many times it is born again so that it has no need of further healing I have wanted.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	From the purification which is done with forces along the entire length of thread I have found the good fortune of the experiment, for the forces cut just as well above as below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens;	For when you press your hand, the nail grows equally in all parts if it is cut short in one place.
mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir;	but that the thread is tightly drawn within the skin;
et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	and if the manner of the first operation is such that you make the child think it, if he understands, then only tie the thread around the stick so tightly, and just let it rest in all the ways possible.
puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens;	Now hold the wound between your hands straight out, and set back the strength between your hands or under your feet so that the children do not see them, nor any of the swellings;
puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens;	Then put your hand on the vein and blow or press it, and pull it up until the head of the vein is drawn out;
puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien;	Then cleanse it well of the filth that is assembled around it, then tie the vein with a thread of two strands, and then tie it under one stitch to another stitch;
et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge;	and hold two stitches apart with the second tie to the pouch and the point, and cut between the two stitches, then draw the vein hastily up to the head of the vein;
puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres;	then let the blood flow slowly at first, for it is the mothers;
et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Instruct the patient to put powder on it and cover it with that same powder; and drizzle glue made from a half cup of melted fat of a swan cooked in vinegar rose, mixed with good oil and fresh rose petals, and let him lie on it till the next day, and the healer will treat with another treatment until he is healed.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste:	When applying ointment to a wound if it happens that:
li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	when the two sides of a wound are tied together and stitched, and also when the stitches are as thick as the equal part of an arm.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision;	when the pus inside the wound escapes from the incision;
donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme;	then it is necessary to extend it on your side, in such a way that the pus makes an abscess.
et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	and let the cut equal, and if you cannot hold fast to your joint, then take tongs, and then cut.
Et s’il trespassent III jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement;	And if it swells for three days, and that which is below the vein has inflamed, then let it be left until the abscesses on the skin are calmed, and the scorching is done lightly.
si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	If you cut it as you move, and keep away from the vein part, it will not do harm.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point;	Therefore treat the swelling pain with powder, as we have said or treated with powders, and if you cut too severely over the measure, it will go up above, and do no harm.
cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore cure him then, as we have said, until he is healed.
dou retenement de l’urine	A retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division;	The retention of urine is due to stone or ice congealing in it, or a bowel obstruction, or a blockage from a tumor, or similar things that we have mentioned in the division.
et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz;	and if the urine is not flowing, and you see that the retention is due to a stone lying in the neck of the bladder, it is advisable for the patient to be laid on his knees.
et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet;	and the knees are placed on the back, and he extends his belly from the upper part of the back, and restrains the patient so that he cannot move.
et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e;	and thus the neck of the bladder is constrained to express the stone above, because the urine is flowing out.
et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme:	and if she does not come, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then it is fitting that you administer extraction to all the instruments called "siringue", because there is a form:
et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil;	and let it be of subtle silver thread, like the feathers of a bird;
et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	and let the bandage be half an inch long and be subtle at the head.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue;	And the manner of the issue of urine if it happens that you take a double thread, and tie one pound of wool or linen to the head, and pour the head into the "siringue";
et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede;	and cut off the superfluousness of the linen and pour it just onto the head of the "siringue", then anoint the "siringue" with oil or butter and rue, and place the patient on the bed, and let the bladder and the urethra be moistened with watered-down oil and olive oil.
puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude;	Then put the ligature more lightly on the vein, until it comes to the root of the vein, then double the vein above over the wound;
puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors;	Then pour the ligature before it gets to the bladder, and feel the patient's pain coming until it gets to the empty place, and that is not done according to this order because of the twisting where it should be going.
puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine;	Then pull the thread all along the vein little by little, and the urine follows the vein, then extract it, and make the urine flow.
et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	and re-pour the ligature until the bladder is empty, and adjust the patient's pain.
des maladies de la vessie	About bladder diseases
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When scorches or blood comes into the bladder, or when putrefaction is assembled, and you see water and medicine distilled there, then do all the instruments called "clepsedre", and it's like this:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus:	It is closed, and if there are three punctures:
II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois;	I d' une partie et i d'autre si com tu vois;
et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est;	And the left hand because that is where the cutting of the medicated salve will numb well the joint, if we can treat the moisture, and blow as needed when necessary.
et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens;	and when you see getting your medicine into the vessel, put a cork stopper in the moisture, and pull out as much as possible;
si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens;	if you pull out the moisture from the cork, and then seal it tightly again;
si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira;	so the moisture will enter again, and come into the vessel now, so that the patient can feel it;
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie:	and this is the form of the subtle bladder castor oil, by which the vessel is castored;
si est ci:	If so:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut;	And is of silver or arrows, and the head is higher;
et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet;	and below at the joint where the ligaments come loose;
puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu;	then take a sheep skin and put the moisture that you see clotting on it, then tie between the two shoulders a strong double thread, and heat it over the fire;
puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie;	then pour the head into the clots in the vein, then strain your hand on the skin until all the moisture is extracted from it, so that the patient feels the juice coming to the vein;
et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor;	and if you don’t have the skin, take a piece of parchment and make a circle on it, and then pierce it all around;
puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument;	Then put in the bottle, fill it strongly with these wounds, then assemble the circle as we assemble the nail, and put inside what you see of oil and moisture and water, and tie it up in the instrument.
et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	and do it as you did with the bladder, of pressing to your hand until the moisture comes to the bladder.
de la piere	of the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines;	We have said in the division of stones and the extraction of assembles of medicines;
et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille;	and have said the difference between the stone which is encased in iron and all the signs, and in which stone one must perform cutting.
et en la vessie, et en la verge;	and in the bladder, and in the penis;
et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	and I will tell you about it clearly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit;	I say that the stones which are imprisoned in the bladder occur more often in children, and this is a sign that they have eaten an overabundance of bile in their subtlety.
et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist;	and when I open the stone, and irritate the patient's penis, and he urinates many times, and then becomes emaciated;
et a mout de ces saut li fondemens;	and at a great cost of these stones, the foundations are undermined;
et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont IIII ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece;	and healing in children occurs until they are 4 years old, and is very painful in the elderly, and is like joint pain that occurs between joints and old age;
et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	and the cure is lighter for those who have a large stone than for those who have a small one.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to treatment, it is necessary first to clean the patient with a cloth, in order to treat all the blood that has accumulated inside.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For this does not come up when seeking a stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut;	Take the patient by the hands and feet, and draw them out and move downwards, so that the knee descends to the bottom of the bladder, and does not go up again at all.
puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval;	Then make the patient sit between your hands prepared, and let his hands be below his knees, so that the bladder is all inclining downwards.
puis la quier et la touche dedens;	Then look at it and touch inside;
se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	If you feel the stone in the space, then hasten now to cut on the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis;	And if it does not flow onto the toucher of all, so that thy right index finger is anointed with oil from the left hand, then either the patient has fever or thy left hand.
et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie;	And let the vessel stand still in its foundation, and choose a stone, and when you feel it at your groin, if it has set up against the neck of the bladder;
puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	then press it onto your groin, and let the vessel go away from where you see cutting.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille;	And instruct the minister to press the bladder with his hand, and he commands that he extend his right hand upwards towards the necks in the groin area, and with his left hand, pull out the skin beneath the necks in the part where one makes the incision;
puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	then put the spatulate instrument on cutting, so that it is the form:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre;	And put it between those who are between the necks and the foundation, neither in the middle but alongside the left side of the bladder;
et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans;	And it shall be straight above the stone, and your shoulders should be placed at the neck or chest, and if the size of the stone is wide in front, then let the length of the passage according to the quantity of the stone, not too much.
par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail;	In case the pressure, if the shoulders are on or at the chest, it will suddenly fall in place.
et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges:	And see where there is a stone or an angle, and margin;
si est griés a issir;	if it is grated to come out.
et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	and if there is something on top that resembles a glitter, and shines, with a light issue.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant;	Therefore, if it has an angle and margin, make the incision larger;
et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe;	And if she does not jump, so it is advisable to strangle at the nails which are just like a file on the head, in order to strain the bone if it will not heal.
ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief;	or you pour drink some of the subtle curved instrument at the head;
et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole;	and if you cannot put it in like that, so enlarge the wound to let pus out, and if there is no separation, then strangle with vinegar.
et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	and if there is more than one stone, so pour first the largest on the belly of the bladder, then cut it up, then pull it out, and the smaller ones afterwards if there are more.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if it is very large, then you should soak it, and make a larger wound.
Car II choses avienent au malaide:	Because two things happen to the patient:
ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder;	He dies, or urine comes out afterwards because he cannot sew.
mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces;	but force yourself to cut, or to debilitate with nails, until you cut it by pieces.
et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut;	and when you have completed your work, apply the plaster of onion, aloes and dragon's blood, and bind it, and put above it a damp cloth in oil and wine, or in oil and rosewater and cold water, to soothe the abscess.
puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	then revive the patient on his neck, and do not release the bandage until the fourth day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you untie it, so that the limb is moistened with oil and water, then treat him with ointment of defernion and ointment of basilicon until he is cured.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine:	And if an abscess comes to the wound and causes corruption and congelation of blood in the bladder, and holds back the urine, which is known in this manner so that without its escape with the urine:
boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit;	Put a dressing on the wound, and extract the blood, for if it remains there, the bowels will be corrupted, and the flesh will rot;
puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then lift the wound with cool water and clean cloth, and apply the aid in all ways as you know, until it is healed.
et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	It is fitting that all the remedies you treat for him should bind both knees and assemble the medicines upon him.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir;	And if the stone is small, and it is in contact with a bone, and fixed there, and the urine cannot come out;
si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	So if the treatment you mention is repeated many times, then we are excused from this operation.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have already proven this thus.
Pren I foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a III angles fichiees en I tison:	Before you begin to cut with iron, according to this form and so that it is at three angles fixed in one piece:
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie;	Now take the file and put it on the inside of the bowels below the stone; so that she cannot come again to the bladder.
puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere;	Then pour a lighter wood into the bowels slightly, so that it may reach the stone.
et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part;	And turn the wood slightly on your hand towards the stone little by little, so that you can pierce the stone from the other side.
si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	If it comes to that the urine, then press your hand on the one that is remaining stuck to the stone which is inside the bowels.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides;	If it breaks apart and escapes with the urine, and heals the patient.
et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie;	And if you cannot do this for any reason that hinders it, tie the file below the stone and the other above, then make the bowels straight to the stone between the two ligatures, then extract for them, loosen the ligature, and clean with a congealed salve the wound.
et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and heal the patient completely.
de la piere des femmes	About the stone of women
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses:	There is often a stone in the uterus of women, and if it occurs once, then the cure is painful, and they are defended for three things:
l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge;	one thing is that perhaps the woman is chaste;
et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	and the second thing is that one cannot find a woman who is knowledgeable about shaving, especially when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains;	And the third thing is that perhaps one cannot find a woman who is knowledgeable in this art of hands.
et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil;	and the fourth thing is that the stone in a woman's uterus is more hidden than the stone in a man's body, because it often requires a deeper incision, and great fear arises from this. And if you need to do this, then it is advisable to take a shave well knowing, and at painful cost, and if you don't find one, do not choose a subtle shave.
et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere;	and he presents a wise remedy for the life of women, or a woman who knows a part of the art, and he commands that she do what you command of the inquiry of the stone;
et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge:	and examine very well whether the woman is a virgin:
adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere;	then it is fitting to pour some water or earth into the hole and seek the stone;
et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	and if she finds it, then she must constrain the thing under her hand, and he commands that she pour her remedy or with the sick person, and wants and presses his left hand upon the bladder forme.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse;	and if she finds it, then it is fitting that she move it from stone to stone of the entrance of the bladder until it comes out to the root of the thigh;
puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie;	Puis cover up the stone at its root on the lower thigh where it meets the middle, and so that there is movement in that part; and feel the stone in that area.
et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite;	and do not move his two fingers above or below the stone; and let them be tied to the first little joint.
puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont:	then pour a draught of water into the joint, if you feel the stone so far down the wound that it may come out further, and see that many kinds of stones are:
c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	that is to say, small and large, sharp and smooth, long and rounded, and which have holes.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	If you know the signs to recognize the outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	and if they do not swell, then he puts on the patient a piece of glass broken, and holds it for an hour until they are stained with blood;
puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre;	Then return to your work, until the pain is overcome, and you have taken up the instruments that I told you in the extraction of stones for people to help you with their work.
et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide;	and if they do not swell and it is an artery that has been struck, put powder on the limb and apply the straining mixture of poultices and bandages, and do not attempt again, let the wound alone, lest the patient die.
puis cure la plaie.	then treat the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the wound is cooled down and the pulse returns, then return to your work, until the pain subsides.
de hernie carnouse	of a hernia in the groin
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef;	Rice water is nothing but an assembly of moisture or white pus that forms below the knee, where it contains the yolk.
et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit I autre oef;	and is called "pus", and it is not properly contained in the yolk itself, unless one believes it to be another egg.
et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit;	and this is the skin around the vein between the white tissue which we have mentioned;
et ceu n’avient se poc non.	and this does not happen.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this water ram is due to weakness that comes to the joints, and it spreads out that material.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors:	And no time comes if it happens from percussing on the veins, and this moisture is so red with many colors:
ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus;	or it's pale declining to yellow, or without red, or black, or white, and this happens more.
et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	and these are the signs of this assembly, because if she is white and swollen like we have said, it means that the abscesses return, as long as they are like an egg, and do not open the veins, for there is moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef;	And if there is moisture in the own skin, then it means the abscesses return with a part of the egg, and because of that one thinks it's another egg.
et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien;	and if the moisture is between the skin of the joints and the white cartilage, he feels well;
donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	then when you see that knowing the color of the moisture, it is always on the inner quadrature, because the form is thus before.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	Therefore those who come after the surrounding area judge what is inside.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors;	And when we cure with iron, it is fitting that the patient be made healthy according to our power and the replenishment of his body.
puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz;	then he covers him with a cloak on his back, on one high thing, and places upon him much cloth.
puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions;	then he lies on his left side, and instructs the minister to lie on his right, and extends the rod to one of the two joints on either side of the joint.
puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir;	Take the spatula and pour the liquid on it, and strike the skin of the joints from your long joint to your little finger, and make your cut straight in devising the skin of the joints just up to a smooth white space, and scratch subtly according to the power.
puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont;	Then pierce the smooth space of the water into the large puncture, and extract all the water, and then put on your [appliances], and look at the space above.
et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement;	and do not touch the skin of the joints, but only the smooth space itself;
cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue;	cut all or in pieces, the same way on the chest of him, so that if you do not cut well, the blood will return;
et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac;	and if the blood escapes to your over, then return it to its place when you have completed the work on the smooth space;
puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Afterwards, gather the two leaves of wood from the knife to a costume, then heal as you would other wounds, until it is well.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc;	And if you find the ulcer of corruption from another disease, it is fitting to tie the vessels that are suspended above, in doubt about the decomposition of blood;
puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	then tie off the vessel to all that is suspended above, and extract the ulcer, and heal as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices;	And if an abscess is assembled in two parts, so that they are like two twigs;
si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset;	so tie the other part in the same way as you did the first one, then wipe off the blood, and put a fresh dressing made of moist linen in olive oil.
et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	and place another type of cloth soft and moist in wine and oil, and put on the two wounds, and cover them with double-draped cloths, and tie it up according to this form:
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil;	Then take two cloths, and fill them with wool filling in the same shape and assemble them by sewing in the neckline of breeches, and one of the shoulders presses on the lower back just to the top, and the other at the part of the joint.
et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier;	and the other two shoulders are placed on top of the two angles, and all assembled together the stricture in the bow of the breeches.
et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers;	and at no time is this remedy of cautery used in place of iron, and that you prick a fine caulderic cautery, and cut the skin of the wounds, and heat it as we have said, so that the white sap contained in the water is uncovered.
si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	If you take fire cautery according to this form, and pierce it at that spot with awl-like instruments, and scorch it with this subtle cautery sharp:
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout;	And cut in all the ways that you can, as long as you mark it.
et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef;	and keep the fire from touching the eye;
et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve;	and know that this work is more saving.
et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille;	and beware of complications from blood and be cautious about the wounds that come with it.
et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	and if no harm is done to you, or an abscess forms or complications from blood, or any other thing, then treat what causes you harm according to what has been said.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit;	And if the patient is fearful and does not want to wait for this work because of its horrible nature, so perform a perforation, as I told you, and it is that when you are certain by the meanings we have said that rainwater is laid up, then seat the patient on the bed lifted high.
pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors;	cut into the abscess in the lower part and to the entire wide surface.
et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer;	and so make the incision large enough that all the liquid can run out;
puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee;	then put cotton on the wound, bind it, and let it drain the remaining liquid, then cure until the wound is healed;
et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant;	and if the pouched cloth does not allow the liquid to drain from the opening of the wound, it is necessary to put a needle or the instrument used to treat the dropsy, because its shape is as before;
et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	and when the wound is large, and you see that the fluid returns, and it is assembled after six months or more, and as it is assembled, just like before, and so will pass the patient's days.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscesses of the throat.
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse;	You observe that in the section of this branch there is fear of more deaths, for which it seems to be worth not leaving.
et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	and I will tell you the work and the similarities of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions;	I say then that many abscesses come out of wounds, and similarly some congeal.
et c’est par mout de cas.	and this is by a great number of cases.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion;	It means that this is caused by the superfluity of sour and bitter, which is spread to the congeals, or by percussion.
et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors;	And it is the color of the abscess according to the color of the body;
et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief;	and there is no pain and it is an abscess that causes grief;
et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	and by chance there is an abscess that is grievous and painful, and of foul color, and at times comes from nowhere in the artery, or swells with vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois;	When it is not from the artery, if it is known by the arrangement of the abscess hot, when you press it with your two fingers;
et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	and it should not be touched at all.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars;	That which is swollen from the vein is known by its arrangement at the expression of gentle pressure with the two fingers, and can be recognized well on this appearance, and on other swellings;
et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	And so instruct the patient to strike the pulse of the wrist, then look to the top, and expose the vein behind white skin, and release the suspension from all parts of the vein.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope;	If the vein is already swollen with these new marks, then it is advisable to treat the vein and strike.
et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	and if it is swollen in the skin, or in that which is within the vessels, it is advisable to release all of that vein and strike round about.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the birth of the scar is behind him, so that you copy it all, and remove the wound, just as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your operations are completed, apply the wound of flaxen cloth moistened in rose oil and wine, then treat another patient until he is healthy.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscesses of the throat.
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait;	This is an abscess swollen with pus similar to that of the bubonic plague, with softening of the lymph nodes, and the patient complains greatly when it begins to open.
et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	and the treatment of this disease is as painful as before, and we will tell you about it, according to what the ancients have done.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment;	It is necessary that you make the patient sit on the elevated seat; then lower him onto the couch suspended by the head down to your two feet, all the surrounding furniture being moved away from the side, and the linens stretched out flat.
puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples;	Then cut with the spatula, cutting deep through to the bones, until all is uncovered, and then scrape from each side, as we have said when extracting arteries that are in the temples.
puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief;	Then prick with an needle where the artery is twice, and tie it to the first place where the vein came in, and tie it straight to the other side.
puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues;	Then cut across directly, according to the length of the body, and draw out the corrupted moistures.
puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions;	Then treat the wound as you do with others or burn it with boiling water, so that no one of those comes to nourish it.
