car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz;	But this does not come of anything evil, and if it comes at all, the vessels will be present, so it is best to treat all the vessels.
si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	so that the vessels do not lose their nourishment through the incision of the vessels, and drying up, they cannot be helped.
de la routure dou syfac	From the work of the cauterization
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions;	The dangers of this operation are such that they come from the separation where it occurs, or the extension above the abdomen in the region of the angles, because the intestines descend from that rupture to one of the vessels;
et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes:	and this rupture is in the separation or extension of it, and come these two kinds of movement from a multitude of causes:
ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses;	Out of pain from the strike, or a fall, or a burning, or the raising of a grievous weight, and by similar things;
et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement;	and the signs when it is a slow extension of the joint, so that it occurs little by little, over a long time, and does not come suddenly.
et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	and the abscesses are equal in size up to the tip, because the extension presses on the intestine.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the signs are when it is from the cauterization that they make a sudden onset of pain at the beginning, and there are various appearances of the abscesses under the skin close to, because it comes from the intestine and the body through the cauterization.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And never again take out the intestines with the ribs, and retain them in place, and make the patient suffer great pain, especially when they are pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these iron cauterizations because it is painful.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir;	And the manner of treatment is that you instruct the patient to bring the intestine into his hand inside the wound, if it can be returned.
puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes;	then take a bow on top of his neck between your hands, and lift the joints;
puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc;	Then bind the heart on top, and cut all the skin from the joints to the long.
puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir;	Then pour into the liver of the stomach, a certain number of stitches according to what you have need for to open the wound, and so that they can come out.
puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars;	Then scorch the skin beneath the joints, until the white skin underneath is exposed from all parts.
puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac;	Then pour your index finger into the space where the joint is, in the space between the skin of the joint, beneath the white skin underneath the skin of the foot, and beneath the second skin, and depart from the back of the foot, and beneath the second skin.
et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille;	And then move your right hand into the space of the joints, and let the white skin be above your left hand, and lift the foot to all the skin from the waist upwards.
et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement;	and instruct the minister to stretch the head upwards, and release those who are standing behind the binding;
et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz;	and take from your two fingers whether it has caught the intestine which is twisted or yellowish in color, and if you find nothing, then pour the fluid into the belly.
puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions;	then take an awl or a thread that has been made of three big fibers, and pour the fluid into its posterior part where it is yellowish.
aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz;	after the size, then cut the threads that appear in the fibers, until there are four fibers;
puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars;	then assemble them one on top of the other in the shape of a cross, and tie the yellowish fluid, which we have said is in the posterior part of the skin, with a strong bond made of two parts;
puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne;	Then you should wrap the joints of the fingers, and they form two parts, so that no lord who nurses them can enter your body, unless some poison comes out.
et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi;	and tie it off directly according to the first joint, with two fingers of that size, and after those two joints leave space below where the kidneys are in the large body of a dog.
et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte;	and after all that according to the circumference that the joint holds;
puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant;	then strike in the part that is under the skin of the joints, where there are no scars, and the bowels, as we have said before;
puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	then apply a moistened flannel in oil, and put it on the wounds, and tie up the joint that we have said.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And at some point, it is cautered with white styptic that we have said, after the incision, by doubt of its decrement of blood.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui;	This happens often, and let the ligature remain as long as it clings to him;
et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece;	and if it does not come to the chair, then let it be soaked in hot water, and put on what we have said, until it clings.
puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	then treat the wound with another remedy, until it is fully healed.
de hernie carnouse	of a hernia in the groin
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this case, I have never seen anyone who dared to do the cure with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz;	And the old people said that it is made just like the nail which joins together the splinter of wood, in such a manner that you tie the cloth around, after cutting above lightly towards the lower part;
puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient;	then cut within it, and treat the abscess that forms, until the cloth falls off;
et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat it just as we have said, until he is fully healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus;	There is no occurrence of a rupture on an artery, as we have said, and it opens the veins.
et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres;	and do not draw anything from the intestines because of the cold, and if you draw something, it's a small thing, and all these hours.
et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent;	and if it remains too long in that place, so that he believes the wound or is constipated, until the intestines come out.
et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert;	and this happens because of the extension of which is in the artery, as we have said, for it is stretched, then softened, and inflates the veins and opens them.
et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit;	and the cure is by cautery, as we have said before.
et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere:	and never is cured with iron in this manner.
et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois;	And he instructs the patient to sit up straight between his hands, then cut him loose from the bandage inflated with fluff according to the amount of three dollars;
et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac;	and then pull out the strap that is under the skin which adheres, and take away the raw flesh from where it adheres to the flesh.
et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre;	and press them to the bottom of the abdomen, then cut the two layers that are near the flesh above the raw flesh on the head of the wound, and cut both.
puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines;	then pull out the raw flesh from the wound, and do not cover it with anything nor extend the gauze or any other thing, as I told you in the treatment of the splinter in the intestines.
puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	then treat by the treatment of wounds.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When you cut the hairs, if they sting and heal the wound, so that it becomes healthy.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The scalp is constricted and has no appearance in the incision; the cautery is more moist in this place, and closer to health.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the skin of the joints.
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir;	Many times are softened the skin of the joints in some men, because those who are inside are softened and become like milk to see;
et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil;	and it is necessary when one wants to cure him, that you make the patient sit on his back, and he strikes the softened skin on the natural skin;
puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a III costures ou IIII fermement;	then gather the two lips to a suture, and if you see, cut first at three layers of the softened skin or four firmly;
puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	then strike between the sutures, and the cure is done as with other wounds, until he is healed and the thread comes out.
dou chastrement	Letting loose from fire
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre;	Which armor is prescribed in our law, and for this reason I prefer not to speak of it in this book;
et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres:	And it is necessary to do this for two reasons:
dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure;	because one of them is that the surgeons know how to answer when they will be asked, and also know what the cure is;
et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	and the other, because we have often had to castrate certain animals in order to help us, such as oxen and sheep and goats and other animals.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres:	I say therefore that castrations are done according to two manners:
ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	or by atrition, or by cutting.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant;	In the one we do by attrition, we sit them in hot water as best as can be, until their flesh is softened and relaxed.
puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	Then take hold of them with your hand, until they are restored and you no longer feel them.
Du chastrement de taille:	Of the circumcision.
covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez;	it is fitting that you dress yourself properly, and press the skin of each wound with your left hand, then tie the suspender, and strike above each wound one time, until you have thoroughly cleaned them;
et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz;	and leave no piece of fat exposed beneath the surface.
et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure;	and this manner of circumcision is more gentle than that made by attraction, for because of the attraction it may sometimes leave something exposed under the skin, on account of which the best part desires luxury.
puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	then treat the wound until it is healed.
des hermofrodites	Of hermaphroditic individuals.
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes:	Eunuchs are according to two manners of men:
l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	One is that between the two testicles opens like the figure of a woman's form, or has hair, and sometimes no urine.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And the other woman also suffers similarly, and has a lump on her finger like a nail.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies;	And the treatment of sterility and famine is that you copy the joined marks, all of them, and treat as other wounds.
en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	In the second manner, of men whose urine falls from the skin over the testicles, there is no cure.
de la tentigene	of the tumor.
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir;	Tattoos are marks joined on the natural part, as long as they are too ugly to see;
et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	And some women have it even more so than a hand, and that's the treatment.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement;	It is fitting that you tie off the surplus of the vein at your hand or on the wrist, and cut lightly;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	and do not cut too deeply, lest there come blood from the vein, for it will be a greater harm; then seek another remedy until you are healed.
et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	and to another char that has its nose in the mouth of the mare, and on the hump, and by chance it bursts forth, and is as if one had a cow; and for this reason they call them old "cows".
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If you must copy it, just as we have said, and the treatment until she is healed.
de erratique	Of error
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis;	It is an error if it occurs at the woman's nature is not perceived, or the cut is pointless;
et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est;	and is its nature born with it, or an accident due to illness that has come upon it;
ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit;	It is done by a stick, or by the force of a subtle suction, or by an insertion made in the marrow, in the ribs, or in the bones, or wherever it is desired.
et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir;	and they conceive and give birth to an infant, and by chance the flowers may bloom.
et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	and knowledge of this is found through observation of the bile.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If it is an abortion that is close in appearance, so be it for your two or the right.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi:	If it is done by a subtle suction and the pulse is near two fingers, then push it back, and return to the same.
met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes;	hold your two middle fingers together, and the woman should lie on her back, spread out her legs;
puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens;	then press the two fingers together until the subtle suction is felt, and when you see the stoppage of blood.
puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	Now take the laine, and the mold in oil, and put it on the joint, and have the woman apply it to each person every day, so that it will heal.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the swelling is hard and dense, it is suitable to cut with a small spatula resembling a leaf of myrtle.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope;	If the stump is in pain, when the pressure is applied and the poultice.
et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef;	and apply the medicine stains, if like caecy, the stain of dragon, incense, assembled in abundance of wine.
puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder;	then apply a poultice of burlap large, so that the wound will not heal.
et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec;	and then let it be for a long time, and apply a tent of dry linen;
puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	then be cured with other remedies until he is healed.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when in the marrow comes a piece of bone, if you cover it accordingly this manner, unless it is an enchantment in the abscess.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For when there is an enchantment in the marrow, one should not touch fire.
des emorroides	from hemorrhoids.
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul;	Bleeding wounds are outlets of veins which do not usually happen accidentally, and when bleeding wounds become old they turn into boils;
et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	and we have said in the division that similar symptoms to boils and signs exist, and I will now explain those which respond to a cure.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I said that hemorrhoids and pain in the thigh occur when they are embedded in the marrow, and if there is no sign of improvement by feeling, unless it is treated with fire.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those who are at the mouth of the mare, one can feel them, are those that one can cure.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses;	Therefore it is necessary that you place the woman in a cold house, then tie the altar (or suppository) with fingers, and cut it at its roots, then powder on medicinal substances restraining blood, as we do, and like dragon's blood and incense, and similar things;
puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide;	then bat her feet against the wall for an hour, then put her in cold water;
et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	and if bleeding occurs, then she will take it (presumably a remedy), by sitting in a decoction of sumac and pomegranate rind and gall, and with similar things; then take wheat flour, mix it with honey and ghee, and apply it on her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if she stains, that is good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir;	If it is not so, instruct them to apply hot air on their backs and at their breasts.
puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	Then take the poultice, and the pus in juice of plantain or of agrimony with wine vinegar, and apply it to the patient.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	And when the abscess has rested, then treat the liver with application of ointment until it is healed.
et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul;	and that which is called "albathir" is red, and resembles the head of an ox, so if you wish to cover it as I have said.
et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then treat him until he is healed.
des apostemes de la marris	of the marshes
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many kinds of abscesses come from the marshes, such as chancre and a stone-abscess, herpes, swellings, fistulas, hemorrhoids, and hot abscess, and many other diseases that I have mentioned in this division.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe;	It is therefore necessary to say in this treatment the hot abscess that comes in the marrow, which is not an abscess like those that boil with bowels;
et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	And if you want to see the work of iron, look at whether the apothems are swollen at the beginning of its appearance, and full of heat and fever, and if it becomes red then you can see it.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie;	Therefore do not hurry to pierce, but let the thing be maturated until the pain is relieved.
et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe;	And then place the sick person on a bed, and have two pettish beds nearby where he can lie down, and support his back and arrange his feet in such a way that they are not near the leg.
et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien;	And have his knees expanded, and place his arms beneath his genitals, and tie them well with a good cord.
puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme;	Then place the ball over the right side of his chest, and prepare the instrument with which one works on the mouth of the mare, because afterwards comes the shape.
et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide;	And it is fitting that when you see this instrument being applied, that you prick the skin first in order to know the depth of the wound, so that what enters into the instrument does not go deeper than it should, and so that it does not harm the patient.
et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve;	And if the instruments are larger, it is fitting to cover the depth of the wound with cloth, so that the instruments do not hurt.
et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	And it is fitting to put the horn on top of the instrument, and to tighten it.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit;	And when the abscesses open and one pulls it with the hand of thumb, if it is fitting to cover the head, the spot where the spit is made.
et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec;	And when the bowel is empty, it is fitting that you put tanned membranes moistened in rose oil or dry green oil into the wound.
et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites;	and tie the tent of the wound to the very bottom of the gash, and put over it in that place the linen strip tied tightly with moisture or boiled in water or marjoram so they are cooked.
puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then the cure after two days of treatment comes to that, so that it may be made whole.
et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites;	and never lift the gash and the wound by means of syringe of water and honey, and then with water or long-stemmed asphodels are cooked.
puis reveigne a l’oignement.	then returns to treatment.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is closed up again on its own, it is advisable that you avoid using hot iron, but treat it as we have said in the division.
de l’enfantement	of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar:	First, the master is to the patient as it knows the figure of the natural birth of a child, and the signs whether they are present when you see the woman hastening after childbirth, and desiring odor.
adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir;	And so the sick person must hasten to go out;
adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui;	And thus he knows that this child-like being is according to the natural figure, and it comes out from its head, and follows with it;
et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost;	and when you see these signs, it is fitting to press his belly lightly, so that the child comes out quickly;
car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification;	because when he descends back to his head, it follows with him, and the marrow of its overflow is cleansed by good purification;
et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	and this one that comes in other ways does not come naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises;	Because he sometimes comes on his feet, and comes out from the body or the shoulder, or hands, or sometimes from his belly, or somewhere else, and is transformed by chance before his neck, and through other bad figures;
si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	If it is necessary to the physician that she be wise and subtle in these things, and warn herself of error and deception, then I will show you all the figures on how one must help.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent;	If the patient comes up to his head due to natural reasons, and a pregnant woman cries out in pain, and the child's virtues are weak, if you put her on a horse seat or hold her there;
et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	and if the oil or fenugreek has risen from its seed, and is then boiled, and you pour the physician's medicine between his two little spatules of which it is made:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers;	and pierce the vein, and strike at one angle until the moist ones that are inflamed are burned;
et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament;	and press the woman's belly until the child descends, and if it does not descend, then it is advisable to tie up the woman with a mixture of muskillaige [musk] and fenugreek in olive oil;
puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre:	Afterwards, let it bleed and purge with condensing, and keep his mouth and nose closed for an hour:
si istra maintenant l’enfes.	if he is then now a child.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc;	And if both hands are sprouting forth, it is to be preferred that you gently pull them out little by little;
et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut;	and if they cannot go in, place the woman on the bed, and lift up her feet.
puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement;	then bend down the bed upon earth, and take hold of the woman, so she will not stumble in rising.
et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	and if the hands cannot go in and the child dies, then cut off the hands with the knife that was placed before, and extract the child, and set them straight.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	from the state of the child on its feet.
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut;	When the sick person comes to their feet, they must lower them down.
et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz;	and then cut a little by little, until it is even.
puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	then pin it on the feet and stretch it a little at a time.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi;	can he jump just as quickly, if the command has to pin it, and make it take off by condensing.
si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	if he can jump, he will live.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it is not like what we have said, so the tumor grows little by little, until it follows its natural form.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	So it becomes lighter.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier;	and if he cannot jump as we have, then take myrrh from aloes, oil of saments, and gum melted, and pound all in mortar.
et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz;	and put on the nature of woman within and avoid this ointment, then place him in the water cold until beneath the ribs.
et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre;	And when it is moistened from below, they make a collar of mercury, and place it there, and let it be for an hour.
puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	Then they make him sit on the bed, then they make him vomit and hold his mouth and nose, and let him take gentle air to his belly, because now he is able to breathe.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	of a child's joint from its place
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc;	When the patient comes in this form, they put on the poultice a little bit at a time;
puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit;	then they put on the bandage above his neck, and hang down his feet, and let him lie on the bed;
et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval;	and let him bend his hands little by little, and then let them press the hands above the belly, and strip off the padding below, until it is prepared for the opening.
et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains;	And if the fever does not fall, take his feet and let them be moved, then move his legs up towards the chest, then pour your hands.
et ewe l’enfant poc et poc;	And give the child some water sometimes.
et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	Instruct the woman to pray as much as the fever lasts.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	of a child that is born with one arm twisted outward
I covient engignier a ramener la main:	It is proper to endeavor to restore the hand.
s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler;	If it cannot be restored, have the woman get up and go.
s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment;	If she cannot walk, have her lie on the bed and straighten up her legs;
puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit;	Then apply the medicine which I have told you.
et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main;	And if she becomes pregnant, so that she sits on a stool, then study how to bring it back into place with her hand;
et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	and she brings the child according to its natural shape, and she brings it forth, and he commands her to bind herself until the fever passes.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	of the child on its neck, and has spread out its arms, and turned its face towards its back its mother.
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement;	It is necessary that he holds his hand, then turns it little by little, and she will bear it lightly;
et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc;	and when it is even, he applies the natural musk and oil of aloes, as we have said, then he commands her to move little by little;
et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne;	and when you have done this, so that she sits on the stool, and he commands her to bind herself;
et la fai esternuer.	And let them burst open.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	of the same manner as it was to all that.
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie;	When it comes to this manner in all the lines, so strike the line at its joint, until the moistures are empty.
et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes;	and if the fever boils on its face and on its neck, so strike at the root, lest it be retained, and die the child.
puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois:	Then bathe the child inside, until you have put it in such condition as is fitting, and command the woman to restrain herself on no occasion.
adonques si istra legierement.	and so if they are light,
de l’issue des gemelz	From the birth of twins.
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent III ou IIII;	So that sometimes they give birth to many times, and sometimes only three or four.
et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	And this is not an unusual thing, and it has happened often.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom;	Two are strange things, and they do not live if they occur.
je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude;	I know this one, which they multiply, and are increased by the same faculty that devises it, which is linked to the blood.
et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	And no time occur in such a natural way as all of us have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait;	And if they occur severely, then the treatment is as we have said, and let the subtle remedies be applied quickly, and clearly, what she does.
et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	And do it in such a way that it is as if it were worth more than the price of medicine.
de plusors enfans	Of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient;	No time are formed in the neck or shoulder I, II, III, IV, V, VI, VII, or more so up to XV, and they are all shaped like an infant by the measure of their father’s glorious size, for the physician knows that such a thing will happen because it often appears.
si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	if it happens according to what is required.
de l’enfant mort	of dead children
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains;	When you cure the woman after a dead child or birth, as I said in the division, and it does not come to pass, and you are constrained by the work of hands.
si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort;	if it is required that you know whether the woman has a healthy nature and does not have an accident or fear of death.
si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees;	if it is required that the woman should lie on her back, and bring her shoulders down, and be inclined to the chest, and lift up her legs.
et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant;	and let the minister apply the poultice of two parts, whether tied to the bed or treated as soon as the child is born;
puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges;	then rub the mouth of the mare with moist oils of mullein and fenugreek and sesame seeds, then apply the oil to her hands.
puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief;	then pour the mare with oil lightly, then let her eat or drink whatever she desires that is convenient for her, and take care if there are signs of illness on her chest so that it appears upon her head.
si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes;	if the sores are in her eyes or on her neck or in her mouth or under her chin or near her beard or in the navel or over the ribs, and if there is discharge from them onto the feet, then apply or prick them with needles and cauterize.
et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide;	And it is fitting that you should tie the bowstring on your right hand and put the arrow between your two fingers of the left hand, and strike with all your right hand lightly, and knock the arrow into any one of those places that we have said, until it comes to an empty place;
et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	and this is the form of the bowstring:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz;	and then strike against another bowstring, or where you have need of it, so that the extraction is even;
et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	and then stretch it equally by moving from one side and the other, so that it may open, and so that the bowstrings are tightly fixed, as is the form:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie;	And if it remains a part of it, so that the bile is gathered on some of its fingers with oil, and strike them in that part, and treat the other part;
et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	If they do not stay in place, then put this needle or more up high where it can be felt, and do whatever you must until all the fire has been put out.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote;	And if one hand comes before the other and it cannot be straightened by straining, you should wrap around that drapery so that all its blood has been let out.
puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	Then cut into the joint of the foot or on the knee, and thus you should do it with the other hand, and two feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue;	And if the head of the child is swollen and it has stitches in its issue, or if it has a painful head, thus you should pour the thorned sponge between your two hands, and make the head and extract the pain.
ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui;	In order to find out what has been lost with this instrument called “almidach”, since the form comes with the instruments or scalpel that is after it;
et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment;	and then perform the same procedure for those who have great natural strength;
et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer;	and then treat the bones with tongs, and hold them tightly at the joint, if they are splintered, until the moisture that is in or on them dries out;
et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues;	and if it cannot be extracted, cut it into small pieces at the joint that you can.
et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	and if it has an abscess in the belly or outside the ribs, so that you may puncture until the moisture flows.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the fever is on his feet, so that there is a light attraction and an address to the mouth of the arrow is lighter.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main;	And if it is in the belly or near the navel, so that you may extract it at the wrapped strip over the hand;
et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre;	And let the belly swell or the stomach, until the moisture which is there dries out.
et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris;	and if another bone is broken, and the head remains, then pour the bile into his hand from the mouth of the mare.
puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer;	then pour one or two ounces, and treat him.
et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses;	and if the mouth of the mare is contracted by hot pus that has come out, so it is not necessary to struggle with it, but rather administer soothing and cooling things.
et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	and let him administer plaster, and cut it in soft water and milk.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif;	And if the child is on its chest, and you can put him level, then administer what we have said to a living child;
et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	And if they have no power, so let them be treated with pieces, and leave nothing of the second part.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris;	And when you have done this, if they take the things we said to be cut out from the arrowhead that comes into the marrow.
et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	and if they start bleeding again, then let it be put in water and restrained, and let them take other treatments.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut I autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman with child who had a child that had died in her womb, and she took another of the dead one instead.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, there came an abscess in the throat, and it swelled so much that it burst open, and great pain ensued.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was unable to translate this as I do not know what it is.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I put under the plaster of strong attraction, and from it came a bone, and after some other days some others.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was surprised greatly, because that womb has no bone.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	So I thought it was the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point;	If the wound is found, and touched with bones, until the woman was in a better state;
et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu;	and the woman remained long and thus, and it seemed after a few days that there was a small amount of blood on her.
et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	and I have not recorded this chapter except because when the masters found an unusual thing, they would seek advice.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	Bring back to their place.
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres;	After the fire cautery, comes the form of pressing, to which one applies books;
et a II tornans as II chiés des II liiens.	and in both shoulders and two joints.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux;	All things, the horns should be more subtle in restriction, and made of white or boxwood;
et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi;	and the mouth of the fist should be twice as wide as long, and one palm and a half long beside the edge of the trees.
et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus;	and in both joints should be two like this same fist, which are firm in one and the other, half a palm long or a little more;
et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	and these two fastenings are tied in the mouth of the mortar to open when you turn both horns.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles;	Another form, with a similar shape but more subtle and lighter, is made from a beam of ebony or boxwood, according to the likeness of the nails;
et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large;	and has two heads and two attachments, just like the palm of a thumb, and two are twice as wide;
et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes;	And when you see opening the wound to all the instrument, have a woman sit with a lit ( possibly a cloth or gauze) over the pieces and the legs exposed, then tie the two attachments together in the wound, and hold the head of the instrument between its jaws;
puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Then cover your hand over the entire instrument, just like you did with the nails equally, according to the quantity that you see opening the mouth of the wound, so much that the blood will make its way;
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances;	These instruments are all pointed, and they have many similar forms;
et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	and when the knives are made sharper, so is their power, and they cut through thicker skin.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	If you do not properly prepare the instrument before using it, because its need is not excusable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis;	When the second tooth is retained in the child, it is wise to instruct the patient to keep their lower jaw closed, and then pull out the tooth with tweezers, and hold their hands to the mouth and nose.
et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	and if it falls, well is that.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire;	If that does not work, take out the root, and make a puncture or wound, and put herbs that can open the mouth of the mare, such as camphor, anise, chamomile, cassia, and centaury;
toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu;	All these herbs or some of them shall be cooked or boiled in water on fire.
puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris;	Then put a chain or cord in the pot, and the other end into the mouth of the marrow, and hold it tight until the vapors come out from the marrow.
puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	Then pull out the flesh, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If his shoulder falls off immediately.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine;	And if it remains after this cure, and is not better, instruct the baron to make her moisten her left hand in oil of sesame or in muskillage of altai, and then pour it into nature, and desire a second application.
et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction;	and when she has found it, so grasp and extend it little by little straight, so that the marrow does not seize at the extraction;
mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie;	but you must move more lightly to the right and left, and then treat;
si venra et se desaerdra.	if he comes and falls back.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes;	And if the mouth of the arrow is tightly closed, we have said the treatment for vomiting, and fumigation with herbs;
et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire;	and if it is nothing of what we have said, be careful that you do not become foolish while treating;
mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon;	but it is said that what is in the mouth of the arrow should be bound to the woman's plexus, and then wrapped with ointment tetrafarmaçon;
si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer;	if the poultice will bring it back, and come forward;
mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	But it happens, when she does so, bad smell comes to the stomach and head, and the patient is ill.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu:	Then it is necessary therefore to give them foul-smelling fumigation to that:
aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	None of the ancients have ever used fumigation with cress and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The form of the instrument at which you should fumigate the woman is, in retaining the flowers and the second joint if it is this:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu;	And it is to be seen like a snake, and put the head subtle in nature, and the shoulders wide on the fire;
et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	and let the fumigation be on the embers, and the lice until it is exhausted, and then another.
de percier lou fondement	of piercing the foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac:	Most children are born without having any underlying foundation, for the child is nourished by subtle suckling.
si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche;	If it is true then let him go to the bath where he will perceive that which is good for him, and do not feel his pulse again by the stethoscope or gentle touch, and fasten the bandage so that it does not touch.
puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then put on a linen cloth soaked in wine and oil, then the treatment of poultice until it heals.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it will stop bleeding, then place a poultice of onions in the wound and let hands lie still, and leave it until the fever departs.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme;	And sometimes comes a sudden bleeding from a wound or an abscess.
si covient coper celui soudement:	If it is true then cover that sudden bleeding:
si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	If it is cured, as we have said of the cauterization.
de la fistule dou fondement	of a fistula in the fundament.
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors;	Fissures that come from under the foundation are nodules, and when they come from the ground before or in the space of two parts, if there is a fistula or more.
et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans;	and when that node is old, it must be treated in such a way, with moisture awakened and causing blisters or subtle boils, and there is no time when these fistulas pass.
et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	and are produced because of the thing that comes out or ventilation when the patient makes an evacuation, and by chance one falls on them.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge;	And if the fistulas occur just above the bladder, and just above half of the penis;
et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	and reach just above the joint of the thigh, and just outside of the knee.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant:	And thus it is known that the fistula persists in the fundament, and does not persist.
et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	and you put your thumb into the fundament, and insert a subtle needle of linen or iron into the fistula when there is no twisting.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit;	And if it has tortuosity, put in place a subtle tent or a horse's hair until you feel the tent or the hair to your will;
et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit:	and if you don't feel it, and no pain or discomfort comes from the wound or the tortuosity, as we have said:
saiches qu’elle ne perce mie;	since it does not pierce.
si te haste dou curer.	so that you hurry to the cure.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula is cut across to the bladder or just across the conduit of the urine, then it comes out and cannot be closed by medicine.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu;	If it is felt at the joint of the elbow, then the tent comes to the left.
s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement;	but if it does not have tortuosity and the location of the pain is on its own, then it is a bowing inward, and no medicine or immediate treatment by applying poultices;
et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	and in these painful ulcers there is no cure except for hard work and useless endeavors of foolish people who intervene.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos;	For one that is not painful and is not old, there is hope for recovery by iron, as I have experienced, and it is that the patient will rest between your hands on their back;
et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre;	and he lifts the legs up to his groin, and bends his knees to his belly;
puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	then he pours a poultice of dung or of wool if it has tortuosity, until you know whether the poultice comes.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet;	If the patient feels pain at the bottom, then it is fitting that you pour your two index poultices there, since then if the poultice has affected him.
et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans;	And so if it is discovered or you sense between your thumb and fingers, then know that they are swollen;
si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If it is not strained very much, then it cannot be cured.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc;	But some people can be healed by this treatment, but few are actually saved;
et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit;	and the one that is healed, if it happens to be cauterized with a subtle fire according to the width of the fistula, as was said;
et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement;	and it boils all over in the fistula until it comes from the bottom.
et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil;	and perform this twice or three times until you know that these swellings must be burned, which are like a feather of an owl;
et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	and then the doctor of tentacles moist in butter, until that flesh be firm, then the doctor of ointment puts on and stitches.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If it is thus hurt, this is well.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez;	But if this, in another way cannot be cured;
et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur;	and if they put pressure between, and do not pierce at just the right spot where it is founded, and there is a covering of thick flesh or fat between the two places, and you see the fistula at that place which has a soft covering.
si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente;	if you cut from the beginning of the fistula, and drain afterwards before the dressing, and then apply cautery until it comes to the head of the fistula;
et sera delivré li tente, et cherra;	and the wound will be delivered, and it will heal.
puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	The hairs that are cut back too much look like the quills of an owl, and they do not remain the same.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if he does not want to be healed, and you cut between you and the wound, then the cautery of fire or medicine will be applied.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses:	For the fire cautery, there are two bone things.
c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor;	which is to say, the irritation of those hairs that are stuck together, and the drying out of blood and the shrinkage due to moisture.
puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe;	and then the treatment for wet or moist swabs in butter or in a cold box, until they dry out and the hairs become arched.
puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	and then treat the wound with ointments that are quickly dried up with cold and harsh remedies, and dry medicines.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	When he is restored, if it is healed and does not come back again.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if an abscess comes just as deep into the bone and is distant from the body, pour in two or the depth of the bone, and ask about it.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres:	If you feel the wound and it is between two things, whether it be linen or a suture or hairs, or if it is close to being perforated, if there are only fires visible for sight and hope, by the care of one of the three methods:
ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier;	If you burn it so as we have said, or if you cut into its root, or if you can pierce it and treat it as before.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit;	and do not pierce too deeply lest you strike the root that holds the foundation, and comes out by chance in the opposite direction.
puis le cure, si com nos avons dit;	then treat it as we have said;
par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé;	in case it heals, then remove that covering and the mud as soon as it is cut from the root, or by probing or with another instrument pointed.
puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues;	then find out what free thing is in the wound, as much as you can;
puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement:	then study to restore the wound and keep the fistula in the back part of the root.
si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere:	And sometimes fistulas occur in this way:
et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	and when you pour the tent into the fistula, and it is stuck at the bottom of the skin above, you take a tent made like this.
Et i boute I fil tort en II, et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And I put the twisted thread in two, and put the tentacle all along the thread in the fistula until it reaches the head.

et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent;	and bind it tightly at any time, until the threads come out of between the two bones and get loose.
puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	Now cure the wound until it is closed and healed.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not perforate, then pierce it in all ways that you can, unless it is too deep.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is not advisable to tie up the wound if it is too deep, and then treat it, as we have said, until it heals.

des emorroydes	of hemorrhoids.
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres:	Herbs are according to two kinds:
ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement;	or they are inside the fundament, like grains of resin, and when there are small and great ones, and in the wound cut on the side, and when there is one or more of them, and it avoids the fundament and at the head of the fundament.

dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	cut very tightly around the veins or foundation
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	It happens frequently that blood clots suddenly in the intestine, and by the force of nature, when the disease is old and medical treatment is worthless.

puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then the healer as long as he is healed.
dou fremit	a fist
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont;	A formice is a small warts-like appearance on the body, and it will grow into a more significant one.
et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	and sometimes the truth is, and it's felt just like death of coldness, and comes to all the body, and more in the hands than in other parts.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor;	And the healer says that you should take a thorn of an swan's feather, or a strong goose feather, and put that thorn on the coldness, until the purple circles appear all around.
puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	Then turn your hand to the entire chain until you can feel it all vibrating together, and bring it out by its roots, and cut through the roots of the vibration.

ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser.	Do not pierce, because it will hold in two, and you must press.

de la forme dou clistere	of the form like a bladder
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet;	Never is done a clistering of silver or bow, or molten lead or patch.
et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	and never is done these small and large instruments, according to the size that they are brought.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	These then one uses in the treatment of children and those who are weak and painful, are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The shape of the small or large syringe depending on whether it is above or below in this way:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez;	and if there is a deviation or the belly is tied, as you see, and the joint is perceived to be inside.
et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I;	And has a fracture on one side, and in the other.
et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre;	And if he is a man who puts medicine from the stomach of an animal or parchment in his belly, and it is perceived to be around with small fractures, then each fracture must have one unit of space, and pour into these fractures a strong thread that is twisted in X or in some place, and assemble the belly as if it were a goat.
et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize;	And when the medicine is inside, if he holds it in front of an instrument with a strong thread, then seal.

puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet;	Then the minister greets him with both hands together, until he is entirely well; then extract the splinter, and raise the patient’s legs to show them off, and if the medicine comes out as it can.
et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	and if he sleeps a whole night, then it is even greater aid.
