et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	and that's the shape of the very subtle splinter where the skin is tightly stretched:
des plaies	Injuries
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies;	We have previously discussed the cure for wounds;
or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	or you will say the cures of hands and medicine, according to its completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that injuries are diverse according to what they are made of, and according to the places or locations where they are inflicted, and why they are inflicted.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses;	Things that are caused by piercing with a stone, or the cutting of a sword and knife, or an arrow or a club, or similar things.
ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres;	according to the laws of the body, if a wound occurs on the neck, or head, or arm, or belly, or liver, and similar members.
et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	and I will tell you the treatment for each wound, and will begin with simple wounds of the head, because the memory of this chapter will come up.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut:	I say that when a simple wound comes to the head, and the bone is not broken, be careful because it may be due to piercing with a stone or similar things, and the skin is completely torn and the wound is large, and you doubt whether an abscess has formed.
si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree;	If you do it soon, the healing of the head itself is what matters first, if it comes from bleeding of the wound, and if they are healed on the opposite side of the navel.
et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	and lest the patient be given a lot of wine and fat meat.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char;	And if he does not heal, if his meat is made thinner and he drinks no wine, neither eats any flesh.
et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice;	and puts on the wound, if an abscess comes in, cotton soaked in oil rosined alone, or in vinegar suppository.
et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés;	and if there is no abscess, puts on the wound, if it is fresh and all its bleeding has stopped, and if it is not moved by air, powder, I will say so later.
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the humors have moved, so put on some bandages, until he is healthy.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is great like a sword cut and similar, and the lips cannot be brought together by stitches, then they are sewn together, as I will say of wounds of the belly, from the seam.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope;	If the wound is exposed to bone, and flesh, and only holds together by a thin skin, it will not heal.
puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	Then treat the wound with medicine, and restore the thickness of skin in its place with leather-like tissue, and instruct the patient to eat great quantities of meat, just like eggs and cooked bread, as well as chickens and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure;	And if you find rotting skin and it clings to bone, cut off the entire rot and take out the pus, then treat him.
et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil;	And if there is an artery in the wound or vein that will not close without surgical intervention, and cannot be stopped with medicine alone, then choose whether to tie off the artery, and if you find it dislocated, fix it with a thread.
et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	If they do not profit from this cautery, then the fire.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere:	And if these wounds are small and simple, then it is a light cure.
et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	and put this powder on which also softens the flesh as it has moved.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est:	And the way to make the powder if
pren encens une partie;	take frankincense a part;
sanc de dragon II parties;	burnt dragon two parts;
chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc;	salt of live three parts, and the subtle powder, and apply the wound, and bind it tightly, until it is well closed and united to all its blood.

car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	For the medicine will not remain with a person when they are healthy.

de la plaie dou col	of the neck wound
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If the wound is on the neck and it is simple, but there is no difference between the two of them regarding the head, but if the nerve on the neck or the artery is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire;	If it's the neck, do not put any other medicine or restraint, for night causes swelling and makes them retract.
et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres;	And do not put anything on the wound, because the flesh of the nail is cold, and the continuation of a boil is with the brain, which is the highest part of the body;

de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of arrow or sword wound
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne:	If it is a blow from a lance or sword, and the wound is deep, then look at the direction of the wound so that you can see.
saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz;	Therefore know that the wound is mortal.
et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide;	And if it is not deep, and the wound is fresh with all its blood, then do not put powder in it or bind it at first, nor let it bleed more than what comes out by natural means, turn back to the heart, and take care of the patient.

et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors;	And if you do not have dressing, put some cotton in the wound to absorb the moisture, and make the patient sleep on the wound for three days, or four, or more.
si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne;	If there is no spasm or trembling of bad thoughts, he should not strain his mind.
et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	And when you see the bone in its proper position, if you know that the wound is healed.

et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule;	and if she cannot be healed and opened, then you should know that there is an abscess.
si la cure si com on doit.	if it is done as it must be.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant;	and if the wound is from a cut of sword or knife and it is simple, on top, or on the back, you should cure the one in front.
s’elle est grans, de cousture;	but if it is large, of suturing;
et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez;	And if it is small, of powder, and she has pierced pieces into the bone, and so chosen the wound, and the flesh is burned when they are severed;
et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions;	And if there are no wounds that have been severed, then let the wound fester, for it will ease the extraction;
et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And other wounds with different limbs are treated in the same way as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	A falling or bursting of the stomach.
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis;	The bursting of the stomach is great and painful, and small.
de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus;	From the large wound there is no time for the intestine to be released or the nerves of the intestines, because of the intestinal insertion.
et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut;	And the stitches are more painful, and no time is worth even a small wound compared to a large one, because that's why you put in more pins to keep the intestines back inside, if you don't put them back up again.
por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II.	Because the intestines swell so quickly that they feel pain, and return later, therefore it is to be feared for those with the inner wound, because for this reason one must move the entrails back to their place which others have done.
Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres:	And it is known that there are four kinds of rupture in the belly:
les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies;	the two common folds occur in the belly fold, and the other three specific folds of other body wounds are also common to all those wounds;
et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	and they are all more specific to the belly fold, and I will say each one and declare them.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres:	I said that when the wound is small and there is no intestine injured, and it's a matter of putting something back, this is one of the two kinds:
ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	Out of consideration for the injury, as we have said, or because the intestine is swollen due to the hurt.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere:	and when it is cold, heat it in that manner:
moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	moisten it with an sponge or the size of a cloth soaked in cold water, or you cook it in boiling water and vinegar and spices, and keep the intestine warm until the swelling is gone.
et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	and at no time do this vinegar-staining, and apply it when the swelling is gone.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose;	and when you see the swelling depart, moisten the intestine with water or boil and salt are cooked, because by this it cleans out easily.
et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes;	And if it cannot enter, they make a small wound to the instrument with which one strikes the hemorrhoids;
et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait;	And the first treatment is castration that equals its size, so we should not cut it unless there is great necessity and no other option.
et c’est li estrumens por le fendre:	and this is the stricture to be broken;
si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	if it tears inside the cavity and does not come out, and then you see the form;
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestines jump out, so you put it back again according to its natural form in its own place, if you have the power, for this is useful.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief;	When the wound is large and it is in the lower part of the abdomen, you should have the patient lie on his back and lift his legs higher than his head;
et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre;	and if it is in the lower part of the abdomen, you should lift the head and the belly higher than the other parts, and so when the wound is on one of the two sides, put your finger into that place so that the navel is higher than the other.
et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	and so it is necessary to treat what I say about large wounds and medium-sized ones.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres;	Treat small wounds with what is applied to you; then take both hands and have the merciful minister who shows all the necessary tools in his hand, and assemble the lips.
et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort;	and this is the common way of suturing wounds, and it is that you prick an awl or more arrows, according to the quantity of the width of the wound; then let off a little from the head of the wound two fingers' breadth, and put in an awl with good strong thread.
et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble;	and prick the two nails of the leather with the two nails of the siphon, which is inside the leather, until you make it pierced from that part, and assemble the two heads of the siphon four times.
puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille;	First instruct the patient to insert the thread into the double strand of the needle, then assemble the two pieces of the wound immediately, and finally leave two fingers' space, and then pierce another needle.
puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte;	Then the thread is tied like you did with the first needle, and do not stop doing so according to what is needed of the needles until the whole wound is restrained.
et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer:	And let the needles be in proportion, between subtle and coarse, for fine needles cut through all the flesh, and large ones cannot penetrate very well:
por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes;	for that is why they should be in proportion.
et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure;	and it is not advisable to push the needles too far into the flesh and skin, lest they cut through and destroy the wound before healing.
et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee;	And then cut the hairs around the needles so that they do not cause the patient to fall asleep, and tie them with strings or cloths around the hairs of the needles to hold them in place, and leave them until the wound is healed.
et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II.	And this method of sewing with needles is more convenient for small wounds, because it involves one needle or two.
Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien;	The second sewing method is common, and it is that you join two pieces of leather together with two pieces of silk in assembly on one needle or where there is only one strong thread.
et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras;	and when you have joined these two together completely, then the needle retracts at the place where you started it, in the manner of sewing clothes.
et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi;	And put space between each fold of skin the size of a small finger;
ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	This fold in the abdomen seven times at home, and I sewed up an injury that one man had in his belly, which was cut by a knife, and the wound was more than half a palm in size, and intestines were protruding well beyond two palms in size, and the wound was located in the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I let the intestine go then it was twenty-four hours later and the wound had healed for fifteen days, and the cure, and I was sane.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle;	And if they had hoped that he would die, it was a miracle;
et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines;	and did not cure him with medicine, for I was in a place where there was no one to be found, nor any medicine.
et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And put more ointment on the wound twice a day, and washed it with water of honey until he was healed.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture:	I can’t help with that.
pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens;	Take the needle and the thread from the back where it was sewn inside.
quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer;	How many times the needle has pierced the vein straight through straight, whether it pierced in the head or on the cost, or put the needle inside and made another hole from the back where it was sewn inside.
et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	And if the sewing is done in this manner, that you sew as the barber sews his beard, and that you leave once on one side, and cover with another, until the entire sewing is completed.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere:	The second manner of sewing, which the Galenists call properly, is such that they assemble both parts in one piece naturally, and apply one end of the vein to another end, in this way:
fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac;	Make a needle or head of a pin close to the mark near; and pierce it only there, and let the two joints at the shoulder.
puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac;	Then turn the needle and pierce it from the side opposite to where it was previously inside, at both joints of the shoulder.
puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit;	Then pierce one and the other from the side opposite to where it was previously inside, at both other joints near the mark on the other side.
et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	and this is the most common way of sewing and dressing.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune;	They say it is so from this phrase, and no one witnesses it, therefore we should sew the belly with two needles, or if there is thread in each.
et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies;	And one must poke one end of a needle from this side, and the other end from that side, in the manner of those who sew wounds.
et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	And it knows that when the laceration is in the belly, the stitches cause more pain than those on other parts of the abdomen.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies:	The judgment of the wound is like that of other wounds:
et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout;	and that when you find the fresh wound has all its sinew and blood drawn out, so that the arrow has moved it, then fix again the intestine, and the wound.
puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe;	Then puts on the powder mixed with charcoal, and if the arrow has moved it, then puts on any dressing that is present, until the wound closes.
et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach;	and they cut the thread, and they sew the belly, and the medicine.
puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat the wound as other wounds until it is healed.
et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	and if you do not have medicine, put on it as soon as it is recognized, cotton wool and then move it twice a day until it heals.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples;	Because you do not need any other medicine in addition to these dispositions for simple wounds;
et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles;	and if you doubt that the wound will cause commonality among the principal members, it is fitting to put a lighter linen in oil of tarre hot, or in rose oil, and place it on the abscesses, and below the swellings;
et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine;	And if he feels pain or putrefaction in the bowels, and this happens many times, since it is caused by wine vinegar, just like that putrefaction comes to his intestine.
et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	and he cuts within, and learns that when it is the large intestines, it is lighter to heal than the small ones.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestine which is called "jeun" cannot heal when it is rotten, and this is because of the plant matter that is in it, and because of the subtlety of the entire body, and its proximity to its natural state.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres;	And if the wound is eaten away from the place, he places it behind, just as with the intestine, while it is fresh.
et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres;	and if it is old and has turned towards blackness or brown, then it is better to remove the one that is black, because there blood and veins will not come from it, for there are veins.
puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	then cut that which is between the ligament, and hang both the two heads down from below the wound until the extraction comes out with the vomiting of the bowels.
de la routure dou boueil	of the burn from a blow
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance;	When the intestines are ruptured, and the wound is small, it can be restored in some men, because I saw that one man was wounded or pierced by a spear in his abdomen.
et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez;	and it was the wound on his right side of the stomach, and became infected and developed a fistula, and from this occurred the evacuation and vomiting.
je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	I treated it according to what I knew, and did not stop subtlety until he was healed, and the pus disappeared.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre;	And when I saw it heal, I doubted that the patient had an evil in his stomach.
et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans;	but he did not have any illness, but instead improved in his condition and ate and drank.
et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere:	and they say to certain experimenters that when he has a small wound in the intestine, he must be bound in this way:
pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus;	Take the bowstring around large testicles, then assemble the lips of the wound, and when the bowstring has passed over the mouth, put it on both lips, so that it constricts his mouth.
et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise;	and then strike the head, and it will stay in place so that he cannot dislodge it, then take another bowstring after, in this same way as before, until the wound is completely closed.
et cout la plaie.	and sew the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere:	Those who have a knot in the intestine, and no trouble to the patient, and can tie the intestine with a thin thread that is cut from the intestine of an animal, in this manner:
pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure;	Take the head of this string from the intestine as much shaved down as possible, and then tie to the head of this thread thin string, then insert the thread into the needle, and cut the intestine, and pull it back in the wound.
et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance;	And this manner of sewing on foreign flesh is only used according to the way of faith and hope.
et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	And if the wound is great and wide, especially when it is in one of the narrow intestine channels, there is no remedy except subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of a fistula or if it is
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Any wound or abscess that becomes inflamed with age is called a "fistula", and especially when it is swollen and has a discharge.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	And a fistula is according to the vertebrae nodulation free of hardness and whiteness, or no pain is felt, and it is also like the beak of a bird.
et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse;	And sometimes a clear bowstring, and other times a thick one;
aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;	sometimes little, and at other times enough;
et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes:	and I have spoken of this in the division of wounds, that any wound which is not healed and does not have a cure, is only due to one of the seven causes:
c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors;	that is to say, by the smallness of the wound or body.
ou por sa malice;	or due to its malevolence;
ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char;	or because it has a hard and stubborn quality inside, and on the lips, which does not allow healing to take place;
ou il i a trop de bowe;	or if there is too much bowstring.
ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit;	The limbs are poor, and the material is of bad quality;
ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure;	For the medicine is not good in the treatment.
ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence;	because it is a sign of plague.
ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature;	because the property in this region is late for digestion and late for health, and fleeing by nature;
ou il i a voinnes ou os:	where there are veins or bones;
et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	and I have shown all these causes and signs and cures for medicine in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	It is necessary that I inform you of the treatment for fistula which is done by operation of hands.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;	which has a fistula in every member of the body;
car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez;	because there are fistulas that come from the great veins, and arteries, and nerves, or to the sac, or to the intestine, or to the bladder, or to any of the ribs, or to the spine of the back, or to any joint of the hands or feet;
et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	and if to those who come to take possession of the principal member, and as if they were.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance;	And all the ulcers in this manner are due to bad health, and there is only labor and ignorance.
et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier;	and if there is no ulcer that does not arise in the place I have told you to look, and you have confidence in the cure, and you see it manifesting, then take a thread of arrow or iron, whether the ulcer is straight or curved;
et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit;	and if the ulcer is twisted, then search for a subtle thread to push it back, because the threads bend in following its twisting.
et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;	and if the ulcer has broken skin and you cannot well search for it with threads, then close one of the breaks, because moisture is more easily closed on another break, and cleansed;
puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent;	Then let the patient feel the pain in their power, so you know if there is bone or nerve, and it's stuck fast, and ask the patient well about the pain they feel when you press on your hand, and what place it is;
et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens;	and when you know truly where it is, and if it's near a joint, or a nerve, or an artery, or a vein, or any of the places I have told you about, if you cut according to what I have told you, and remove the foul flesh and corrupted bones that are inside;
et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;	and then the cure until it is well, and if the fistula is deeply set in right direction, so that it must be cut deep to remove, as long as you can, then put wet tourniquets in medicine ague, and pour them into the fistula, until the medicine corrodes the remaining superfluous matter at the bottom;
et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then I put ointments on clean wounds, so they become healthy;
et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	and if it is not healing with these, then cautery as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted by an ulcer, kill it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit;	But if a vein or nerve does not grieve or affect the principal members, as we have said;
et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if the bone is exposed, and there is corruption and blackening, then remove the corrupted part as much as possible, and cure with ointments on clean wounds until it becomes healthy;
et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font:	and if it is not healing, and the wound festers as before, know that you are not going to cure it unless you start anew from the beginning.
si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu;	If you uncover and desire it as much as you are at the bottom, and remove all the corruption, then restore him.
et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	and if he is in such a state, that's good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir;	If this is not the case, know that the corruption has gone too far, you cannot expect anything from it;
si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature;	if there is no other solution than to resort to the art of nature;
et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un;	and if there is a small, corrupted bone, and you can treat it with tongs, if the strain is on a convenient instrument for this, and if there are many bones, take all of them, don't leave any one.
et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	and if the moisture makes it worse, and there is no error or fear, cut and dry, and deliver the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os;	If you do not remove them within an hour, put the wound under a cloth and apply ointment to prevent rot, and let it sit there until the pus sets in between the bones, and then they will have less difficulty with the bones.
et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie;	and if it's a large bone, such as the thigh or knee, remove only the rotting flesh until the blackening is complete on the bone, then restore the wound.
et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os;	and if there is a great part of the corruption, and it comes to form a mole on the bone.
si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez;	if it is suitable and covering all the corrupted area, then let the patient be covered until he has become sound.
et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	and I will tell you of a fistula that occurred in the patient's leg, so that you may take an example and assist me with your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	It was a young man within XXX years, who had pain in his leg due to a cause that came from within the body, until the materials arrived at the leg, and he fled from a large abscess, and had no other reason for not opening it;
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	but the mirror by their folly opened so much that the abscesses opened, and they flowed out a lot of material, and it became a fistula, and many of them got infected with pus and moisture of the body;
et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	and many mired his cure within II years, and there was no remedy in the art of hands, until I was summoned, and I came to see his leg and the medicines that were used to treat him, and what was flowing from the infected wounds had great harm to the body;
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	And so he became red the body of the youth, and had the color citrine.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I applied a tent in one of the abscesses, and then I searched for all the abscesses, and found that some were meeting at other parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	I failed then, and cut into one of the wounds so that I discovered a part of the bone, and found it corrupted and rotten, and there was corruption inside the bone.
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	I saw that which appeared to be the corrupted bone, and thought there could be no other corruption except what I had taken.
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	and began to restore the wound with medicinal salves for a long time and could not heal.
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	and then resumed, and discovered the bone in its original state, and found the corruption continuing inside the bone, and I saw it, and then I removed it, and thought of healing it.
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines;	But I could not cut through to an inch of bone, and the treatment was very painful, then I restored him with medicine.
et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	and he became healthy and whole quickly, and it did not require further work except for the weakness of the patient, who could no longer endure, and because I feared his death.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For the evacuation of blood often takes place, but it brings no harm and the person recovers entirely, and in their place an iron-hard cartilage forms, and they are of good disposition and have no harm or ill effect whatever, neither at rest nor when coming.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, and he wishes to be treated in this way:
pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	take the ligature, and strain the tendon at the head of the bone which is open, and command that it be stretched upwards;
et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	and take another ligature of a thicker rope than the first one, and tie it above the skin which covers the exposed bone, and pull the skin tight until you treat the infected flesh downwards, and uncover the clean flesh as far as you see, lest the wound infects the skin.
et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	And place a stick or a table under the bone to cover up the corrupted flesh;
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	and it is necessary to sew as soon as you can see and feel the corruption, and sew again afterwards.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute;	And if the bone is corrupted and will not open, and the corruption is in the middle or in a part, then uncover the flesh completely.
puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit;	Then put a stick under it, and then sew the one part to the other the corruption, sewing above the lower part of the corruption, as we have said;
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	and if the corruption is in a joint, then cut out the corrupted joint and sew the bone where it contains on the other side;
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	and if corruption is in the continuation of both joints, so there's no other sign but a boil.
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	and if corruption is at the nail of the hand, or at the nail of the foot, so that thing is very strong, but you must always inquire how that corruption came to be.
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	and purify it in all the ways you can, but make sure that neither venom nor nerves cause harm.
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	and know that the incisors and hair are many, depending on the setting of the bones and the appearance of them, their thickness and subtlety, and their size and fragility, and their hardness.
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;	and so it is necessary to prepare each type of bone according to their likeness, its instrument.
et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	And it will show you the instrument that you will need, according to the knowledge of this art, and the testimony of the ways of diseases;
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	if it is necessary that you have the instrument according to what it should be.
dou feu	Out of fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	The joints will dislocate either because of being inside, or because of not being there;
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	and when you have medicine to cure the corruption by the treatment of medicines, and it does not help, then it is necessary to cover that member up to its joint or where the corrosion comes from, so that the patient escapes death or by malice, which is greater, from the defect of the limb;
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors;	and if the signs are that the limbs become black, as if they have been burned by fire, and after that blackness, it spreads to another member, and takes over all the body;
si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	If you touch the fire cautery, and if it is by striking of certain venomous beasts, such as scorpions from the sea and lizards and similar things, so that the corruption is in the head to two, then strike again, and do not give him space until it comes before his hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	And if it comes to the hand, if you strike on the joint, so that the corruption does not come before the arm;
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute;	and if it comes to the arm, if you strike on the elbow;
et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	and if it passes the elbow, it is death, and there are no other remedies than those that depend on its power;
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet:	and do so in the same way whenever the corruption comes to a bone;
s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	If it comes to the first joint, then apply it after the other joint.
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	and if it comes to a bone, then cut through all the bone.
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	and if it goes up in the leg, then cut at the joint of the knee.
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	and if it comes above the knee, then there is no other treatment but to kill the patient.
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	and the way of cutting or dressing the limb if it is such that you bind above and below, and tie one stretcher to the lower end and another to the upper end, then serve the cloth that is between the two stretchers at a distance of one span wide, until the bone is visible.
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	the needle or thread, and tie each of these parts with linen, so that the needle does not touch the healthy part, and comes to the patient another wound and abscess.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans;	and if bleeding occurs while you are working, then immediately cauterize the wound with haste, or apply certain powders to restrain it;
puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then return to your medicine until it is completed, then bind the injured limb with a strong cord, and care for it until it is healed.
et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet:	and I will tell you how it happened to me in that house of stone:
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	there was a black spot that seemed to be burning with fire, and this burn came first on his two toes, until it consumed the entire foot;
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	And when the bones see the corruption, so he covers the foot, and is made well.
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	And long time after the corruption returned, two fingers of the hand were affected, and he came to me, and I put above those affected areas counteractive things after cleansing the body, and could not stop the corrosion.
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	and he said that I should cut off the hand, and I did not want to, because I had hope of repelling the matter.
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible;	and also I doubted whether if I cut off his hand, he would not die, because the virtues of the body are weak;
et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	and he despaired completely, and returned to his own land, and he covered his hand with earth, and was made well.
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	And I have heard this tale of fire cautery only because of another treatment, if it is needed.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	But sometimes an abscess comes up on the skull, and it remains so for a long time that it causes great swelling of the forehead.
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	And then it bursts and perforates, and the bone is shot out, just like our vessels.
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	And the skin that covers it is just as subtle as a dried thread, and does not run against the bone or the nerve; and such disease is called 'healthy', and is not called a fistula.
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	But if it is so long that it reaches the bone all the way through, then it is called a fistula.
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	And the treatment is such that you strike that skin all over, and meanwhile as it is subtle, just like we have wrapped.
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	and does not heal because of its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	And if you have assumed that the skin heals, and the corruption is not in its entirety, and the skin is thick from fat, then apply a poultice like this:
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	examine the size of the breasts and the bowels that are in them from a foul odor, then apply a poultice made with Egyptian medicine as follows:
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	take equal amounts of aloes and oil, and put them to be cooked in one vessel over the fire, until the medicine is red and becomes as thick as honey.
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	And then take what is needed according to your necessity, and make it in water and in honey, and bind up the breast, and strap the wound.
et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	and let the medicine remain on for two hours, then pull it out by pressing.
fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	do this many times, until the breast is well defined, and draw out the pus.
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;	and at no time do bind with hot water of ashes, when this medicine is not available; and take ash from the fust of grapevine, and pour on warm water over it, then let it run, and bind up, until you know that the breast is well healed.
et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet;	and if the patient cannot bear it, or does not have any relief from Egyptian medicine or hot water of ashes, bind up with water and honey when they start to break out in small boils.
ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain;	You clean it with honey and wine made sweet, so that the honey has property to purify and cleanse, and the wine is boiled until it becomes healthy.
et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin;	And when you have done this and believe that the breasts are well purified, if the cleanser made from it (the honey) produces pus inside it, and you prick at it with forceps, and make a puncture with oil rose and in wine;
ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens;	Or you clean it with some medicines and ointments, of which I have previously mentioned the properties or treatment of the ointments;
et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez;	And if the rupture of the breast is small, and the canker from the cleanser cannot enter, then enlarge with a needle by one puncture, and apply a tent of Egyptian ointment or basilicon ointment, until it is enlarged;
et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if the wound is too large, so that the cut and its closure can only be done at a joint where it can enter, and if there is a fracture with the bow (above) exposed, then the patient must lie on one side as much as possible.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;	But when the bone is in full depth, do not let it be left untouched.
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere:	And if you cannot cover the shoulder area underneath so as to see it properly, do shape it in such a way that the bone is brought down to its lowest point, for when the bone is deep, do not let it be left untouched and if you cannot cover the shoulder area underneath so as to see it properly, shape it in such a manner:
que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe;	so that the bone moves slightly downward, and do not leave anything of the bone.
et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain;	And take conserving medicines to put on the healthy one, and stand over the linen drapery that covers the whole body.
puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois;	then bind the wound with a bandage that is not too tight or too loose, but rather according to its size; and place it on the healthy one to alleviate the pain, and do not put on the thick bandage of fire until after many days once.
et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste;	and the one who has on the wound in the breast will often take out the bowels, and knows whether it is venom or blood or if it is undigested or un digested.
et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez;	and take precautions if the patient feels pain or numbness, and if there is an abscess or not, and when you see how your medicine has spread in that manner, then observe whether the wound heals quickly, and approach the healing.
et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	and then put it away at morning or the third day, and when you put in a new bandage, change another and renew the tie.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breasts are swollen with indigestion after many days, he knows that the breasts do not heal.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle veins are cut after a long time, do not despair of your health, for good health is approaching.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire;	For it is known that there are men who have been late in applying heat to their wounds, and those who do the opposite.
et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie;	and if a bowled-up indigestion swells up near the breast after many days, knows that the breasts will not heal.
et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine;	and if the breasts are slow to absorb and are far from healing, add dry medicines mixed with moist ones in equal virtue, since the bandage is tight, for there is a great part of vitriol, and this is the rear medicine.
pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance;	tie the bandage tightly and make it with rose oil mixed with equal virtue of olive oil and vinegar.
puis le confit et en use;	After the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu;	And this same treatment makes the flesh grow thicker, when no injuries are present, or you take a mirror and oil and incense, and grind it, and make powder on the honey while it is over the fire.
et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire;	And then in the glue I wrap, and stretch it over the breast, and sometimes an ointment of gold is administered, and roots of the celestial lily, which is as fine as flour.
et en use de simples ou de compostes:	And using simple or compound remedies:
broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use;	Grind them up and make a powder, and put it on the honey that I told you about, and use.
et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens;	and if the treatment is prolonged and does not heal with this treatment, then you know that corruption has entered deeply into the bone, or it presses on the joints, or makes the limbs hard.
si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	if the treatment of the fistula is such as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	Of the abscess of the foot
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	Panarice is an abscess that forms under the fingernail, or under the toe, or sometimes in other parts.
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	and when it is old and not tended to, so that it comes to an abscess of the flesh, and swells and becomes infected, they cut away and clean the wound as long as they can reach the root of the nail, and sometimes they even cut all the way through.
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	and the corruption comes just to the bone, so that it brings great pain and a foul smell, and the flesh of both feet is swollen, and its color is flushed.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it in the manner we have said in division, and the treatment does not benefit him, so it is necessary that you apply to him a piece of iron to all the remaining surplus of the foot, then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	The cautery is much great aid if the bones are healthy, and the joint is healthy;
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	and if the joint presses against the cartilage, and begins to pierce it, and swell, so as to apply a cloth under the joint that covers the cartilage, and bandage high up, then carefully strike that subtle and gentle blow, and put on the remaining of the cartilage medicines sharp and corrosive to remove all.
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat with ointments until they are healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	and if the corrosive is in the bone, then strike it, and pull out, because as long as the bone is corrupted, it cannot heal.
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if you see the doe ( likely a corruption or inflammation of the flesh) corrupted, then strike it in its place as previously said, and treat until it is healed.
et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	And if it is frozen, and you drink, and it feels great pain, then it would be best to cure him first.
puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	then cut the wound with a straight edge at an angle in cutting across it upwards, and be sure that the cut does not come too close to the flesh under the wound, for the patient will feel too great pain.
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	and if it has happened, then put something on top that soothes.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	The pain from a sore throat
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The two joined bones in the hands of some men are charred and sometimes there is bone, and occasionally there is an ingrown nail, and sometimes the birth of a new joint does not occur at the root of the joint, or it occurs in no one.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	Those who are born in any way other than by the two, do not move afterwards, and those who are born at the joint of the two, perhaps will move.
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	the cut on one who is emaciated is lighter, in this manner:
taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	cut the root of a large splint.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer:	That person who is born with a defect in the root of the joint will suffer from illness.
si te tien dou coper.	if they are tied under it.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	In him who is born or must be cut at the bottom, if it suits to first copy around the circumference of the bone just on the bone, then cut the bone to a suitable stringed instrument for this purpose, then treat so that he is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The symptoms that come with a severe injury or condition often arise from birth, or due to sudden wounds, or by fire, or similar causes.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	If you cover the wound so that it heals, they must repair it according to its natural forms;
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	then put between two tents or cloths moistened in oil of roses so that it will not heal.
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	or put between two thin slices of onion so that it will be closed, if it is fitting.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If the symptoms come to any of its parts with the palm, then treat the wound as it suits.
des vils	Old age
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	Where such large veins are swollen and full of melancholy fluxes, that they come to many other limbs.
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	and it happens more often in the legs of those who go to feet and who work and carry, rather than others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	It is therefore necessary that you give them no enemas of bile, and then cleanse the spleen with basil.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres:	The iron cure is done in two manners:
l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	one is that you cut them and treat the black vein;
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	and the other manner is that you tie a vein, and extract all the blood.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere:	The cutting is done according to this manner:
arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	first the leg of the person who is ill with hot water should be cut very hard, until the fat tissue is removed carefully, then extract the leg from the wound upwards to just below the knee.
puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	then cut the vein in three places, with a large cut, then lift and extract the black vein at your finger, from head to toe, until as much blood comes out as the virtues of the patient can bear.
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	and then tie, and he commands to take meat in sauce with black iron.
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	and resume the evacuation and bleeding when the veins are empty, and it harms the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere:	the elevating of his chest is according to this manner:
reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	raise the leg of the patient if there is much hair on it, then put it in water, and he makes the leg soak in hot water until it becomes red and inflamed with veins.
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	and if you do not have vinegar, heat it on the fire, and then make an incision directly into the vein at the long point of the elbow or in the area below the knee;
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	Then cover the wound with linen, and burn the vein of each part until it appears when one feels it;
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	and as you see it red and black, and when it enters the linen so that it seems like a white thread.
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois;	then pour out the blood from below, until it rises to the linen, and then take it up lightly, and cut into another level as before three times.
puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	then burn the skin above the vein until it appears, then lift up the blood, as you have done, and cut into another linen, as you did first.
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille;	then cut another size, or as many as you need, then lift it up, and cut again at the foot, then take it and lift it to the second size.
puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	Then take out the bone by piece by piece until it is completely torn apart; then cut.
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	And if you cannot treat and lift it, then prick the bone with a sharp needle twice on each side of the fracture, and apply the plaster from both sides, until it hardens.
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	And be sure it does not harden, for if it hardens, the bone cannot be treated or lifted and comes to cause harm to the patient.
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset;	And when you have completely treated the wound, apply a cloth soaked in wine and olive oil to the patient's leg.
et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And care for him until he is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie;	And if the bone is crooked and twisted and has become dislocated together, and it is not straight as we said, then it must be broken with great force, but do not cover it.
et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	and as we have said before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	The form of the iron wedge used to cut open a vein if it is curved and does not pierce, will damage the vein.
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	and is of a large curve, because if it were subtle, it would cut the vein, but when it is big as we have said, and this is the form:
de la voinne civile	of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein is set in the legs, or in hot parts where there are no herbs or trees, and on dry land where there is no moisture.
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	and by chance it is found in other parts than the legs, and this happens because of putrefaction that comes from under the skin, just as it goes inside the body serpent-like and downward, set between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this vein cutting are such that it comes to the leg a great inflammation, then change the joints, and start cutting the vein vigorously, like one pulls out a root from a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	When the joint opens, it is advisable that you wrap around an inch and half of the knee with bandages from one side and a half to two inches on the other side, and the ligament, and leave the bandage on the leg, and every time it is not near the joint, wrap it again around the plonc, and the new.
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	and if it is too long, cut off a part of it, and wrap the rest around, but do not cover its root, until it comes out entirely.
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	because if you cut it, it may enter into the cartilage, and cause an abscess and putrefaction there, and a very bad illness.
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	because of which thing it is advisable to treat it little by little until the head, and leave nothing of it in the body.
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse;	and sometimes this vein when treated with the palm of one's hand, or with X, and a man came to me, to whom it arose from X palms long, and when you copy it, so your blood flows out or gets pierced, and the puncture just reaches its source, so that everything is lost;
et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	and let the material inside be evacuated, and let the medicine penetrate into its depths every day, then the cure is done as with abscesses.
