Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains;	And sometimes to this vein it comes down in rain, and itself when it opens up at the joint of the foot, or of the toe, and it comes out much blood, and from it there flows.
cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	Therefore, cure as we have said beforehand.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	of worms that are born between the skin and the flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	This disease is called "disease of the cow" in our land, because it often occurs after drinking, and it has a small worm that nests between the hide and the flesh, and goes through the entire body, mounting and descending, and feels bad at the head as one member suffers until the hide opens or it escapes, and then fomits.
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	and it is corrupted by the pus of some humors, just like they come from serpents and worms and other parasites or intestines.
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil;	and there is doubt about its evilness, because when it goes through the body, and it climbs to the head, and it comes to the joints, by chance enters and destroys them.
et ceu avient maintes fois.	and this happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you see a cure being done and treated, so it cannot be done when it's cold.
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	Then it is necessary to tie the limb above and below a strong thread tightly, then cut up and treat it, and if the vein is bound completely in its length, and you do not find it when applying the fire cautery on top, so that it dies.
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	And the greater harm he causes is that he will run oil, as we have said.
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	And if you see him coming or near the oil, then bind under it with a cord, and cut up and treat.
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	It is necessary to use the patient in a kind of purgative medicine for broken solutes of bodies, and he should be given food spoiled and putrid.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	of the pain which comes from overexertion
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre;	This disease is called "vakirir" in our land, and it is a pain that comes to some members, and causes them to move from member to member;
et je vis ceu que je vos di.	and I have seen this which I told you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was summoned to an ill woman, and she showed me on her arm, and saw a small swelling in the vein of her arm;
et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	and then after a short while, I saw it rise again just like a worm on the shoulder, faster than anything, like living silver when it cuts through.
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	the pain left the arm, and set up in the shoulder, and then it came again after a short while, running through all the body until it reached the other arm;
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	She now tells me she has torn her insides inside the body, just as I saw.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was much surprised that she moved thus from member to member, because I had never seen this disease in such a manner.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	I have tried to get it to move again for many people who had pain in their limbs before, but I did not do so with her, just as I saw in the woman.
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	and I thought it was because of that which the woman had a cold body, and the women uncovered wounds, and for that she appeared to be in great distress.
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	and do not appear to be so for those who are healthy, and have moist bodies and wounds that heal.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	And when you see someone curing this sickness, and the patient feels that pain, if it appears as we said, if the humors are above and below in abundance, and then strike at it until the great constraint leaves.
et cauterize le leu;	and cautery the joint;
et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	and if you cannot see it with your eyes, then the cure of those who treat the swellings, such as fetid pills and serpent pills, and similar things.
des saiettes	from the arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	The arrows are different, according to their appearance and according to the nature of each person's body or where they pierce.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	The various kinds of them are that there are those with great points, and small ones, and spikes, and nails;
et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	and those with two angles, and those with tongues, and those that have parts;
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres:	and those who are found in any member, expelled according to two manners:
ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	or in the principal member, which is like a brain, liver, spleen, stomach, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When she falls then in any limb of these members, and the signs of death, which I will tell you after, appear to you:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	if it is fitting for you to remove this arrow, because death comes afterwards in many situations;
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	and when this bad sign does not appear to you, and the arrow is not properly extracted, take out the arrow and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	And when the sign of the brain occurs, when the arrow shoots and pierces the bone, and blood comes forth from the skull, which causes seizures, and confusion, and swelling, and redness in the eye, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasms and disturbance of understanding, and vomiting blood.
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles;	and perhaps he has no fever of the nose, or ears;
et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	and sometimes it is in the throat and voice;
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	and falls from the white, moist wound like flies, and leaps out in the same way as a stream of urine.
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	and if this sign appears to you, then take care of the wound, and remove the bandage if it's not on.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	the sign of the bandage when it's bleeding or congealing is that it's near the left nipple, and feels like it's been pierced in something hard, not empty.
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	and perhaps the bandage dries up like the flies, and in darkened blood, it comes with cold sweat and frost, and fainting.
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	When the head of the shoulder feels a sense of doubt because the death comes.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	The sign of the arrow that does not bleed is only without any scum falling out of the wound, and its throat is swollen, and the patient's face turns red, and they gasp high and are chilled by the frost.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes;	And if an arrow sticks in the covering of the thigh, so that it is lodged between the small ribs;
et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire;	and causes great pain and great difficulty breathing.
et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And all the limbs of the shoulder move.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow hits the stomach, by chance so that it falls from the wound any indigestible meat.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow hits the stomach, and it falls into nothing but air through the intestine, without any hope for the treatment or extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor:	And if an arrow sticks in the bladder, and urine comes out suddenly and flows away, and the patient feels great pain:
saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	Knowing that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other limbs, if they are cut and bruised and swollen and the shoulder and elbow and groins and axillary region and spine of the back and flanks and groin and thighs and limb, as the condition is: they are safe according to many opinions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or artery and it does not cause harm, as I will tell you, for that reason: that you may do the same.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	It happens in the house with an arrow stuck in or near the root of the neck.
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I tried it, and the treatment of another patient from behind the ear took place, and was safe without any harm.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles;	And they tried to pull out an arrow that had been shot into the fat under the ear behind a piece of paper, and the arrow was pulled back, but no more than to the tip towards his fist, and the arrow was great like a Turkish bow to all the iron for easy pulling over ears;
li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	the treatment was successful, and no further bad accidents happened.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And they pulled out an arrow from the neck of a Christian, and it was an Arabic bow to the ears:
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I cleaned the beards and pulled gently until I had done it, and the Christian was made safe.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And take an arrow to his house, where it had fallen on his stomach, and thought he was dying;
et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	and then after having passed thirty days, he did not improve in his condition.
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut up the arrow, and set it in place, and made a mark on it, and there was no bad outcome.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if I saw a patient who had an arrow stuck in his backside, and the wound was closed.
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	and the arrow remained inside him, and his natural disposition did not change, nor was he in pain for any of his natural works.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And I saw another man who had an arrow stuck in his face, and the wounds were closed.
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor;	and he endured thus suffering great pain;
et mout d’autres semblans.	and many other similar afflictions.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie;	And there was an arrow lodged in the king's palace at home, which had been shot into his left side, and was starting to decline towards the right side;
et estoit li saiette toute reponue.	and the arrow was entirely blocked.
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	I went to see the physician after it happened three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	If I found the wound extremely narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I tried to extract it with great subtlety, but I didn't feel anything.
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	and he felt a puncture and pain below his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I thought it might be the tip of the arrow I placed above his liver and stomach, because they were swollen;
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	And the leeches of the arrow came out.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis;	I put the plaster on my hands every day, and solved the wound directly, and kept the patient for such a long time that they felt the arrow leech come out inside their nose.
et il le me dist.	and he told me this.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	I put some medicine that is both sharp and corrosive on the wound every day, until it was fully opened, and I tried it, and you felt the head of the arrow dry out inside.
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	then I pressed it into the opening of the wound with that sharp medicine, until the leeches of the arrow appeared visibly.
et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	and after three months, I saw that the wound had opened up and I closed it with hot tongs on both sides, but couldn't get it out;
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	And so do not cease to subtilize and devise ways of instruments, until the day I took good tongs well-made, according to what its shape will come at the end of this chapter, until I tried it, and restored the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And they judge that the membrane from the nose cannot be restored:
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	I restored it therefore, and the wounds were closed, and the sick were entirely healed.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	I have told you the quality of extracting arrows, so that you put your care on what I do not say, because the books cannot grasp everything;
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	but wise masters know little but a small amount, and on what is present and faltering, find new work, and nine instruments, at the handling of strange things that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres:	I say that arrows do not penetrate or fall out of members where they are fixed, except for two kinds:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	or from the side where they enter, or from another place.
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	and the one that falls from where it enters, is an arrow entering into the internal organs, and will never happen again.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it does not fall now, let it remain as long as the wound is open and the pus is discharged.
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	and also if it is stuck in the bone and cannot come out, let it remain for some days, and move it every day.
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	and then it falls, and if it does not fall, if it pierces into something more substantial, until the internal organs are enlarged, and then take it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide:	And if an arrow is shot into the bone of the head, and it goes just in front of one of the two stomachs of the brain, and some of the accidents that I have said to the patient:
si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	but if it is not treated immediately, but lets it remain so long that it becomes even after some days, for if the arrow comes just in front of the brain surface, it's death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is fixed only in the bone alone, and does not come out at the same spot, and the patient stays there some days without any new accident, then it engages itself into the treatment.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit;	And if it is deeply lodged in that way and cannot be extracted, since I have said to you.
puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat the animal until it is healthy again.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the arrow is returned to the body of the animal if it cannot be seen again, and whoever has all the tentacles.
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	If you feel it, then let it go with an instrumentable thing.
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	But if you cannot open the wound due to its tightness and because of the deep extraction of the arrow, and there is no bone or nerve in it, then let the wound be closed.
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	If you can remove the arrow if it has ears in it because they hold, and if there is a chariot stuck on two parts of the bone that you can reach, then break or bend the ears of the arrow so that you can pull it out.
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And be subtle so that you do not break the arrow, but rather pull it out more forcefully.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot do it once, so that the pain is gone from both sides until the limb is put back in place, then try again, for the extraction (of the bone) is painful.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if the symptoms of bloodletting disagree with you, then follow what we have said about the treatment in this chapter.
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement;	and take care of the incision on the nerve and vein, and tie a bandage in such a way that you can easily treat the arrow wound quickly, soon or firmly.
et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	and put the patient back in the shape they were when the arrow hit them, because that is the greatest help to be found there, and if you cannot do so, then put him according to what the sign shows you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	the arrow that comes from another side, or if it is closed up in anything, or the skin is swollen on its own, whether we see it or feel it, apart.
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai:	therefore draw the arrow up high, so that the tongs can take hold, and then extract it.
si saut fuer maintenant.	if now they are swollen.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is retained in the bone, so turn your hand around completely, until it enters into the bone, and then expand the bone, and pull.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	If it cannot come out, then let her go again, and then continue extracting until she comes.
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	and if the arrowhead was stuck in the flesh, drink the whole of the pus.
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument;	and if the arrowhead falls out, and you see the pus, then administer poultice, so that the tip of the arrow between the hair of the instrument.
et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	and then drink more, and if the arrow is stuck in the head, so that you pour the instrument into the wound, to alleviate the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow has entered into it, so it is fitting that you copy all of its length within or where the venom is, if you can, then treat the wound as it needs.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	and if the arrow sticks in the belly or more, or in the abdomen, or near the bladder, or on the side, and it is close to the surface, then you can cover it up, if you like.
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	and protect the vein and the nerve, and then pull it out, and then cauterize the wound, for that is proper.
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And the treatment until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The form of the tongs used to remove arrows are like the beak of a bird, and thus we have this shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres:	And there are many ways:
grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	big, small, and middle-sized, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The form with the handle attached to the hair is like the feathers of a bird, to push into the tip of the arrow, as it is in this shape:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The form of the nails for pressing and stitching is thus:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of veins on the body common
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir:	Veins from which one is saved are thirty-one, because it has sixteen veins, that is to say:
II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	Two branches behind the ears, which are called "herbets".
et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans;	and two arteries that are in the left temple appearing.
et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	and two veins that are in the right armpit of the right eye, which are called "aspieres".
et li voine que est emmi le front;	and the vein which is inflamed at the forehead;
et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	and the vein that is in the head, swollen.
et les II guindeges qui sont ou col;	and the two tendons that are near the neck;
et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	and the two veins that are above the lips of the mouth, and these are called "augerich" (or possibly "augeriche").
et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	and the two veins below the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras:	The veins that are commonly found in each arm.
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	one is the cephalic vein, which is located on the left side of the chest, and they call it "vein of the head" (or possibly "vein at the forehead").
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»;	and the joint is called "fast" and it is composed of the cephalic and basilic veins, and they call it "venne du cuer" among the common people;
et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	and the basilic vein is found on the right side of the clavicle, and they call it "venne du ventre" among the common people, and it is located near the fissure, and that is the vein from which one heals, which opens up obviously in the pouch.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains;	And the radial vein is the vein that is between the auricular and ulnar bone, and it has two openings;
et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes:	and in the leg and on the foot are three veins:
l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit;	one is below the wing of the bicipital vein on the left side of the clavicle, and the second one located at the ankle on the right side of the clavicle;
et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	And the vein which is called "nasse", located at the other side of the joint.
et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	and in the other leg there are three veins below those ones.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The vein that is behind the ears, which is used to treat catarrhs and migraine.
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre;	and the quality of the vein, just as I told you, is that you lift up the head of the patient and rub the vein with a rough cloth.
puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief:	then the patient's neck is tightened with a rope until the two veins appear behind the ears in two places depending on the head.
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	only if then you see the pulp under your thumb, and where you feel the pulse.
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	Take the lancet, and the tourniquet below the vein just until the bone, then raise your hand all along the vein upwards, strike and cut the vein well; you must do it twice to cross, and make the wound bleed.
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	Then tie off and secure, until she is healed;
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	and I have also said incising and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	Those suffering from double arteries in both temples, if they have ancient inflammation, and swelling, and eye problems accustomed, and to the eyes due to acute pain.
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	and the qualities of the patient if are so as I say:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement;	And when the patient dislocates his neck, so much that the two veins are tightly closed.
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	and feels pain below the elbow and then becomes numb;
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	then lifts the vein up to the elbow above the wrist index finger, and cuts the lancet under, and lifts the vein up high, and pricks it, just as you have done in other veins, and make a cut according to your necessity;
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	then lifts the patient up, and puts his elbow on the vein for an hour, then puts cotton on it;
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee;	and then forms a bandage, and leaves it until she is healed;
et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	and we have discussed their cautery and extraction, as well as the beginning of this book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The illness of the vein in the forehead is worth as much as the illness of the head, and has ancient diseases such as emigration, and redness;
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	and the quality is that patients with straining turn their necks in twisting, until the vein appears;
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	then take the instrument called "trencher", whose shape is:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	And place the point on the vein, and pierce upwards with your hand, or with something else, and let the wound bleed according to the quantity you see;
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	Then deliver the patient to their neck, and tie the vein until it is healed and there is no sign of a flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus;	It's not suitable to describe a specific outcome for this prompt since it does not provide any context or results.
et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	And the healthy are prone to it, because the bone is near, and by chance breaks the flesh when it is subtle.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	Those who are sick in both veins that are in two arms will be aided with the eyes, and the tongue, and the redness, and the swelling by the ointment, and with diseases of the face;
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	and those whose sickness is that the patients twist their neck in a strange way, without any bond, as before.
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	then the healthy, and if their sickness is through the passage, some short, some long, some small, some large, because there is no flesh.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise;	And if the skin is subtle, by chance may break;
puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	then sew the wound, so much as is necessary, and then tie it tightly up.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	The sickness of the vein in the nails is so serious, and full of fever, and sharp pains, such as inflammation and redness that comes to the face, and most especially when it is old;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	and if the wound becomes so serious that the patient clamps his neck, then pulls on his nails to your left hand, and takes out long, subtle flake, and strikes it into the space between the two nostrils, for the vein does not open well in that place, and the pain will now begin.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	And don't go too deeply into the wound, and do a clean cut according to your neediness, then tie it up for a night, because it is quickly restored.
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	And this is the form of the flame:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	The sickness of the two glands is aided by the constricting of the vein, and at the beginning of swelling, and with much suffering, and with epilepsy, and with corrosions, and with herpes, and itching.
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	and the qualities of the sickness are that the patients strain their neck away from one and the other, as we have said;
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	and the masters standing above the patient's head and the patients cutting at one side of the vein, then heal the vein a little longer, then treat the wound temperately, or as much as is necessary;
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle;	Then make another incision on the other vein, then cut the ligament, and gently constrict the veins, so that the patient does not strangle.
et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	and let him just stay there until morning, so that the wound is healed.
de la sainie des leivres	Of the sickness of the feet.
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The sick of the veins on the lips are aided by coal in the mouth, and by corruption of gums, and tearing of lips, and they do not heal.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And you will test whether it is healing by sitting the patient in front of you, and constricting his neck as I have said;
puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	then turn the wrist, and look at both veins, one is in the right hand's wrist and the other is in the left hand's wrist, which you can recognize by their black color, and because there are small black veins around them:
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	Therefore take both of them, and if you do not recognize them, and are in doubt, then cut the largest one on each side, and do so for all four veins, because it is the same manner.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	Of the vein below the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	The patient suffering from wounds below the tongue benefits after the treatment of the cerebral region, and this is due to the constriction of the throat, and eye troubles, and mouth afflictions.
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	And if the healer is of such quality that he brings the patient between your hands in front of the sun, and lifts the tongue, and looks under each corner a vein black.
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	Then heal both the one and the other, and do not pierce too deeply, for under these are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres:	The veins of the throat which are commonly healed are healed in two manners:
ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	or piercing with a pointed needle to the full length of the mitten-sized vein, or an olive oil subtle as it is called "anesil".
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	And are large and subtle according to the size and tightness of veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The famous mercurial form is so renowned, and it is wide as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	And has necessity to open the vein cheeks that are smooth with a large amount of blood visible, and which contain a lot of blood and turbidity.
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	and this is like the form of a burning olive tree:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	And it is more subtle in application, and it is for healing the small veins subtly, or with subtle blood clots of citron.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The gall of the basilic, which is one of these veins, helps in all diseases that are under the throat, and near the collarbone, and near the chest, and near the stomach;
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	and it is fitting for a lord that he should heal with his own blood, and that he should war against the artery that is below.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	And if he cuts the artery and bleeding ensues, then it is fitting that he should staunch it, as I have said;
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	and should not be pinched by the flame, but rather cut like a horse.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	And if the ligature does not open immediately, it is advised to remove it and replace it with another.
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras:	or you want to give some blood, or you will make the vein open with a needle in the arm.
elle apert manifestement;	if it opens immediately;
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	and cuts the flame with a horse's knife, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	And if you see the vein opening in front of you, so it is also advisable to remove the arm, touching the joint until you know the pulse;
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	then mark the vein of the wound, and then tie the arm, and cut the vein with a horse's knife;
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere:	and guard so you do not cut on the artery when you see it swollen, for this is of the artery:
eschui la donques.	choose accordingly.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	And if you see it protruding above as the urine of a child, and it is pale and subtle, know that this is without an artery:
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	hurry up then, and put a tourniquet on long, then draw it off when there is no bleeding, for this often happens:
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides;	if the arm is stuck, and leave it so, and do not move the patient;
et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	and let fear have its way, and do not move him until he is cured.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient;	If he is not scratched at his birth, and it strikes him, and the medicine does not apply to him, then cut the artery when it opens up, because the head of it will retract.
et estainche li sans.	and scratches him without being noticed.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	Take a splinter from a thorn and insert it, then take one of the halves and tie it to the other well tied yesterday.
se li sans estainche, c’est bien;	if he is not scratched, that's good;
se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	if so, if the treatment, as we have said, with powder that scratches blood;
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	and the hemorrhages do not cause harm to more people with thin blood of the wound and with the power of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	The sick woman in the middle is treated with a strong medicine for her head and body because she is composed of basilic and cephalic, as we have said;
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	and it is fitting for the lord that he should be wounded in the lower nerve, and if he strikes too hard, and wounds the nerve, and it swells and his health is impaired, and by chance he cannot recover;
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil;	And this nerve is often opened many times, and if it does not open in any other person because of its subtlety, it is fitting that you use the aseptic instrument on him;
et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	And choose your poor (i.e. weakest) man for this task.
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if he has a vein between the two nerves, then pull it out long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	The sick person of the head is treated with medicine for her head and also helps her eyes;
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	and it is necessary to heal or staunch the wound with olive oil flame or myrtle flame, because this is the safest of all veins, for it does not damage the nerve or artery.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	It is necessary to seek the lighter part first, and do not grieve anything if you must start again.
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	and by chance the swelling of the vein may occur in some people, but you do not grieve anything.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the blood is according to your opinion.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	The first thing you must know to heal is that healing is only possible if it is done for the sake of preserving health, and in order to avoid future illnesses.
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute:	and whether healing is done on one of the three veins that are in question, namely
c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	This is what the text means:
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	And instruct the patient to fast in the beginning of prayer and at autumn and winter after cleansing, when the signs of replenishment appear;
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	and instruct to fast on the first day or third, after two hours or three days.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	The fasting that is recommended has no fixed duration for all diseases, but rather when it becomes necessary to fast on a day or during the night, in every hour and at all times.
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	And it is not advisable to fast children under the age of XIII years, nor women who are pregnant only up to the seventh month.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	It is not advisable to treat the elderly who have passed their 60th year.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	And when some people fast in any way, if he defecates the intestines of an easy enema, and has a great amount of feces retained, if the veins do not drain off the excess intestinal contents through the pores, causing harm to the principal members.
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	He who is too rich in flesh, nor in leprosy, so long as it remains unhealed, will not recover.
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	and if the disease is caused after colic, vomiting, and decrease in stomach wind, and frequent urination with woman, and toil, watchfulness, and purging, then all the virtue, whether through an arm wound or from a bodily source;
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	and then subtly correct the humors, if he is not greatly overfed, by meats and drinks and medicines, if you have him eat bread.
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	and then take a bath, as nothing is to be feared, in order to further his cure, and he will recover from the wound in the vein on the third day, just as we have said.
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	And keep away from work, pain, and luxury, and similar things;
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	And be calm and cheerful, and let the remedies be applied higher on those who are sick, and rub the arm twice or three times, then release the bandage in a moderate manner, because when it is too tight or not tight enough, it will not correct the limb without.
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	And then rub the patient's arms with his own hands, until the veins swell and you can feel them.
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	Then moisten the remedy with a small amount of oil, and put your left thumb on top of that vein below the patient's arm until it swells or fails to swell.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	Because there are veins that burst like strings at the patient, and some are so full of windiness, so that when you put the flame on them, they retreat again into the vein, and cannot be opened, and thus it happens to those.
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	If he has opened a vein, if the wound is too narrow, because of this you should advise the surgeons on these things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin;	And if he has opened a vein for the first time, it is good;
se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	but if not, you should continue to reopen it a little lower or above the joint, if the swelling is still present.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras:	And if the swelling is present and the patient hopes for a cure, if he lets it swell for one or two days and does not tie up the arm:
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus;	perhaps an abscess will form.
ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	do not enter into the bath, then reopen the wound if it pleases.
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	and if the wound is small, or without subtle treatment and you doubt that it will not cause much blood as you see, then be firm in that same wound itself with all its flame directly.
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez;	and the wound is handled quickly, so that the swelling may be reduced;
car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	because this happens many times when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see the swelling, do not re-open the wound again, and put on a little bit of lard oil, because it lightens the body in sickness, and is mild in this place like the oil that it is.
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	and thus administer the oil of lard to each wound you treat, so as to dry up the flow of sickness.
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu;	and this same thing causes a triangle and bow of pain, when you put it on the limb;
si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	if subtlety is lost and splintering when it is too big.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	And if one comes across a large abscess, which often happens, when the vein is opened only at those times when it is very small, then hasten to it, and put on a sponge soaked in water and vinegar, with a bit of salt, and restrain for an hour.
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	and it is fitting to do this after the issue of the vein, and if it remains in the limb for some days without either blackening or greenening, then it will not be harmed.
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	and if you see, put on some aloes or mirror dissolved in calamine juice, monster.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique:	And many times there is an abscess and appearance at the saint's wound:
met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	then take your hand up, and if you find the spot soft to the pressure of the hand, if that appearance is bad.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere;	Avoid therefore that you do not put anything of what we have said, because perhaps cutting without the artery.
mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	but the artery must be ligated tight to harden the spot, then treat with another cure until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each person according to the quantity of their virtue, and the color of the wound.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges;	For if they are not black, so let them issue blood as long as they are red;
et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez;	and if you see it large, let it be so that it becomes subtle.
et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	and if he is too cold, let him cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	It is necessary for the one who is weak and has need of extraction of blood to make a larger wound and let the fangs be wider.
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	And for the weak person, make the opposite, and it is necessary to heal them more quickly and often, and they should be healed by cutting across, not piercing.
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And this way of healing is safe from deterioration of blood and compression of nerves, and it is better to heal quickly with a small cut than slowly with a long one.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates;	And for the one whose body needs healing, it is necessary to give moist pain in grape juice.
s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	If it is scalded, if drawn from the wound three times or four; and if it is of cold temperament, if you apply a moist bread to the wounded flesh in honey syrup, or in aromatic honey syrup with spices, such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and cloves, and a well-smelling syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if the palm is affected, after a great amount of blood has been lost, it is fitting that he drink a weak broth made from charcoal and fragrant syrup, and use other things we have said in the division or chapter on syncope for the evacuation of blood.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wants to take out another limb, and heal himself again, it is fitting that when he is weakened by great blood loss, he should recover little by little, according to the continuity of his virtue.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And who wants to take out another limb after the first blood loss, and he has a strong constitution, then he will recover in seven hours after the first bleeding, or in the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And who wants to heal himself on another part, should he be able to heal himself the second day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre;	For it has much blood inside the body which is scalded, and brings on fever;
si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	so if you want to treat a great quantity of blood, and enlarge the puncture so much that it breaks into the brain.
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	then you reward all the signs of recovery and place your hand above the swelling, lest death comes in its place, for this happens many times when the healer is careless.
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	and it is not necessary when you see a dislocation, to untie the arm, and to make an incision a second time, and if the wound is closed, press firmly on top of.
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	but if it is crooked, then extend the arm quickly, for this would be bad.
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois;	but let him wait until he heals a second time;
ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	or you will point to the tip of the flame, until the frozen flesh has broken open at the vein's wound, and put on some powder mixed with water, and press gently.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is pulled out, let it go and do not hold it tightly, so that the abscess is calmed.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if the wound needs to be treated again, on the same spot, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein on the arm is healed in place of the wound on the head because it was composed.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	And the manner of dressing the wound is that the patient pours hot water on his hand, until the flesh is red.
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	After a while, bind it gently so that the vein appears well, then heal it now through and not too much or too long;
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	and let the large wounds be bound, and heal well near the joint of the hand, and if it will not come out, then put the hand in hot water, and let the wound drain in the water, until you have enough.
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	but if it's in a cold state, do not put the hand back in hot water, for one puts it in winter rather than in heat.
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	and healing from this vein is more safe than any other vein, without artery or nerve.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	The healing of the thumb nail is worth for all diseases of the liver, and this is the way:
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	Strain the hand, and pour hot water upon it, until the vein is drawn out, if you can see.
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	and if the vein bends and twists, and you cut it all the way through, do not cause any trouble.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	and do not cut too far in because the nerves are now numb and dead from the cold, and then put the hand back in hot water, if the pain does not come out of the wound.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have cut the wound as much as necessary, put oil and sinew to close it quickly, and so do each of these things.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The sickness of the left hand is equal to the disease of the mouse, and do it just as I told you over to the right.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The sickness of the spleen is worth more than all other diseases that are in the body, as with illnesses of the stomach, and retention of flowers, and disease of the rains, and of the kidneys and old joints, and similar illnesses.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet;	And tie off the vein if it is that you put some powder in hot water, and rub up the vein until it dies, and tie above the joint of the foot.
et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	and if the vein is at the ankle, and comes up from under the foot to great swelling.
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	The healthy ones when they are weak or more swollen, or at the ankle, what value.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant;	And if you treat it on top of the bone, then ward off the evil that is below, and cut the healthy as well as the diseased.
et soit li flaimes anesil.	and apply a blister.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if it cannot come out, so he puts his foot into the water, and leaves well to empty the vein.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	And if the healthy ones require it for the first time, then recapture it on top a little, because the pus is salty;
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	do not doubt the nerve, as we have said, and do so with the same care for both feet.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The salt of the vein on the calf is at the ankle, and its pus is worth the pain in the hamstring, when it's for draining.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne;	and the qualities of its healing if it is that the sick are in or bathing, and extracting above the ankle four times by twisting, because otherwise the vein will not open.
et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	and when she opens, if you cut her so that it heals in all manner as you can, and across.
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	and it should be copied as much as possible because the limbs are swollen, and she is very sensitive to touch.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	And if you cannot find it, so that the wound heals without any signs of blood or pus, on the back of the foot, and towards the little toe, and beware of the roots.
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint;	and do as many cuts on the wound until you see, and then tie the ligature, and put cotton and a bandage.
ele est maintenant sanee.	she is now healed.
des sainies de ventouse	From the venereal sicknesses.
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre;	Ventouses are made of horns, or thorns, or glass.
et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres:	And if evacuation is done according to two manners:
ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	or by piercing and attracting blood, or by piercing.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres:	And this evacuation which is done by piercing is according to two manners:
ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	or when it is with all fire, or with fire.
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief;	and evacuation done by piercing and blood extraction is performed in 13 ways of the body, so that one part may be all bone with the head.
et li autres est emmi le col;	and the others are emulsified with the neck;
et II autres en II costeis dou col;	and the other two are in both sides of the neck;
et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	and the ventose below the chin;
et li ventouse des II espaules;	and the wind of the two shoulders;
et li ventouse sus les crupies;	and the wind above the thighs;
et les ventouses emmi les II bras;	and the winds above both arms;
et les ventouses des II jambes;	and the winds of both legs;
et les ventouses des II chevilles;	and the winds of both ankles;
et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	and the woundings do not treat blood, unless for small veins that are scattered throughout the flesh, and because of them one weakens very little, just as one does when cutting into a vein.
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	and it should not be treated with heat, neither fire nor cold, in any disease that comes from overloading, until the entire body is empty.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if necessity demands because of illness, or by habit, so we bring it forth each hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and in every interval;
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	because there are some who, when they need to bring it forth, have heavy heads;
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	and some who find repletion and redness in their face, and in their head, and at the neck, and in their eyes;
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	and some who find a drop of blood in their mouth, and have swollen the tongue, and bleed.
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	and some who dream, and see blood and nausea and wounds and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	When we see these signs, and especially when it is in the middle of the month, we command to ventouse after three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The illness of moisture supports the healthiness of the head ... which comes to the eyes, and it is not suitable for this to happen after the evacuation of all the body;
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	and this ventilation is in place of the illness of the head, and it is not suitable for those who have a cold constitution to use, or who have flatulence, because this causes them much harm;
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	and therefore it is not suitable for the elderly to use it, or those who have head colds and other diseases.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who recover from this often become blind, and for that reason it is fitting to place the vacuum a little further down by the suspicion of blindness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	Ventilation of the neck is in place of the illness of the head and of the tonsils, and for this reason it is valued at constricting the breastbone, cutting into the channel of the stomach, and applying poultice, and treating with rest.
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	And it is right to stop for a moment, because if she holds too tightly, so her stomach or back becomes twisted.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique;	The swelling in the chest if it is near the collarbone causes pain in the head, eyelids and ears, and strangulation, and pain in the roots of the teeth, and is in the place of a bellyache.
et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	and it is right that you command the lord to express his hand before applying, so he does not cut an artery, and has no further bleeding.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche;	The swelling under the chin if it causes mouth illness, and gum corruption, and similar illnesses that are in the mouth.
et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	and is in place of sore throats.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The windings under the shoulders value to a disease that comes from heat and fullness.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	The incisions on the thighs are worth as much as three veins of the arm, because they bring blood from these large veins.
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	and instruct the master to not cut too deeply, for the flesh is naked from the bone, and it knows underneath the sinews and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire;	The incisions on the rump are worth like emorrhoids of the fundament, and illnesses underneath, it is necessary that the incision be large, and made with hay, for they have need to treat well;
et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit;	and in case it is subtle, it would break.
et i fai grans plaies.	and will make great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors;	The incisions on the legs heal quickly, because they draw blood from the whole body, and are worth like old pains from the rain, and of malarial fever, and move the festerings;
et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	And they are located on both shoulders, and both knees, and whatever they weaken the body after long use, causes death in various conditions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc;	The way to put on a suction is that you first put it empty, and then apply it correctly, and place it hastily, and move it evenly, and do not cease doing so, until you see the vein red and swollen, and touch the redness of the wound;
puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez:	then put on the suction again, and take care in the position of the body, because there are those who have contracted such diseases, and clerks.
si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes;	so it is fitting to strike once alone, and it is fitting to make large wounds, and a small depth.
et suce legierement.	and cut smoothly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois:	And if it is not big, so he should be pierced two times:
la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	the first time to subtley open the way for the great vein.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois;	and if it is very thick, so he should pierce it three times;
et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	and when we want to catch the vein little by little, he should pierce it only once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent;	And if we want a lot of blood, then we must start again often;
et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	and if it is not thick, then we pierce him through and through, and finish the cut so that the veins are perceived suddenly, and cut at the person with big skin and tough flesh, who has big pores, you should anoint them with oil of aperitif and dissolving.
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	It is made with olive violet oil, or sweet almond oil, or oil of sesame seed.
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	or oil from rue, or lily, or chamomile, or any other kind.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the swelling is big and cold, so take olive oil of marjoram, or balsam, or anise oil.
