Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if that person has healthy skin and large pores, do not put oil on them, but instead wash it after the water rose, or cold water, or elderberry water, or cucumber water, or porcelain berry water, or other similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those who have much moisture, lift them up with similar remedies, such as mint water and sumac.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	and those who have great swelling rise from a old wine, or dew, or decoction of anise and chamomile, or other similar things.
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II;	and should not be operated on with a vacuum before or in the bath, but after the bath for an hour or two.
et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	and should not sleep after the operation, and it is necessary that he warms up, when he must be operated on, and when he is swollen.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	And warn those who recover are choleric, and if they do not become too angry and inflamed;
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	if you must apply cold things, such as apples of Grenada and endives and lettuce at ease, and similar things;
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	and boiled fish, and char of chestnut, and moist meat.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And those with a cold complexion, should apply syrup of honey and a sweet-smelling wine, which is between old and new, and eat little, and eat boiled fish, and small fowl, and pease.
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	and on the day it will be purged, he must drink more than eat.
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	and it is advisable to give some to certain houses triacle or mustard before the purging, or after, for comfort of the main members;
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And instruct the patient to let his hair grow long but not too long; for it is not fitting that he who is bald should drink.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne;	The venesees that are applied to be painful are those that are placed over the liver, and the mouse, and podagra, and over the stomach and boils, and rashes, and hemorrhoids, for this member does not suffer from being pierced on or at it, and is done only in order to attract blood from one part of the body to another, just as we place them on the mammary glands when they are healing.
por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	in order to loosen the viscosity that is in the member, as we apply venesees to the stomach and boils in order to relax the member.
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	and to take away the pain, when there is suppuration or a stone, so that by its attractive power the suppuration goes away, or the stone falls out of place.
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement;	And so he does it when you put him under the liver and under the spleen because the blood is retained there, and these vessels are emptied to clean only.
et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	And sometimes they are managed with fire, and sometimes plain water is poured, as in the case of diseases related to pleurisy, and in such a way that one fills the vessel with hot water or cold water in which there are convallable herbs.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the vacuum administered with fire is thus:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	And it should be two fingers wide and half a palm in depth, with the tip bent towards the middle like for piercing an arrow, so that if she hits the artery, the patient will not bleed on putting on the member;
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	And in the middle there should be a cross-shaped nail or iron, to tie a bandage on, and they should be large and small according to the disease and age of those who take them;
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	For the boils of children are different from those of adults, and thin ones than fat ones.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And you must then place this boil on the limb:
empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	Take a candle made of wax or linen and put it inside the boil through the handle that is inside the boil, so that the light comes to the bottom of the boil, and does not burn the patient.
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	and then put it on the limb, and let your two fingers be above the wound that we have said about, so that when you take it off, if there is vapor coming out, and you remove the boil.
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	and take off the linen in the same way, and reapply it frequently, if you have need.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	In the wound that is managed for chest pain, if it is full of fever, do not have a wound or an abscess, and are treated only when it is full of fever, and placed on the limb alone;
et c’est li forme:	and it is the form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	There are no treatments applied only to the gums and skin, such as incisions or stitches, like it is done for broken bones;
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	and in the nostrils of horses, as well as of dogs and mules, and similar animals;
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	and the quality of the user is such that when you find wounds that are in clean and clear water without risk of infection, then take them;
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	And let them tie up the hair with a warm water dressing, until they become familiar, and have nothing in their stomachs;
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	and then let them bind a vein and apply pressure, and rub the member until it becomes red, and apply poultices;
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	and when they are smooth and have healed, if it is possible to apply a tourniquet, then apply it, because this is most effective.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If not, lift the limb from an anchor point, and then to water, very well, and then inspect it;
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	and if the limb is healed too late after applying poultices, then apply a moist linen strip soaked in cold water, and put it on, until the poultices are dried.
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	And if they are multiplied, he puts upon them vitriol crushed or vinegar, or similar things, until they are stung.
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	Or, to heal the cold spots on the skin, you put moistened snowflakes or peeled-off flesh there, and let them dry so that they will stop now;
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	And if you have more of the same thing needed, then take other poultices.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	And if the poultices will not take hold, then rub the skin of the wound with fresh blood or prick an arrow so that the pus comes out, and then put it on, and at once as soon as they feel the wound, they dry.
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And when you see that they are draining, then powder some aloes and sawdust, or ashes on a little bit, if it will now take hold.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	The Book of Injuries begins.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, for restoring fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Learn well, dear son, that the fire cautery is a matter so rare and unknown, that no one has ever seen it in any of the old books, nor have they read anything about it.
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	and for this reason the art is rare in our land, because I have never found any good one.
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	and I know nothing, except that by the knowledge of the ancient books, where I have studied so much that I have treated the art, and through experience, and by the habit of my life.
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	and I have here described what is contained in this chapter, and condensed it at the end, and have shown clearly the forms of the instruments that must be used, as I did in these two preceding chapters.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is therefore necessary that we say in the prologue of this book about the sums of speech and the chapters or where the wise man puts his understanding, and keeps silent for so long that those who have experienced it will learn and acquire this noble art, and teach others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	I say that when breakage or dislocation or torsion or seizure comes to anyone, it is fitting to hasten to heal the sick person from one side and the other, unless any remedy is available, for weakness of body, or illness, or old age;
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois;	or if his teeth are very bad, or too cold;
et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre;	and when he consumes cold meats, that is to say cold joints, char of fish and fowl, and does not drink wine, nor eats any fatty foods, and does not stuff himself too much with meat which fills the veins with blood, until you have doubt about an abscess or inflammation in the limb;
si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	if the sick person has used the first treatment.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	When the broken bones begin to heal, it is fitting that the patient be nourished with foods that cause great swelling, such as those which have viscosity, just like bread cooked in water, and ris, and testes, and piez, and pance de vaiche, and oefz, and fish, fresh ones, and large wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For swelling caused by this nourishment appears sooner and happens more quickly than the break itself.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	And know that the bones of old men and aged people cannot be well healed or soldered according to their nature due to the dryness of the members, nor those who are too soft, as the bones of small children;
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant;	but a remedy can be found in crushing the large bones that have become hard and joined the limb together, until they strengthen as they were before;
et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	and this should be nourished with great foods, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And you know that fractures are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	But the fracture of the head is different from the fracture of the leg or foot, and I will tell you in this chapter all kinds of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	Because there are fractures that occur at the joints, and others caused by cutting, as if with the length of a pinhead to write.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And when there is a fracture with an open wound, and a fracture with a small split or crack.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And every kind should have its own instrument and proper equipment in restoration, according to what the memory brings with it;
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	and it is known that the fracture of the bone occurs because the bone is twisted, and opens well by force, and happens near the pressure of the hand;
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	And when there is no curvature or bend at the shoulder joint, and the patient does not feel great pain.
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	But it can still have curvature, or a crack, or a small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If it is not necessary to move your hand, but put on medicines that come after this, and then tighten now subtlety.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	And says that the fracture that is in the arm, and are the two parts of the joint, they must now be put back equally, so that the abscess comes out.
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	and if the abscess bursts, he must let it dry for one day, until the abscess is smoothed out.
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces;	then he puts it equal to the muscle that you can easily and surely apply pressure to, and says that the restoration of this is lighter than the restorations of those where there are pieces.
puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	The patient must then bind himself, as it is fitting after this.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	And if in the bone there are broken pieces, then take out two parts, as it is either by hand or by foot, or by little fingers, or by two cords, or one cord and by hand;
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	and put the limb according to its natural figure, so that when the parts of the broken member are missing, repair them by all means as much as possible on each side, and make sure that through your work there is no new injury or pain for the patient;
et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	and put both joints of the bone in the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien:	And let it feel good in your hand if you think it is not quite right:
si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	If the dressing is applied perfectly, and not too tightly strained or pressed so that they are subjected to hot and painful contractions in their work, as we have wanted many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	And when the limb is at a standstill, instruct the patient to hold it still, neither when awake nor asleep, neither turning, nor in any other manner.
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	and take care that the limb is securely fixed so that it does not feel any pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	For when it feels no pain, they are not at a standstill, and rather should be placed in such a position that they do not feel any pain.
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	and be careful that it is placed correctly, lest twisting occurs when it is restored.
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	and the qualities of the broken limb are as I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	The part of the body that is broken is different in size and form.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans:	For there are small limbs, such as arms and shoulders and similar ones:
si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	so it is necessary to wrap a linen cloth of waxed and subtle thread;
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe:	and those that are large, such as thighs and knees:
si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	so it is necessary to wrap with a wide and hard cord, because the wide cords embrace the entire large limb, and compress it evenly from all parts, so that there is no gap;
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	then tie around with light bands, three turns or four, according to the limb, and tighten your hand all over the cord, then go to the top of the break and tighten less, so that the break will slowly move away a little.
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	And soften the joint little by little, so that you pierce a great part of the healthy flesh, then take another ligament, and turn back towards the broken limb;
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	then go back to the lower part of the break, and tighten it gently, neither too tightly nor too loosely, as we have said in the first rule above;
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	then put rags of linen or bandages between the ligatures, so that it is all even, then bind everything from above with a strip, and then put your arrows well made on it, if there is no abscess or inflammation.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	And if it has inflammation or abscess, then put a soothing substance on the abscess, which will bring out the inflammation, and let it stay like that for some days;
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	Now strain upon the arteries, and let them be of a heavy chain, or of a fust wood, or of palm splinters, and they should be according to this figure:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	but it is fitting that the artery that one places on the break should be slightly larger and wider than the others;
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	and so long as it is necessary to the limb whether small or large;
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	then strain the arteries in the same way as you did with the first ligature, then tie above with a thread of linen, just like on the first ligature over the break.
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins;	the tighter you tighten it, the less so.
et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	and it is fitting that the thread should be smooth, not too thick nor too thin, and of fine linen.
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	For the head of the shoulder, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is wounded by the arrowheads after the bandage is applied to their wounds, then put soaps of linen or wool under them, so that they do not bleed.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with a fracture, and the nerves are broken, I will tell you the cure after this.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not advisable to strain or pull apart all the broken limbs on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	For when the limbs are large, it is not advisable to put in stents unless after five days or seven, or according to your safety following a cautery.
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion:	and thus the way of the ancient embalmers for restoring fractures, dislocations, and twists:
et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	and so you take flour that is kept by the walls of the mill, and mix it with much egg, and make this confection, not too clear nor too thick, and use it, because this is the common manner of the embalmers restoring fractures in many ways, especially for women and small children, since it is neither too hot nor too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion:	Another manner of embalmers restoring fractures, dislocations, and twists:
pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.;	Prepare the cautery and antidotes and oil and gum Arabic and mustard, for X.
mirre et aloes, ana V З.;	Mirror and aloes, for V.
alechil VIIII З.;	alce (or alchen) of the seventh degree, X.
et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef;	and make powder, and mix with honey and water.
se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	if the complexion of the person is hot, then use this plaster, because it has good composition, and restores broken bones quickly, and saves many lives.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion:	Another kind of plaster that is worth its weight in gold.
pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.;	Prepare mustard and valerian, for X.
mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.;	Mirror and aloes, 77 times.
acaice VI З.;	Aconitum 77 times.
bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Boil Armenian X, and pound well, and congeal with water or honey, and administer.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure:	Another method for emplastery with joints and after removing their bones, it calms the following pain, and uses the bone to cut the fracture.
pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Apply a new ointment, and mold it in ashes and oil cooked, and put on the limb.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	Plaster casts do not restore the joint, but they are good for soothing abscesses and properly healing pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez:	Another method of emplastery that restores broken bones:
pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Apply leaves of dried fig and earthy leaves, together pounded, and make emplastery.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another way of plaster for restoring the break in the bone and to alleviate the remaining abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie;	Take root of valerian, chamomile, violet flowers, wheat flour from each one;
et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	and crush and mix with wine, and apply to the members being warmed up, mixing it with moist coriander water or cold water, and use.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another way to treat with more force than the first, when an abscess comes back to restore the limb.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie;	Take roots of valerian, and seeds of flax, balsam, meadowsweet, and licorice, and flowers of violet and chamomile from each one;
et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	and crush and mix with salt water or sweet water, or with wine, according to the heat of the member, and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Iporcus writes in his book that you should not put oil and wax on the broken limb to restore it, except for this method alone, and he says that it should be between too dry and too damp.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems that one must place the broken limb above, to restore, things dry and warm, like mirrors and ointments and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor:	Another way to apply a poultice that values injury and pain:
pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Take the hairs from the shaved and bald, or take those of the bird, and venom, and cut them equal, and break them, and make it an embalming paste and bind with a thread.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu;	And then lay the bone loose a little bit, and watch that the patient does not feel any pain, or that he is not troubled by his own bones.
si ne lou deslie par mains jors.	if you do not lay it loose by hands.
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant;	And if pain comes to the limb, or it pricks, with rest or swells, if you hasten and let it go, and remove now the embalming paste.
et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	and take a light drapery, and a sponge of moist sea water, and plunge into the water, and lift up the limb, until the itching ceases, and the pain is appeased.
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	After that, let the limb rest for an hour, then put it under a clean cloth, moistened in water or oil rose, and bind it up with a bandage, until you are sure of the abscess.
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant;	and rest the inflammation in the limb, and may be cured of pain, then resume subtle incision, and a little emplaster, and do not strain it too hard as before.
et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	and subtly until it is cured.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	If you see that there is an abscess on the cheek and redness and pain and swelling it has set in all over, and you have to apply plaster and tie it up again if it happens again, as you did with the first part.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII;	And if the limb does not come to an end as we have said, do not release it more than after three days or four or five or seven.
et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	and never let it remain for twenty days, as we see, until the fracture heals and the swelling approaches.
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant;	And therefore you must hold it tighter first, and swell its flesh, just as I have said before;
et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	and if you see the shoulder drying more than necessary, know that this will not come to anything;
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	the disease arises from hot water then, every time you dislocate it, and this happens to everyone at least once a day, and also later.
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement:	therefore cut off the swelling of the member, and make haste to do what the foolish barber does, which will leave the limb twisted.
c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	this is bad, and if it's caused by fear, and I see nothing else but to loosen and set it right.
des diverses manieres de brisure	of various kinds of breaks
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	There are many kinds of breaks, and diverse forms, and the causes are predetermined;
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust;	for it has fractures that are caused by the percussion of a spear, and the collarbone is broken all along the bone just below where it is embedded in the bone, as when hit or struck.
et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	and for this reason it is called this kind of fracture "haicheure".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»;	Where the spear strikes the bone from above to pierce it, and is called this kind of fracture "absolute".
et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	and there are two types of wounds for these two fractures, large or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if it has been pierced by a thrust, or a cut, or from the bone of a stone, or from a blow on the bone of a stone, or similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if it has an ongoing fracture that approaches just below the skin where it is under the bone, or above the bone, and this injury is big or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	And if the wound is closed in the bone with as much subtlety as we sew, and there is a small split, and for this reason it is called this fracture "capillary".
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres;	and if the wound made or by striking with iron or stone, or by falling, and pushes in a piece of bone into it, and its hairs are as they do when the cautery is applied to the cauterian (heater);
si entre li piere dedens.	if the stone goes inside.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	and this happens more often to those who have moist bones under their head, like that of a child;
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles;	and happens in all these kinds of fractures where small pieces are discharged like dust;
et je em parlerai en son leu.	I will speak for him.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And know all kinds of breaks by removing them, and investigating, and by the corruption that is above.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The similarity of hair is known through this: when you discover the bone, and you stroke upon it, if the break is opened.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of the break, be careful for accidents in the patient, and if you see no evil accident, such as vomiting of bile, loss of intellect, swelling, paleness, fever, and the eyes protruding and reddening, and other similar symptoms, then it cannot be cured without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see an impossible accident, and you expect a recovery, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	When the patient comes to you for the first time, and it is in winter, it is fitting to remove the bone in front of the 14th day before the moon.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if this is the case, hastening to remove the bone in front of the 7th day instead will bring about corruption of the tissue underneath the bone, and come the accidents that we have stated.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi:	And if the bone fracture comes just to the wound that covers the brain, you should cut the fractured part in this way:
et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	Instruct the patient to press firmly on the head and discover where under the skin you can find it, in all ways that you can, and with the shape of the wound as soft as possible; for when the blood stops coming out from discovering the bone, or the abscess closes, he must use what is necessary, and it is so that you fill the space with wet draplings soaked in olive oil.
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc;	And then make the wound rest until the abscess closes, and be sure that there is no more blood coming out.
puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige:	Then begin to remove the bone, and this is done in two ways of work.
l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	one way is to copy the narrow cut on the front, and that's the shape:
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then you must break the other limb more than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde;	And the second manner is that you have many different knives, some are three-edged and others long, and they should be sharp and made of iron.
et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	and when you apply it lightly, so that you do not hit the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os;	And if the bone is hard and tough, it is wise to pierce it through so that you can administer knives with care, neither cutting too deeply nor piercing further than the bone of the joint, and leaving on the edge of the point a margin or circle, so that the point does not go beyond the bone.
et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test;	and it is wise to have many, so that each one comes in its proper place of the joint space, so that you have knives for all tests.
et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	and this is the form of the three kinds of tarses:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez;	The ones that pierce through the bone when it is broken are pierced with one tare (tongue) on the bone, and turned to your two hands so you know when the bone has been pierced.
puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures;	Then put the tare in another place a little after that, and do it all around, then cut at the incisions the space of the bone between the punctures, and do it more subtly than you can, and lightly, as we have said, until you touch the bone with your hand, or on any other tool you have, such as pliers.
et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	and be careful that you do not touch the brain or the spongy part.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	And when you have pierced the bone and treated it, so that you can retrieve what is left in the bone after another instrument like an incisor, but it should be more subtle and more refined than the other instruments.
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens;	but if it leaves nothing of the small bones, or no scutes, if the bone is lightly attached to other instruments;
puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	then treat the wound of tenons and ligatures that we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus;	And other methods, if what the Galenians say is true, which is more accurate;
et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	and it is much stronger, and this is his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first that you uncover a part of the bone, at this place or where there is a fracture open, so when you have uncovered that part, you will put below the head of this incision, lens-shaped, because it is this shape:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os;	And do not cut from one side, and if the part is diseased in two places, so that the cutting is towards the bone;
puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	Puis fier de petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l'os tout entor, et te donne bien en garde de la toile qui est dessous.
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	When she is irritated to the bone, cutting it lightly, because the bone causes great pain and fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the break of the bone does not penetrate to the skin, and the bone is broken only above, and there are small pieces, so it covers again that roughness, and removes the scales with a subtle rasp that you must have in various quantities, in order to fit each one as comfortably as possible, according to the work and figure of the break.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you choose before many raspers, and after more subtle ones, and do not stop doing this until it is well done.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement;	For each other type of hair cutting and subtle breakage, it is necessary to consider the cause according to its direction;
et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	And this is something that cannot be replied by one who has put his knowledge in this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	And if the sac is uncovered, it is necessary to take out the drapery of linen, according to the quantity of the wound, and wet it in rose oil, and put it on the wound;
puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil;	Then take another cloth doubled in II or in III, and soak it in wine and oil rosary, and put it on the first cloth;
et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	And do this more lightly than you can, so that you don't weigh too heavily on it, then administer over the second cloth, and do not strain it further than when it only reveals the wound.
et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses;	And leave it thus for one day or two, until the abscesses have subsided, then remove it, and administer medicine as with willow roots, flour of fenugreek, powder of incense, and aromatics, and similar things;
et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	And make powder of these things, and put it on the wound, and administer as usual medicines with rubbing.
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice;	And beware that the wound becomes infected and clean, lest you do not leave the ointment on it, or do not let it assemble with a bow, for when the bow assembles upon the cloth of the brain, so does the corruption and pestilence, and it brings great evil to the patient;
car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	for when you put up a sharp instrument on the skin, it freezes below.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Precaution first then, if no other accidents come to the patient as we have said, because it is doubtful without doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	And if the blackness does not come from the medicine that we have put on it, and the virtue has some effect, then you should take a piece of honey, three parts of rose oil, and one part of adhesive, and apply them on the sharp instrument;
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then apply a remedy in ways of treatments until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os;	Things that are never broken into two parts, except for one part by itself, because they are two bones.
et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	And this one is cartilaginous and does not break, unless it is bent or twisted, and then it heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	And if one of the two parts is broken, then it is necessary to put your little finger or bony protrusion into the fracture and set the break in place according to its natural shape.
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And do it lightly, and take care that the patient does not feel pain due to your action.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	If the break is in the upper part of the neck, and it cannot come down to its place, so that you put an equal weight on the head of a straw a little bit thick.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	And if the break is in two parts, then repeat this process, and hasten to restore it the first day, if you can;
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	If it is not so, after the seventh or tenth day, when the abscesses are calmed down, then boil the head with new linen cloths, if the breakage is in one part.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est;	Where you pour another of another kind, if the breakage is;
et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	and let the cloths be so large that they fill the wounds of the head.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And said a restorer that we must moisten the coverings in butter, and move each person daily.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin;	I do not think that is quite right, but it should be moistened in the composition of honey and miller's powder;
puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	then let the cloth remain, until the bone is firm and the cartilage hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi;	And at no time pour in onions of goose into it instead of cloths, and if the wound is covered up and kept still, and holds the breakage together, and blows gently on him;
or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	The instruction to do this task
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	And if an abscess comes to the head while you are working, apply hot or wet cotton in oil rose, or in a poultice of dayquil.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	And if an abscess does not come, then apply plaster by default, made of flour of sesame, and powder of incense, mixed with honey, then place it on light caustic, and do not tie the nose.
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	and if the nasal fracture is small, and it has been broken into little pieces, then draw out with suitable instruments what can be removed, then close the wound, and apply to cure wounds that require tarring or soldering, as does plaster and ointments.
et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if there is no wound inside the nose, then apply a cure for wounds, and put sticks of wood in until it heals.
de la routure de la mandibule	About the jaw fracture
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jaw is fractured under, and there is no wound to prevent it, and the fracture is only present, without breakage in others, if one notices a slight swelling.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide;	It is fitting, if the breakage occurs in the right hand, that you put your thumb into the mouth of the patient;
et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	and if the breakage occurs in the left jaw, put your thumb of the right hand into the mouth and gently push the break inside, and cover it with the other hand to keep it in place.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the jaw is displaced upward by two parts, it is fitting that you extend the second part so that they are even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double;	And if the movement of the teeth has occurred, or a fracture, then bind with a thread of gold or silver or silk, and put a layer of wax on the broken jaw and a double cloth.
et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	and put on the outer cloth an estee well-made, or a piece of leather equal, long and wide according to the jaw, and bind it there with what you can, and instruct the patient to rest, and serve him light victuals.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet;	And if you see that the figure changes, let him lie on his back every day, and then put it in place what was changing.
et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote;	and put plaster on it, made of powder from the mill with abundance of oil or flour of sesame, after you have extracted the fat.
et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez;	and put on a lighter layer of plaster, and if the plaster sets, and the patient's condition does not change, let him remain so until he is healed.
maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	often healing occurs within three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if an abscess comes on a joint, then follow what we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee;	And if it has a break and wound together, reward no piece of bone that is exposed;
si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	if subtlety of the extracted bone causes swelling.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, then enlarge it according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When you have extracted all those bones and it remains empty for a while, cut the wound, if it is wide, and apply plaster according to what is suitable, in order to prevent infection, until it is safe.
de la forcele	of the gallbladder
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres:	The force breaks multiple times before, over the shoulder, and the breakages occur in three different manners:
ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer;	or if it is broken and split into two parts, and it heals faster.
ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	or where there are breaks with wounds.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie;	And the treatments are when the breaks occur with wounds, that you have two remedies, so that one of them tugs on the shoulder joint where the break is.
et li autres estende lou col vers la partie;	and the other stretches the neck towards the part;
puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	then puts the break into your two hands, so that the form is as it should be, and there is no appearance or swelling.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit;	And if you have to extend it further, then place the round spear of cloth or linen over the shoulder of the patient.
et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	and hold and lift the swelling, and tie the spear with your hand, so that you put equal pressure on the break, as it requires.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	If you cannot treat the head of the fracture outside, because it is coming in full, then it is fitting that the patient lies on his back and puts a bolster under the shoulder; and gives to the minister's shoulder downwards, so that the bones of the fracture are lifted.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus;	And then instruct the break to be on your right hand, and if you find any dead parts, it is fitting that you cut them off;
et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as;	and throw away the lighter pieces, and if the bone cannot be joined together due to any swelling, if you cut at one of your joints;
mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	but place over the swelling this instrument, to guard the wound;
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre;	And it seems like a spoon, and is not hair, and is as large as it needs to be, according to the size of the bone and the skill of the worker.
et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	And has two heads, just like you see it, and one is large, and the other is narrow, just as is the route of the wound that you made when treating the bones.
et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	And when you are certain of the thickness of the abscess, count the wound, and if the route is small, then doubt the thickening of the abscess, apply the wound with drapes and tents, according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if an abscess comes to a head, apply it in oil of rose and in ashes and in wine, and put on.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;	The binding of the bone, when it is against wounds and swelling, is that you place the bone under the plaster of powder from the mill and of horse manure, and put lightweight stones above, and a spear below the axle, if need be;
puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre;	Then take a very long bandage of one palm's width, then place two drapes over it on the stumps, and tie it.
puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;	Then take a small needle of three to four fingers' width and long, and tie it around the bandage so that the head of the bandage is on top.
et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide;	and place the needle on the break, and turn the bandage up on the neck, and under the healthy side, and under the sick side.
et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;	and tie from each side, and when you see that the ligature holds the break in place, and you see clearly that the needle does not move over the broken bone, then reward it every day, and when the ligature is looser, tighten it.
et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut;	and make the patient lie on his back, and put him on a small pillow under the head, to lift the shoulder joint up.
si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors;	if the broken collarbone is alleviated by adjusting the shoulder joint, or you tie the arm to the neck, and do not untie it in case of a bad accident, for twenty days.
puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez;	then resume the plastering if you see it necessary, and bind and leave him in that state until he is restored.
et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	and she is restored after twenty-eight days, and fewer than any others.
de la brisure de l’espaule	Of a shoulder break
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement;	It rarely happens that a shoulder break or separation causes him to lose his strength, and it is only through touch.
si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	If it appears according to the form of the breakage, and you reset it according to its natural shape, in all the ways that you can;
puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double;	Then put on the limb powder from the mill with much salt and fine dust, and puts over it a double cloth;
puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment;	Then puts on a broad and subtle spearhead, a little broader than the shoulder, and smooths out the spearhead in any spot of the shoulder, so that the speareth cuts equally;
et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor;	and then tightens it firmly to a great band, so that the spearhead does not move from its place, and watches the ligament every day;
et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit;	and every time it is moistened, so tightens the band, and puts back the spearhead if it has moved from its place, and lays the patient on his chest;
et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en XXV.	And the shoulder is reset after twenty days or twenty-five.
Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	And when these numbers are completed, if the dislocation is corrected, and you are sure, because it's not the bone that is put back in place lightly.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	If a piece of the bone is torn away and points downwards under the skin, it should be pulled out upwards, and the bone, and do what we have said in the breaking of the abscess.
de la brisure dou pis	of the break of the foot
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc;	The flesh is never broken at the point of the dislocation, but it happens sometimes;
mais il brise sovent au defuer.	but it breaks often before.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in the middle, if it inclines towards the underside, and the patient feels great pain, and lack of warmth, and swelling, and by chance vomit blood, and expose the broken marrow, and the flesh feels bad.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient;	And the restoration is such that the patient lies on his back, and you place an armpit between the shoulders, then press the shoulders, and assemble the two breast bones with your hands, and be subtle in placing them in all ways, so that the figure of the bone becomes as it should;
puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve;	Then put on splints and poultices above the subtle bone of salt, or a lighter fist, and lift it in an iron band, and bind it to the broken bone, so that it does not move;
et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint;	and round the ligature to the back, and tighten it immediately, and reward each hour the wound, and if it swells, tighten the strait;
et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures;	and if it seems wise to loosen the bandage, because of corrosion or itching that comes to the patient, or pain or abscess, if you hasten and loosen it, and scrape off the poultice, and address what is coming from it in ways of cure;
puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	then scrape off the poultice, and tighten the strait until it is safe.
de la brisure des costes	of the fractured ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses;	The broken ribs do not happen from the large ones after the back and in the head inside, they bend only because they are crooked;
et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	and feel quite good with the inquiry as it should.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the remedies are that you put equal the break, as it is fitting.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then apply plaster and bind with a stick if you have need.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile;	And if the ribs break are declining inside, the patient feels great pain and puncture, just as with pleurisy, because the bone points at the membrane;
et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	and they have pains, and swellings, and vomiting great plant of blood, and it is a source of ill health, and the old men have put great strength.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if those who say it is proper to administer meat that inflates the belly, in order to break the fracture away from the bone.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not do this unless pus comes out of the wound.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it has come, then the blood.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison;	And they say that one should apply windbags on the limb, to cut off the flow, and it seems reasonable;
toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	All sorts of diseases occur from air entering the body due to weakness.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And they say that one should cover the limb with a linen cloth soaked in hot oil, and put tourniquets between the ribs to straighten the joint, then treat the patient with the cure of bleeding, meat, and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac;	And if the patient suffers great pain from the bone piercing the lung, and there is doubt about it, then it is advisable to break open the lung of the broken rib, and it is wise to put some instrument to guard the wound.
et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And thus one must cut the bone, and treat lightly, and then sew both cheeks of the wound, if it is great, and apply plaster to heal until he is cured.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu;	And if an abscess comes to a head, then put on moist cloths in oil rose, and put on the wound.
et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And treat while the wound heals of that which it is necessary for the abscess, and apply ointment to the place where it must be, until he is cured.
de la brisure dou col	of the broken collarbone.
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie;	There is no break as a result of the bone of the neck, and little happens if it bends;
et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	and also at the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when it happens that there is a fracture and you see whether he will be healed or not, if you see his hands softened and swollen and dead, and they cannot move nor stretch, and when you press them with an needle, if they do not feel.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Those who have died from more severe dislocations, and if they are silent and feel well when their joints are strained and not moved, know that the bone joint is saved, and that patients recover, if it is put in treatment.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit;	And if such a thing comes to the spine of the back, and you see whether it is healing or not, take care that the joints are softened, and if the accident is in the hands, and on the back, one feels a violent motion and emission against will.
et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	and when one has it set upon his belly, he feels a violent emission against will.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when it is put back onto its own back and it wants to be healed, but cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz:	It is mortal.
si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	if he does not work properly in his treatment.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not come to pass, then it is a lighter thing.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez;	And the cure says that if you reward him if he has an abscess hot, put oil of rose or oil from mutton fat on the spine, until it is pacified.
puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer;	Then puts on one of the plasters comforting and drying, and binds it with a bandage, and instructs the patient to rest;
et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And does not lie down on that part where he feels the pain, until it is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur;	And if some bones are cracked, then it is advisable to cover the wound;
et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then set the bone, and assemble the two lips of the wound, if they are large, with a suture, and apply ointment made from pitch, until it is healed;
et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier;	and if the head of the bone is fractured, which are called "head of the knee", then put your left hand in your pouch and place it equal to the other hand on your palm, then put the plaster and the stile on, if you have need;
puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Instruct to bind the patient, and if it has swollen bones, then cut above them, and extract the bone, and treat the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the break of the shin bone
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief;	There is a chance that the shinbone will be broken, and if it has, then do not worry too much for only a little alleviation at the head.
et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	And stretch to the length, and pull down to the joints, and it will come to the patient with pain in the limb, aching, and swelling.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure;	And if there is healing, then stretch your hand over it, until you are above the fracture.
et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li;	and mark how the bone and joint are.
et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And if the fracture is only in the head, then mark this bone and make it even until it has taken on its natural shape.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the fracture is long, or it inclines towards the inside, then have the patient lie on his stomach, until the restoration of that fracture has been made known.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve;	And when you have set it even, put on the plaster, then put on an arrow made of wood or bone, and strain the break so that it does not move;
et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	and apply the plaster on both sides of the cost, until the wound is even.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And instruct the patient to lie on his healthy side, or on his back.
