Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit;	And if an abscess comes up, do not touch it, until the abscess is allayed, and put on what we have said before.
et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident;	and then return to the restoration, and restrain it as necessary, if there is no further injury.
et c’est li maniere.	And this is the way.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of a shoulder dislocation
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres:	The joint is that which is between the shoulder and the cut of the arm, and if it is broken, one must restore it according to one of the two methods:
dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	Dont one is to take a large iron rod, according to this form:
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege;	And tie the two shoulders together, and fasten them up high, and sit the patient on a stool;
puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval;	then lift the broken limb to the place of the bone, until it comes to an anvil, and attach a strap of iron to it, then fasten on any weighty thing that is given to him to endure.
puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	then put the linen over the broken limb in its proper place, so that the break may return to its proper position.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a II ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout I liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And another way is that you serve the patient on his bed, and tie his hand to his neck; then command two servants to pull up the part above the breakage with their hands, and the others below by all its joints, and stretch out each one to their side.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction is more difficult, then tie the joint below the breakage, and above the breakage, and stretch each one of the servants to their side.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure;	And if the break is close to the head of the shoulder, so that you may put a middle rope under the anvil, and the other towards the back, under the break;
et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute;	and also if the fracture occurs in the heel, so it is necessary to put a light ligature on it lightly, without labor, until the fracture is even with its joint, and with its skin.
puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	then put the fracture back in place if it seems right to you, and hold tight, so that pus does not come.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez;	And if pus comes, do not hold tight for seven days, and put a moist cloth on it in a clean place with rose oil, until the pus is calmed.
puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein;	then hold tight, and the way to hold it is such that you put the plaster on the fracture, then reassemble the arm on the shoulder, and place your hand on the shoulder or on the breast.
et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	and tie the bandage and restrain under the shoulder, and on the arm, so that the arm is in place, unless any part of it impedes its movement, or if the bone has moved.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part;	And if you doubt that the bone does not move, then use a splint, and place two larger and stronger splints on either side of the break, with one space between each splint, so that each splint spans the break three times from each part;
puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	then tighten the splints, as I said at the beginning of this chapter on the break, stronger and less loosely.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit;	And if you see how the splint is applied and tightened, as we have said, when restoring the injured member, and you doubt whether to leave the abscess alone for seven days, as we have said;
puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	the patient should look at each of them every three days to see if the swelling is going away, or if it will come back to life, and the pus cannot come out from the member because it is too strained.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If the advice, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac;	But if such accidents do not happen, then only to free the man after three days or more, and let the patient sleep on his back, and put his hands under his stomach;
et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens;	and on the shoulder put a cloth in the shape of an arrow, equally plain, and look at each one every hour of the day or night, whether the figure of the broken limb is fixed or not, or if the ligaments are softened.
si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz;	if it happens by the power of medicine, and you give him the meat that we have placed before him, in such a way that the meat is first finely chopped;
et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	and when he comes to try again, so it is large.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout;	and it is customary that the shoulder and the leg should be reset in forty days from the start.
et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	and therefore one must untie and administer baths and medicine to ease the pain.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	If the bowstring is twisted and stuck, so that it cannot be untied for one or two days.
de la brisure du bras	Of a broken arm
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet;	the arm is composed of two bones, which are called the "fossicle", one small and that one which forms the pouch.
et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi;	and the other is large, and it is under, towards the small bone;
par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	by chance break the large ossicle alone, or the small one, and by chance join them together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations;	When the bones are broken, restoration is light, and healing.
et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	and when the great bones are broken, so is healing, and it is more grievous than when they were broken at first.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If it is only the small bone that broke alone, you must gently extend it, and set it even.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort;	And if that's a great fracture, then one must strain harder;
et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor;	and extend the splint above the cussion, and tighten the pouch of his hand higher than others, and the bones should be set lower than others as well, and let the patient cross his own limbs, and the cussion in front of him shall be raised higher so that the patient may suffer no labor;
puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	then extend the minister's thumb to the lower part of his arm or at the joint, and another minister on top.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then put him in the mirror, according to his best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if in the breakage there are pieces, each one put back in its place; and if it has no matching part that can be held together, and you cannot restore it to its proper place, then make a bone cast, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler;	And if with a break there is an injury, I have spoken about it to the singular doctor;
si pren la cure.	if they take the treatment.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz;	And if in the beginning of the restoration there are abscesses that form pus, I apply a cloth made from ghee oil and white beeswax, so that it is neither too hard nor too soft.
et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	and the cloth applied above is done subtly, until the abscesses are appeased.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres;	And then I take out the ghee, and I apply the plaster of powder milled with a lot of wine, because I put the stitches, and so that the stitch from the break is made stronger, and a little bit larger than the others;
et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions:	And you know that he must have six stitches or more in wounds or injuries.
soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II;	Whether the fracture is in one of the bones or two;
et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre;	And tie more tightly above the fracture than in other places, and every day less when removing, as I said at the beginning of this chapter.
et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres;	And let the dressings that are on top of the fracture be soft and moist, not hard or rough.
et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	And let the strings that hold it in place be made of linen, not too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And reward the limb and the joint after some time.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez;	And if some other misfortune comes to the limb, such as itching that is coming to the limb, it is fitting to raise the limb in hot water until the itching is relieved.
et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	And let the limb not remain still.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then tighten the binding, and if the ligaments are loosened and the bones deviated, it is like a similar case, so address it.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if the swelling cannot come to the limb because it is too tightly bound, so that it can be freed, it is fitting to loosen it a little, and let it remain for some days, until the swelling subsides, and then tighten.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things that we have said will come to the patient, then do not bind or release anything within twenty days.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos;	and asks the person to place his hands on his neck, and if their necks are even, then he will guard against movement and digitation, and let him sleep on his back.
et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	and knows that this fracture is restored in thirty days or thirty-five days, and by chance in twenty days, according to the composition and complexion of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	of the hand fracture
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	know that at the back of the hand there is little fracture, and it often comes to nothing but inflammation many times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement;	And when the finger of the hand is broken or bent, it is advisable for the patient to tie a cross around himself and sit upright in the same manner.
puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint;	then places his hand over the stretched joint and stretches out the broken bones, and sets equal the joints of the fingers, until they are well joined.
et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu;	And applies the plaster and dressings; if no abscess comes, then he puts a stethoscope according to its quantity.
et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	and it is wrapped in an iodized cloth of linen.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie;	And if the break is at the joint of the arm near to the belly of the hand, then he makes a splint of cloth, and instructs the patient to wrap his broken hand.
et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	and then the wrapping of a length of cloth, and so fastens the bandage as large as the plant of his hand, and wraps it, just as is needed.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	If the fracture is in the finger, then it is advisable to put a splint above and another below the palm, so that the hand is straightened and upright, and then bind him all around with the hand, and secure the ligature between the two.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient;	And if the break comes to no one of us of the two, and it is swollen, then he lets it be even, just as is needed.
et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve;	And hold with the plant [i.e. finger or toe] and if you see so put a small stake straight for lifting the break, and it does not move;
et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés;	And if the break is on other sides such as in the index or one of the others, so that it is even, and the link with the good vein which is after;
ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet;	or you tie them all in the same way as before, whatever value it has, or if you put a stake up, such as a pouched one;
et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	and take care in the restoration and arrangement of the abscess, and heal those who come to you, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	of the shoulder breaks
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier;	The bone of the scapula is often broken, and one can see well when it turns in front and behind;
et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	and let him bind with linen above the fracture, and below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment;	And let the patient sit with his face, then stretch out each minister's linen equally.
et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	and this is when the fracture is set in place against the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the break is close to the root of the shoulder, then there are either one of the ligaments towards the bone, and the others below the break.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval;	and also if it is near the groin, and then so let the linen be tied around the groin, and so let the extension below.
puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	then put the splint upon the bone equally to its two hands, so that it conforms to his natural shape, and then apply plaster, and linen, so that no arrow comes near.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure;	And if there is an abscess like that, let it be allayed then return to your work and to your treatment.
li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	The limb is made in this manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus;	It is necessary that you wrap the limb around the fracture with a bandage doubled in II or III, and keep the swelling, then turn the leg until the heel reaches the root of the nail, and put I long thread between the crotch and the leg, loosening below the knee, and pulling the head of the thread above.
puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe;	then turn the leg and the crotch with the bandage, then put a splint on the fracture, and put another splint on the bone of the leg.
puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure;	then apply the leg eight between the thigh and crotch with soft fabrics to tighten the binding, then begin to tie in a bow of III or IV knots on the fracture.
et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint;	And when you go further up of the fracture, and less it is constricted;
puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet;	Then tie both knees of the cloth that you have poured between the leg and the thigh, and tie three strings that are above, then return below to the head of the cloth, until you find the foot.
et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	and tie it, if it does not move out of its place, then let it stay so, then if there is no swelling or abscess or other sign.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois;	And if it has (swelling), if you separate it, and address the thing that comes, as we have said many times;
et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet;	and if it has pieces of bone that grasp, then you must sew them, if possible;
et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer;	and if we cannot, then it is proper to break down the limb, and treat it with force.
et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	as has been said, so that the patient may be healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras;	And sometimes is broken the chest in such a way as when we insert stitches, just like in the shoulder and arm.
toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	and will not close again in the same way the patient has been restored.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And so it is known that the cube can be restored in three or four days, or slightly more or less, according to the diversity of the complexion.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the groove of the gallbladder
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	They say that in the hollow of the groin there is often a break but it bends many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	But if it breaks, then it's not just a cut or a rupture, but rather an opening or a wound, which causes all pain and feels painful.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet;	and the restoration is as if we make equal those things that are broken at their two ends, so they may be assembled and put together when possible.
puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant;	then apply plaster, and put a rounded arrow around it, if necessary; then bind as needed, and after all the arrangements we have said for other fractures, just like the abscess and another similar thing.
si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it happens to anyone of these accidents which they must avoid, until they are healthy.
de la brisure de la jambe	of the leg fracture
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»;	We know that in the leg there are two bones; one is called by the right name "moustelle", and the other is called "fossicle".
et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	And all other fractures come to the arm, and for this is the restoration just like the arm itself, and the wounds are all one; and if both bones are broken together, then turn the leg in all directions.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the subtle bones break, turn in front.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien;	And if the big bone is broken, it causes great pain and you can see it well;
et torne desoz.	and turn downward.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement;	And then apply an extension, and set it equal, and tie the splints equally;
mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere;	But the whole view is necessary, for it is required that if the fracture is ugly and there are many pieces, then the extension should be smaller and lighter.
et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	and in proportion to its worth.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz;	And when you have completed your work, take two strips of cloth that are red and purple in color, and are long from the knee down to the joints.
puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien;	Then tie both ends of the bandage above and below in the middle, so that the leg cannot bend to the right or to the left, and thus it is good.
et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie;	And no one should apply two strips of cloth from the knee down to prevent movement in that joint where there is a wound.
et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident;	And move every day the limb, to see if it has an abscess or another accident.
si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	So that he may be healthy.
de la brisure des os dou piet	of the bone of the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the knee there comes no break, but sometimes when a bone is on its foot it breaks and causes a wound, and in some cases only swelling.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus;	And if he has a broken bone with an exposed bone protruding from another, and you see these bones touching each other, if the patient lies on his side, as if he were walking, and then put now your foot on his side, where the bones are raised, press it so that they come together again in their place.
puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	Then apply plaster and binding on the wound, and place over his belly with a small plate to two exposed bones, then strain him onto the affected limb, afterwards you wrapped in bandages, and other things which you have need.
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three or four days have passed, if you release the bandage, for you will find that the bones are evened out, whether they are broken, or swollen.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main;	And if it has some of the bones broken, so they repair them, just like we said about the bones of the hand;
puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment;	then put an splint on the broken bone according to its length, and so that it is not too big, then place the foot on the table as I have said, and hold fast.
et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet;	and if there are two or three, or more, broken bones, then put on each bone a splint according to its quantity, wrapped in one layer of linen, and hold the table under the foot.
et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	and if it is standing with the head of the table near to the belly of the foot, so that he can hold it well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit;	And be sure not to forget the other things I have said about other broken bones, since we have spoken of them.
et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And treat each injury as it is suitable.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the bone at the finger
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier;	When the bones of a woman's body are broken, so that she grows and swells, then incline her to the part of the back of the head, and hold her behind.
puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto;	then fill the belly of the woman with woolen clothes, and put there just as much as is.
puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto;	then tie up the woman, and lift her back little by little, and thus pull out the wool, until it comes to the opening of her body, and returns the bone with the same amount.
et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor:	and when she wants to urinate, pull out the wool, and when she has urinated, put it back again, and do thus for seven days before.
si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature;	If it is restored the break, and you see, take a vessel of wool, and tie to the puncture a cord, and pour all the vessel into the body.
puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens:	then breathe through the cord formed, until the vessel is blown inside.
la nature si revenra li brisure;	the body will return to the break;
puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then be filled with cotton, and leave it so for some days, until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche;	And when the bone at the elbow of a child or woman is broken, or restored in the same way as we have said for the os of the hazel nut.
et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	and these nearby breaks are not concealed by one who makes his study and practice, and pays attention to my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration:	For the break signifies more opportunities on the right way of restoration:
enten le donques.	and then therefore.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge;	In the phallus, when it is broken, take a goose's neck and swallow the phallus;
puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	then wrap up the bandages around it, and let it remain for three days or more, and he will be cured in a short time.
de brisure avec plaie	of breaks with wounds
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is to be believed that the one who has breaks with wounds, especially if it is great, like the bones of the shoulder or arm or similar ones, will be healed now, if the remedies we have said testify to this.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound is healthy, then apply vitreous (glass) to it, for if you have nothing else, do so again on the same day or the next day, unless an abscess forms.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if an abscess forms, then leave the restoration for the next new day, until the abscess is allayed, and do not touch it or set it again on the third or fourth day, for you will cause a bad accident.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the bone break is found near the joint of the shoulder, it is fitting to tie (or set) you lightly on the tip of your finger with a small extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie;	And if the extension does not have provided for the placement of equal numbers on your hands, when using this instrument made of iron, which has seven fingers or eight, and the length is according to the quantity of the wound;
et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure;	and for that reason is a skill of the barber who must press three or four times, according to what he needs in each wound.
et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	and if it is swollen and small, that when not compressed on the limb above, will not bend at all, and be swollen in front, and large from the middle to the forehead.
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent;	and is called "palanche", because it must be placed above the curved bones of the skull.
et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	and apply it once, as long as it clings, and make the swollen one equal to the other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	But if the break is subtle and the splints cannot well take hold of the bone, it is advised that you copy the head of the bone, until the splints have a good grip.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir;	And if you cannot return the bone, as we have said, then apply it with an instrument suitable for that, such as cutting or sawing.
puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	then retrieve what is stuck in the bone due to roughness and small scratches.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is restored and the patient feels great pain afterwards, know that he is not in his natural place.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit;	If you do it so that it is in its place, then fill the wound with a vinegar-soaked cloth, and this is how one should do it;
et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption;	and put no more on the wound than clay or another substance with oil, lest it bring putrefaction and corruption;
puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure;	then apply stitches until you have restored the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, and cover the entire surface, according to the quantity of the wound, and take good care that the wound is not constricted with the break;
et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois;	and many times they have done this to the foolish man, and brought the patient either death or corruption.
et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	and so let the restraints be softer and more gentle for other breaks.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles;	And if the wound is bad or great, and you doubt that more accidents will come, as we have said, and you find pain in the limb, so it cannot be treated with nails.
mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	but tie him up with ropes and hard bonds, and the limb.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after the first day or the second day that the bow is stuck to the wound, so keep what you put on top of it in all wine, and apply soothing salve for wounds, as a salve tetrafarmacon and similar things.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary that you dislocate the limb twice a day, morning and evening, until it is cooled and cleansed.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the limb be tied in a way that the bow can move freely along its edge lightly.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if every day the wound does not heal, and it only gets worse again with new bowing, see that there are little pieces of bone, for this reason you must want to treat the wound with poultice, and remove all these useless parts that come from the pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	If a fistula comes to the liver, or another kind of corruption, then it is wise that you cure it, according to what he says in his chapter before this.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse;	And when the bone is broken and opens up on the limb, as with the ribs or shoulder blade, and other large joints, do not treat it because many die, but let it heal.
par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues;	if by chance it falls out after twenty or thirty days, then treat the wound, if you can.
et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	and if you cannot, let it be.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	of those who come from the stool (feces).
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre;	We come many times after the health of the break, equally when it is near the joint, and see a bad thing to behold at the figure of the limb;
et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	and by chance, the limbs cannot do their own work naturally.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres:	Take care then if we see that it is fresh;
si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil;	so if the administrator gives medicinal drugs such as aloes, incense, and mirror, and sarcocolle, aconite, and similar other things, so that you do not take any of these things, or all together, and mix with vinegar medicinally or with a lot of wine or with oil;
et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors;	and puts it on the nose in a poultice, and presses well, and does not loosen it with his hands each day;
et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee;	and then it loosens, and begins again, until the knots are pulled out;
ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite;	or you strain on a well-made splint;
car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres;	because the property of the splint is that it pulls out all the swellings from above the limbs;
et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent;	and if the knot is converted into a hardened swelling as hard as stone, and it must be pulled out, if the flesh beneath, and the obvious superficiality appear;
ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	or you remove it to a smooth surface, until it is pulled out, and the treatment until it is healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	A limb which is weak after the garrison.
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes:	When the break in the bone is restored, and it stays after the weak and subtle limbs, for many causes:
de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit;	Because one is because it was tied too tightly, and was not tied as much as it needed to be.
ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre;	or because there is too many ligatures and cannot come the swelling in the member;
ou por multitude d’arosement;	or for multiple swellings;
ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre;	or for too great movements, neither in its hour.
ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	or because it has little blood in his body, and is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui;	And the doctor says that you should make the patient eat, and make his body soft, until there is no swelling in him.
et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce;	and administer a bath, and give joy and relaxation;
puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre;	Now apply the poux to the limb, so that the poux attracts a great swelling, and it often rises with much pain until the swelling subsides from the limb.
et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	and returns to its natural form.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	One tortured limb after the health.
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil:	When the limb is twisted after restoration, and the bones are broken open, and the form of the member is ugly, one should not try to restore its natural shape.
si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre;	if one does not believe the foolish people who say that you must break the limb anew, and many fools have done this in our land.
et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors;	and these works are blamed, and it brings great harm, and by chance one dies.
toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses;	otherwise, if the nodations and tortures are fresh, it is to be preferred that they should be raised with hot water, or herbs are cooked, like those of valerian, roots, and meadowsweet, and similar things;
et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus;	Instruct the doctor to apply a mollifying plaster, just like quailon does well, and take the musk of violets, and mix with fat of geese or olive oil, and apply it on.
ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	Or take greasy figs, and grind them with flour of rye, and similar medicines that soften the pain.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And sometimes the nodal joint is loosened by constant friction and prolonged rubbing with wet hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And move each limb every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement;	And if the twisted bone is old and hardened, like stone, and requires plaster of iron, so that it covers just above the bone, at the subtle incision lightly.
et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	and put cushioning and study in the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	This begins the book of dislocations.
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation comes upon, if it can be now set in place again.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu;	For if one delays, since swelling of the limbs, and by chance, if it is reset with pains.
por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez:	because you do not need to move at all, when it is swollen.
maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors;	many times pain and other pains have been brought on.
toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez;	whenever it happens, if you make the patient healthy again, then leave him alone, until the swelling subsides.
puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	then apply the limb to cold water and oil, then gently reset it, and treat each limb as the treatment comes in its place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have prescribed the chapters for dislocation of the head joint at a price.
des mandibules	of the jawbones.
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres:	and sometimes the jaws are displaced inward, and joint dislocations of both sides occur in two ways:
ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc;	or they have a small bone of their joints, and softening a little.
ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	When they are completely dislocated and hanging down towards the chest, and you cannot hold back their vomit, nor close your mouth, nor keep it inside, they swallow with their tongue along with their speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When small dislocations occur, they return to their original place by multiple movements.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie;	And if it is complete and accomplished, then you should reset it quickly, and do not postpone.
et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars;	and in such a way that the ministers take out the chief from the patient, and pour some powder of mice into one of his hands at the root of the dislocated jaw within the mouth, if the dislocation is two parts;
et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal;	and pour the other two fingers be avoided, for making them even.
et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	and instruct the patient to loosen his jawbones, and move them in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And the mixture is put even, until it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement;	And if it is reset, meaning that the two jaws are assembled together, so they apply hot water and oil, until the dislocation is easily set.
ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	do not force it to return, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens;	and when they are returned evenly, and the mouth of the sick person is closed well with a softening, so you apply moist cloths in a rose oil and beeswax mixture, then bind it lightly with soft ties.
et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules;	and let the sick person sleep on their back, with their shoulders between two cushions, so that they do not move either to the right or to the left, and do not exert themselves more, but take lightly food, until the pains are gone and the jaws are closed.
et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	and then take what he wants lightly, and do not labor over opening the mouth to eat and drink, until the jaw is well closed and healed.
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two mandibles cannot be put back in place within an hour and are not converted to their original state, then fevers and chills appear accustomed, and by chance vomiting appears with stool.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions;	And when you see that, then know it is a delusion;
et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	and many die in this condition after seven days.
de la forcelle	of the shoulder
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	the shoulder cannot be moved along the ribs inside and below the skin, and is dislocated every time without fail, and it hurts very much.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras;	And the restoration is that the sick man gets up from his bed and extends his arms;
et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra;	and then presses the joint in the palm of his hand, and it will return;
puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint;	then puts on the plaster and the bandage, and ties it;
et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer;	and the joint that is opposite to the injured spot cannot dislocate.
se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit;	He is not so, and if he dislocates sometimes, then the reset has taken its place, as we have said;
puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then put on the plaster and bandage, and bind it, instructing the patient to rest until he is healthy.
et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	and just as before, the head of the shoulder is reset when it has lost its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	The head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres:	Know that the shoulder joint is dislocated only in three manners:
de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz;	when one is dislocated due to the part being displaced downwards from its proper place.
et li seconde est a la partie dou pis;	and the second is at the level of the heel;
et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc;	and sometimes it dislocates upwards, and this happens rarely.
et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners;	And do not dislocate me behind by the shoulder, and do not dislocate me inside with the nerves.
et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment;	and again and again dislocate in that direction towards the elbow, especially those who have little strength, because those will be hastily taken.
a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	and to those who have enough strength, the limb will swell and return to its original size.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And sometimes it happens to some people that they strike or crush the shoulder with an abscess, and think that this is a dislocation because of the swelling.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains;	Therefore it is necessary that you test it, until you are certain of it;
et adonques encomence la cure.	And then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste;	And it is known that there are dislocations when they occur below the elbow, and you will find a difference between the diseased shoulder and the healthy one, and you will see their diversity clearly.
et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes;	And you will find a cavity at the shoulder blade, and below that at the armpit the head of the shoulder blade, so it is when we have seen.
et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens;	And the patient cannot return his hand to its normal place, nor move it from any movement.
et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier;	And also, if it is dislocated above, and not hidden inside, because you will find it obviously at the armpit.
et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And this kind of dislocation is not difficult to fix when it is new, or if the patient is sick.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu;	And the manner is that the ministers will lift the hand of the sick person in the armpit, then put your hands under the shoulder, and lift the joint to force in the upper place.
et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz;	and hold the hand out high, because it is below.
si venra hastanment.	if it comes suddenly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude;	And if it does not come as we have said on the hands the day before, then it is advisable that the patient be bathed in hot water;
et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree;	and he gives him an appetite-lifting and pain-relieving draught, as a decoction of alum and fenugreek and malloloth in hot water, and it is given to him;
puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide;	then place the patient on his back, and put an equal-sized cloth on his chest, neither too soft nor too hard, then put a towel over his shoulder, lift the head of the shoulder with virtue, and treat the hand of the patient;
et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval;	and put another head on the patient, so it does not move.
celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere:	that shoulder returns now, and if you see it again in this way;
et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides;	and that you have make him be present to someone larger than the patient.
et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar;	and stand straight on the cost side, and pour water from above onto the shoulder of the patient, and lift the shoulder up, so that the patient hangs by the arm;
et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	and another servant treats the hand of the patient towards the belly.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	If the patient is too light, then he will lie with him on any heavy thing, and the dislocation returns now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere:	And also, it is done in another way:
et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile;	and it is as to strike a long knife into the earth, which is so that the head is like the pit, and not too big nor too small.
puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust;	The patient will lie down afterwards, but if he has soft bandages on, and the patients are lying in a long bed.
puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment;	Then stretch out his hand opposite the other limb, and the joint will return to its place quickly.
et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure:	and if it does not return for all these things that we have said, then do this treatment.
pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	take two fingers of the right hand and four of the left, which have the head at the center to pierce in depth beneath the nail, according to this form:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide;	Then place the head of the fist under soft bandages to prevent the wound from bleeding the patient, and then put it beneath the abscess on the patient.
et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part:	Instruct the patient to stretch out both arms above the body, and tie the arm to the body, then pull the arm towards the head of the hand, next put the arm on top of an eschar of a large size, and so stretch out the hands downwards, and leave the body hanging from another part:
li jointure reva ens maintenant.	Let the joint be fixed now.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is so in any manner, if it pleases you to do so, then put under the bandage one sparrow of wool equal, then put on the plaster mixed with powdered flour, with incense and myrrh from the bees, above all the shoulder and around; then pull out from under the bandage immediately, and turn the ligature onto the plaster, and encircle the hand at its neck, so that the hands remain thus.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost;	And it is fitting that he does not move too much, until the limbs are comfortable, for he will recover more quickly.
et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve;	and then move again after three or seven days, and the limb.
et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And if it is firm and it does not soften, then he is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is swollen due to moisture or for another reason, it is necessary that you administer cauterizations at three points, as he is placed in front of or on the cautery desk.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis;	And if you do all this, and he dislocates after seven days, and the joint will not stay in place, and cannot lift any arm upwards, then know that the nerve at the top of the shoulder is either crushed, stretched out, or softened.
et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And he knows that a joint can never be fixed in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure;	A dislocation occurring near the elbow or kneecap, or behind it, which is caused by pushing and stretching of hands, and one uses another joint.
et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And cure until he is healed.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after the healing there comes a gretez at the member, and late in movement, then use the patient many times, as long as that gretez is alleviated, and returns to its first nature.
de la dislocation dou coute	of the dislocation of the shoulder.
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient;	He knows that the joint of the elbow is dislocated at points, and it re-dislocates.
et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien;	And it has been dislocated from all parts, and itself in front and behind, and the dislocations are not renewed, because one sees well and feels well.
et desalue selonc chescune figure.	And dislocates according to each figure.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the sick hand with the healthy one, so you can see it open.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	Because the joint is swollen, and cannot bend the arm, nor touch its shoulder in any way.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener;	And it is necessary to reset it in the same way that abscesses come out, because if they were coming out, it would be a great grievousness.
et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier;	And by chance, it cannot be restored to its original state, same as when it is at the back;
si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	But it is worth more than other dislocations, and there is great pain, and by chance it can lead to death.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains;	And when restoration is possible, when they are of such extent that one can be restored, then you stretch out your hand to both hands.
et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the arms be spread out, and the hands be placed according to the cost of the injury, above and below, and fix the joint to its bones, or to the root of his palm, until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is in front, so it returns when he doubles his hand to his hand, and from the root of the palm he feels the cost which is dislocated.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension;	And if it does not return to its place, then perform strong extension;
et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension;	And so there are two assistants who stretch out the arm, and two assistants who tie up the arm, if it does not move with the stretching.
puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large;	Then turn the arm on each side, because you have wrapped a double cloth long and wide around it.
et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne;	and when the mirror joins the joint to his hand, so that he applies oil to the joint, then he tightens the joint firmly, until it returns.
et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	and when it is in the place, so he applies plaster with powdered gypsum and oil of beeswax, tightens the wound, bends the arm to the neck of the patient, and leaves it for some days, then he removes.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse;	And if the joint is firm in its place, so he releases the thread and leaves it;
et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis;	And if you see that the joint does not tighten well, then resume the plaster and tie it, and let it be so for some days, until it is firmly set;
puis le deslie.	and then dislodge.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez;	And if it feels pain after the movement of the joint, and it is silent, then bathe and rub well, and press so that it becomes relaxed;
ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain;	or you put a fat lamb's wool on the joint, then let it be for one day and one night, then remove it, and let it go into the bath;
et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain;	and when he sweats, then rub the joint temperately, then put on the wool again, and then let it go into the bath;
et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and so do this two times or three, until he is healed;
et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus;	and if you see, place a poultice of hot vinegar moistened with butter on it and strain.
si revenra a sa disposition.	if he returns to his state.
li dislocation de la main	The dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures.	The dislocation of the hand joint is easier than other joints and returns quickly.
Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	Regardless, it is necessary to return the joint to its own place immediately, in the same wound where it was dislocated, so that it may swell or an abscess form.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne.	And if it is corrected so that you put the diseased hand on a table, and extend the affected fingers, and put your finger in the same place as the joint, and press hard until it returns.
Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu;	It's necessary to inspect whether he is well at home;
adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	so put the patient's back of his hand on a table at extension and flexion.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	If a dislocation is at the back of the hand, he instructs the patient to put his back on his hand over the table, and the operator puts his hand over that appearance of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien.	if it returns now, that is well.
Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If not, then take a poultice of plaster to calm the abscess, and let him continue in that way.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte;	And if he cannot bear it, and you cannot put him back on his feet after some days, the joint will be crooked.
et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout:	and do not put the patient through anything until his hands are fully swollen and he cannot strain or exert himself.
adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere;	Then you will know that the nerves are pierced or damaged, or the arteries.
si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	if there is no other remedy than to strain by the cautery of the case, and by chance it does not bring anything.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse V jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	When the hands are at rest, put on the plaster that we have said, then strain and let it be in place for three days, then take it off and leave it as is.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it does not move well and it has no inflammation, then apply the poultice of hot water and rub until it is healed.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	of the dislocation of the wrists
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre;	never are the joints of the hand damaged at each point, never on the back of the palm or in the belly.
adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins;	then the joints are known, and put the dislocation in the grooves until it comes back into place, then hold the head of the joint with your fingers and direct it towards the part where it is dislocated.
et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor;	and let it be two days, and then put it in its original position that day;
et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut;	and tie it up as we have said, and the dislocation of that day, and make it move, and bind it with a strap.
et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and do this often, until it is tight, and just the same, if it is dislocated in the palm of the hand, and do so as you did before, until it is healed.
et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	and just the same when it is dislocated on another side.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	Due to dislocation of the shoulder skin
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the skin of the back or neck is dislocated, or if there are multiple dislocations, and there is no treatment, for fear of death, the patient rushes to their grave.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I.	And the signs are such that the excretions come forth with great violence, nor can they be held in place, and often some member is softened, or one of the two knees or both the arms.
Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars;	And many times the ulcer opens into four parts;
celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»:	the one that opens at the back is called "gibbose" or "gilbosis".
li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance:	the cure is that you apply to it if the gilbose has come from childhood;
si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	There is no cure nor healing for all things.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit;	And that which comes from a fall or from blows or from similar things, the old manners of cures speak with great words, where there is no great benefit.
mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	but I have reduced it to its essence according to my intention, and formed remedies in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit;	I say that in gout at the toes there is no cure.
et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis;	and also that which comes directly in the two bones, and cannot be cured with fire unless it is applied specifically to the back, as I said.
et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece;	and that the sick person is laid on their face in an equal position, and has a strain beneath them, lest they fall.
puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles;	Now put the finger on the bone in the head on the ground, and on the other side the knee, and tie a string around the armpits of the sick man, and on the other side the groin and ankle.
et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons;	and two ministers feel the strings, one at the head and the other at the knee, between the two fingers;
et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	and be well closed, the finger as we have said, and the nail meets its palm on the spine, until it turns.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee;	and if it does not return by this remedy, take a wooden beam three fingers long, and shave the surface of it, and let the sick man lie on that side, then put the middle of the beam on the spine.
et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu;	And place the mirror on its feet above the other chest of the table, and press well, until it returns to its place;
et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	And if you see, if you do that on the tonsil which turns to the hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc;	And that you tie two tonsils to the head of the patient on one arm, and to the feet of another, and put between each tonsil, above and below, a span's width of wood.
et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent;	and that in each tonsil there is a puncture, or the tonsil bleeds, and the tonsils are firmly planted in the earth, so that they do not move;
et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet;	and between each two tonsils there is a tonsil turning, whether the ties turn, and have in each of these turns two small tonsils a span wide, to turn the tonsil;
et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	and then tie the tendon that is between the bones near the neck to the top of the head, and the other tendon to the feet at another turn, and each of the ministers turns their turn around the entire tendon, and the master ties the equal needle as we have said.
