Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez;	And when it is equalized, he puts on a plaster dressing with many beeswax, and then the poultice, and then the edge of a tablet of three-dozen lengths, which stains the leg of goutiness and the healthy part of the spine, and then ties it with a cord as we have said, and uses the patients gently until they are healed.
et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant;	and if no remedy comes to the end of the healing, he must administer soft and soothing medicines with the edge that we have mentioned before;
et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations;	And sometimes they give him a poultice, and sometimes it comes to appearance in the lower spondyle of the back, and think that this is a dislocation;
et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption:	And it's the bone that opens up, because you shouldn't have any presumptions about it:
par aventure feroit venir la mort.	But by chance might it bring death.
des dislocations de la hainche	Dislocations of the hunchback
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures;	Which joints of the hip and shoulder come only from dislocations, not from other joints.
et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties:	And the joint of the hip is swollen in four parts;
dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier;	within and without, and before and behind;
et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	and more within these joints, and less swollen before and behind.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu;	The knowledge of dislocations is that when you put the sick limb together with the healthy one, it becomes longer and opens up more the patient's knees than those who are healthy, and cannot double its knee joint at all in heat;
et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	and it is the pus that comes out of the abscessed cartilage, because the head of the cartilage comes loose.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the signs of he who suffers from this defect are such that these accidents are contrary to those foreseen.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement;	And the signs that occur before a patient with this condition are that his knee is perfectly aligned according to the completion.
toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	unless he doubles his knee joint with pain, and if one tries to make him walk, he cannot before, and holds back his urine, and swells the groin, and when he goes, it passes above the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of he who has this behind him are such that he cannot stretch his knee, nor double it, and because that leg is more bent than the other, and the groin swells less, and the head of the chest bone is at low level beneath the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure;	The limb of this dislocation is when you return to its normal form if the dislocation is old and it stays in place according to its nature; if there is no cure.
et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	and it's not fitting that he has confidence.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des IIII manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre;	And in those whose dislocation is fresh, and it's one of the four kinds of dislocation, if you hasten so that you return to the joint, and open it inside and outside, and move it from right to left.
par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	in case he returns, and no other cure is needed.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil;	And if he doesn't return in this manner, it's fitting that you should bring a strong minister, and fasten the leg strongly with two hands, or tie it up above the knee.
et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe;	And other attendants stretch out their hands in this manner so that they pour water over his hands and below his feet, then tie a string around the crotch.
et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien;	And other tie up the head with the cord.
et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	And stretch it up and down all at once, so that the patient is lifted off the ground once, and remains suspended.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as IIII semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This method of extension is common for four reasons, and if dislocation has returned, as we have said, this is very good.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance.	If this is not the case, then it is advisable to apply treatment to his appearance.
Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele;	When the dislocation is in the shoulder joint, if you want to, place the patient on their healthy side, then tie the cord at the root of the crotch, and the one that is under the angle, then stretch the cord upwards towards the angle, and downwards towards the armpit.
puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment:	Then take another set of attendants to grasp his arms, and embrace the large limb of the sick person, and stretch it out towards the form:
si revenra a son leu maintenant;	if it returns to its place now;
et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	and this manner of dislocation is lighter than the others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres;	And if you cannot close it in this manner as we have said, then it is advisable to bind the two feet and two knees of the sick person together with a strong cloth on both the lower and upper parts, so that the diseased leg is stretched out twice more than the others;
puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc;	then be hung suspended over the head of a stick, and also above the ground two arms of long cloth;
puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	then command the attendant to embrace the head of the sick person, and let another set of attendants be hung with the patient, who will embrace and form a tight closure, because the joints are returning now quickly.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi;	And when the dislocation occurs at the joint, so that the patient suffers, just as we have said in the case of those with gout, and cut off the ligament on the diseased leg properly, and on the flesh as well;
puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme;	Then put two thorns, one on the head and one on the other joint, then drive a thorn between the bones into the patient's flesh in the shape;
et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	and cover the moist cloth over it, so that the patient does not bleed, then stretch out those two ministers towards him, and put the ligature equal to his hand on the dislocation;
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, that's good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If not, put on an ice. I.e., a table, and press it as we have said in the gout, and grieve the patient on the healthy side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit;	And when a dislocation occurs in front, it is advisable to stretch the diseased leg very much, and according to what I have said;
et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	and put the mirrors on the patient's face of pain, then press with the other hand, and extend away towards the groin.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches;	And if the dislocation is outside, it does not suit to extend the patient downwards, nor lift him up onto the ground, but rather it suits that he be in the same state as if his joints had been dislocated outside, as we have said when covering the two joints;
et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table;	and be on his face, and the ligament is extended as we have said before, and must not press upon the joint at the table;
et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz;	and when the patient stretches his legs, and they are made even.
adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve;	and then tie the knees, and apply an emplastre, and strap with a bandage, so that the joint does not move;
et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus;	And if he rests for three days or four, then let him be laid down; and apply plaster on.
et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors;	and if you see them growing even, then strain the skin, just as before, and let him rest for three days.
puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	Then lay him down again, and set him to walk gently until the limbs are comfortable.
de la dislocation dou genoil	Of a joint of the shoulder
Li genous est desaluez selonc III manieres:	The groin is dislocated in three ways:
c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier;	that is to say, inward and outward, and behind.
et ne desalue point devant.	and does not dislocate forward.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez;	And if the sign is that you command the patient to bend his knee to his groin, and he does not straighten up at his groin, then it is dislocated.
et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez;	and let the patient sit upright, and extend his leg if he can, and place your back on his face, and put his foot on your feet;
puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment;	then take his groin between your palms, and push it between your two hands, then fold the two sides of the groin together;
et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement;	and other servants stretch his foot so that the groin returns to its place, and let it be a sign that he has well restored his leg with light movement;
et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie;	and put the plaster on, and let it dry by applying heat to his leg at the groin, and binding together three days or four, then release.
et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	and do not worry about the sick man until his members are comfortable.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the limbs are not at all moved by that, stretch them greatly, just as we said in the treatment of hemlock, so long as they remain safe.
de la dislocation dou talon	of the foot dislocation
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The feet are sometimes swollen, and sometimes completely inflamed, and they swell inside and outside.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee:	And the signs are that the ankle is swollen, and it tends before it is displaced at the part where it is displaced:
li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	The remedy is lighter, and you must extend it lightly with your hands when it is only inflamed.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville;	And when it is completely dislocated, you should seat the patient on his right side, and apply gentle pressure to the joint with a linen band above the ankle.
puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut;	then take the stone to your right hand and then to your left twice, then stretch it upwards, and pour water well into the top of the stone.
et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet;	and do this twice, as we have said, pouring and taking out the stone.
s’elle revient, c’est bien;	She has recovered;
se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient;	If this is not the case, then it will begin again, because it recurs.
et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide;	And if it cannot recur in that way, then have the patient lie on his back on the ground, and place a firm pad between his thighs, and tie tight cloth around, so that the patient does not bleed.
puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet;	Then the ministers will apply to the joint, and another minister will extend the foot to his hands or to the cord that is tied around the neck.
puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent;	Then each minister extends it equally, and the cord is tied tightly between the thighs of the patient to hold them in place when being extended.
puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	Then put the mirror on its level at the dislocation in its hands, and another minister holds the healthy leg down below, and the dislocation will return quickly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois;	And when it has come to a point, if one applies the plaster and casts on top, and the strain forms, and ties the foot to the leg, and binds the nerves that are above the ankle bone so that the ligaments are not too tight;
puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain;	then he lets it be for two days or three, and if the strain occurs;
puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors;	then he frees him on the third day or in the fourth, and sends him away after four days;
et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	and if he goes before the appointed time, it is not safety for him; he will dislocate again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess comes to a head, so you must calm it, just as we have said elsewhere, until it is healed.
des dois	of the two.
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When both are dislocated, so they must be extended with work, and it is a light matter.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne;	If the dislocation is in any other position on the back or foot, then you should seat the patient upright either on a plain floor or on a bed, and place your foot under where these joints are located, then press with your foot firmly, until they come back.
et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie;	And when it is even and nothing opens, then you should place under the sole of the foot a wooden board with two joints, then fix them firmly, and leave three days, then lift.
et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let him rest, until he is cured.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	of wound and dislocation together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert:	When a wound occurs with the dislocation and one attempts to restore it, this often happens that the patient dies.
si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis;	if you are not presumptuous in the treatment, for if you are not skilled in the art and have not used it for a long time, and if you are not pitying or merciful and delaying unnecessarily, do not be too harsh.
et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit;	and instruct the patient to begin with soothing treatments for an abscess, and let him lie in the hands of God, if you do not see a chance of recovery.
et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne;	and if you see a chance of recovery, then reset the limb immediately, so that the abscess is cleansed.
et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis;	and if the limb is in place, administer soothing treatments for an abscess, and treat the wound as needed, using dried bandages.
et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples;	and if there is a fracture with broken bones and small pieces of bone that must be extracted, do as we have said for simple diseases;
et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	and beware not to fall into a state of fear, as I have said, for this is what your Creator has warned you against, and because it will lead to more suffering according to your own arm and body.
